# Pathfinder Scotland -- Session learnings

A running log of concrete, session-specific lessons not yet promoted to 
standing conventions in CLAUDE.md. Entries live here until a quarterly 
review decides whether to promote them, archive them, or leave them 
logged for reference.

Most recent session first.

## 2026-04-25 Schools-8 -- SEEMIS import (pupils / attendance / classes), SQA results with value-added, alumni destinations, primary-to-secondary transition

- **Files touched:** new migration `supabase/migrations/20260424181202_schools_import_destinations_transition.sql` creates 5 tables (`seemis_imports`, `sqa_results_imports`, `sqa_results`, `alumni_destinations`, `transition_profiles`) + 20 RLS policies + `set_alumni_destinations_updated_at()` trigger + `class_students.import_id` column + index; new libs `lib/school/import-parsing.ts` (CSV + XLSX parsers, auto-match column hints for 6 import types, value helpers for postcode/bool/year-group/CfE/grade, `nameMatches()` for SCN-less fallback, `currentAcademicYear()`) and `lib/school/import.ts` (auto-map builders + orchestrators `runPupilImport`, `runAttendanceImport`, `runClassListImport`, `runSqaImport`, `runTransitionImport`, `runDestinationsImport`, `rematchUnmatched`, `getDestinationsDashboard`, `mapDestinationType`); 12 new API routes under `app/api/school/import/*` (parse, pupils, attendance, classes, sqa + sqa/analysis, transition + transition/dashboard, destinations (list / dashboard / import / manual-entry), history, history/[id] delete, rematch (GET list + POST run)) and 1 new `app/api/student/sqa-results/route.ts`; new page `/school/import` (6-tab upload + preview + column-mapping UI + import history + unmatched panel); new overview widget `components/school-dashboard/import-widget.tsx` and results-day silent-when-empty card `components/results-day/school-imported-results.tsx`; extended guidance profile API + UI to include a Transition section on Overview; `lib/school/analytics.ts` `getSimdGap` now reads `positive_destination_pct` live from `alumni_destinations` (was hard-coded `null`); `getCesCapacities.horizons` now blends engagement 80% with alumni positive-destination rate 20% when destinations exist; `middleware.ts` extends `protectedRoutes` and the non-staff-on-school redirect with `/school/import`; school dashboard gains an admin / tracking-manager Data import quick-link row.

- **Migration drift resolved this session (ninth school session).** Local file drafted as `20260425120000_schools_import_destinations_transition.sql`; MCP applied as `20260424181202`; post-apply rename via `mv` to match. The wrapper script `scripts/apply-migration.sh` was shipped in Schools-7 closeout but MCP's `apply_migration` tool bypasses the `supabase db push` path the script wraps; the drift pattern therefore recurs when using MCP. **Rule: the rename-after-apply step is still required whenever MCP `apply_migration` is used instead of `supabase db push` / the wrapper script. The wrapper only helps when applying via CLI. Phase-2 candidate: add the `list_migrations` + rename step as a post-step in MCP apply invocations, or always prefer the CLI wrapper for DDL migrations.**

- **CSV parser is 40 lines of inline code, not a dependency.** `lib/school/import-parsing.ts::parseCsv` is a state-machine parser handling quoted fields, doubled-quote escapes, CRLF, and BOM stripping. Schools-6a / 7 used similar inline helpers for CSV export; this session pairs it with an inline CSV _reader_. `papaparse` would be 35KB minified for code that's less than 40 lines of handwritten parser — rejected. XLSX parsing uses the existing `xlsx` package (already in deps) with `sheet_to_json({ header: 1 })`. **Rule reinforcement (CSV export from Schools-7): for CSV read / write under school-scale row counts, handwrite the 30-40 lines. `papaparse` / `csv-stringify` are overkill until streaming or locale-aware separators become requirements.**

- **Column-mapping heuristic: normalise headers to lowercase alphanumeric, then exact-match first and partial-match second.** `autoMatch(headers, hints)` strips everything except `[a-z0-9]` from both sides, exact-matches first, then falls back to `includes()` for hints of length >= 3. This catches "SCN", "scn", "Scn#", "StudentSCN" equally. The minimum-length guard on partial match prevents "s" from matching everything. Per-field hint lists live as module constants (`PUPIL_HINTS`, `ATTENDANCE_HINTS`, etc.) so the UI can display them as fallback dropdowns when auto-match returns `null`. **Rule: auto-match for user-supplied headers should be deterministic (exact before partial) and tolerant of punctuation/case, but never so aggressive it misroutes obvious fields. Always surface the detected map to the user for confirmation.**

- **Stub students for SCN-only imports.** When a pupil CSV contains an SCN with no existing `students` row AND no name-match fallback, `runPupilImport` creates a stub row with synthetic email `stub+<scn>@import.pathfinderscot.co.uk`, `user_type='student'`, and `school_id` set. No `auth.users` entry is created. When that student later creates a Pathfinder account, the post-signup linking flow is expected to match on SCN and merge -- an operation not wired in this session and logged as Phase-2. The current "Re-match by SCN" button on `/school/import` handles the reverse direction (unmatched records re-linked to students who exist). **Rule: when importing records for users who may not yet have an auth account, create a placeholder row with a synthetic unique-identifier email rather than nulling the required fields. The placeholder carries the school link + demographic data so analytics work immediately; the account link happens on signup.**

- **Value-added uses the existing tracking_entries.actual_grade column, not a parallel calculation.** `runSqaImport` does two things per matched row: (a) inserts `sqa_results` with predicted vs actual + value-added; (b) updates `tracking_entries.actual_grade + is_predicted_grade=false` on the matched entry. Downstream, `lib/school/analytics.ts::getValueAdded` (shipped in Schools-5) reads from `tracking_entries.actual_grade` directly -- no change needed. The analytics _already_ had the plumbing; Schools-8 just populates the column. **Rule: before wiring a new analytics module, audit the existing analytics module for placeholder columns / null-returning fields. The correct wiring often only needs the upstream data to land, not a new function. Schools-5's `positive_destination_pct: null` was literally a TODO waiting for Schools-8 data.**

- **Best-of-both: RLS broad + API-layer filtering for staff reads, but narrow RLS + jsonb lookups for student-specific reads.** `sqa_results` SELECT is "any staff at school" (broad) -- the `/api/school/import/sqa/analysis` route does its own filtering because the analysis aggregates across many rows and doesn't need per-row visibility gating. `transition_profiles` SELECT is narrower ("guidance + leadership + admin roles") because the data is inherently sensitive and the narrower USING is cheap. `alumni_destinations` is broad because any school staff member legitimately needs to see leaver outcomes for context. Admin-only DELETE across all five tables. **Rule reinforcement (Schools-5 / 6b): RLS expression complexity should match the expected query cardinality and the content sensitivity. Aggregation-heavy reads favour broad RLS + API filtering; individually-targeted reads can afford narrower policies.**

- **Dest-type mapping via substring search, not enum coercion.** `mapDestinationType(raw)` scans for substrings like `'he'`, `'college'`, `'apprenticeship'` in the raw value (lowercased) and returns a canonical `destination_type` enum value. This tolerates "HE", "higher education", "University of Glasgow", "Going to uni" equally -- because SDS feeds from different local authorities vary wildly. Returns `null` for unrecognised values so the import surfaces them as errors rather than silently bucketing everything as `'unknown'`. **Rule: when accepting free-text enum-style input (destinations, grade bands, postcode formats), use substring coercion with explicit `null` for unknown — never a default bucket. A silent default hides data-quality problems that will resurface as analytics nonsense later.**

- **Imports stamp audit rows BEFORE the per-row pass, then update counts AFTER.** For attendance, class lists, SQA, and transition imports, the audit row (`seemis_imports` / `sqa_results_imports`) is created with counts=0 first, then each imported row references that `import_id` via FK, and the final `update` sets counts from the accumulated summary. This pattern means a partial failure still leaves an audit trail showing _some_ rows were processed. The pupil import is the exception: it creates the audit row at the end because the import operates on existing students (no FK needed from imported rows). **Rule: audit-first, counts-second for any import that produces rows with an `import_id` FK. Audit-last is fine for imports that only mutate existing rows and never insert new ones. Picking the wrong order means rows either can't FK (audit-last) or orphaned audits on full failure (audit-first with no error recovery).**

- **Silent-when-empty pattern applied to Results Day + dashboard import widget.** `<SchoolImportedResults />` on `/results-day` returns `null` if the signed-in user has no `sqa_results` rows. `<ImportStatusWidget>` on the school dashboard returns `null` if the viewer lacks tracking-management permission -- not just "empty state" but entirely hidden. The alternative (always render a placeholder) pollutes the page for the 95% of users who don't have school-imported data. **Rule reinforcement (Schools-6a / 7): episodic cards for school-driven content default to silent-when-empty; only interactive self-serve cards should show empty-state placeholders.**

- **Pre-flight studying of existing code paid off.** Before writing the destinations snapshot logic, I checked `student_subject_choices` columns and discovered the table doesn't have `qualification_type_id` or `submitted_at` (unlike what the prompt assumed). A 30-second schema lookup prevented a broken join that would only have surfaced at import time. **Rule reinforcement (eight prior sessions): the task prompt's column references are drafts. Run `information_schema.columns` against every table the code will touch before writing the code.**

- **Typecheck + lint + build all clean.** `npx tsc --noEmit`: 0 errors. `npm run lint`: 0 errors, 213 warnings (+35 vs Schools-7's 178 baseline; all 35 are `@typescript-eslint/no-explicit-any` on the new import files matching the existing school-domain convention). `npm run build`: compiled in 2.4 min; 12 new import API routes + 1 student-facing route + new `/school/import` page all resolve. 20 RLS policies verified (4 per new table × 5 tables) via `pg_policies`.

- **Phase-2 follow-ups logged this session:** (a) MCP-driven `apply_migration` still needs a post-apply rename step -- the `scripts/apply-migration.sh` wrapper only covers the CLI path; add a second helper or document the MCP-specific workflow; (b) stub student creation uses a synthetic email but there is no onboarding flow to merge the stub with a real auth.users row when that student signs up -- "Re-match" covers orphan records, not stub promotion; (c) import deletion is audit-only -- full rollback (delete the rows the import created, restore previous values) is a Phase-2 feature noted in the UI; (d) the `seemis_imports` audit row notes column is a JSONB grab-bag (updated count, stub IDs, academic year / term, unmatched subjects etc.) -- consider columns per-import-type if these become queryable; (e) `transition_profiles.source_primary` is free text -- add a `cluster_primaries` lookup table once more than 3-4 schools adopt transition imports; (f) attendance CSV upsert is idempotent on (school_id, student_id, academic_year, term) but there's no UNIQUE constraint -- add one if concurrent admin imports become a risk; (g) the value-added grade-to-numeric mapping hard-codes A=4...D=1 with a generic fallback -- Scotland has National 5 / Higher / Advanced Higher with different grade scales (Band 1-7 underneath the letter); use the existing `grade_scales` table for more robust point calcs; (h) SCN-matching on SQA results only covers rows with SCN + matching student; rows with a name but no SCN are skipped (not name-matched) -- bring in the same `nameMatches()` fallback the pupil importer uses; (i) the CES Horizons blended formula (80% engagement + 20% alumni positive-pct) is a first guess with no pilot data -- tune once more schools have leaver destinations; (j) `/results-day` is a 1400-line client page -- the new `<SchoolImportedResults />` injects at one fixed spot but the broader refactor into smaller sections is Phase-2; (k) `value_added` is stored as INTEGER (grade-position delta) on `sqa_results` -- if schools want fractional value-added (e.g. tariff-point differentials), migrate to NUMERIC; (l) the import parser assumes UTF-8 + the first worksheet of an XLSX -- if schools submit workbooks with summary sheets, add a sheet-picker.

## 2026-04-25 Migration timestamp drift -- wrapper script

- **Migration timestamp drift resolved.** `scripts/apply-migration.sh` (bash) and `scripts/apply-migration.ps1` (PowerShell) wrap `supabase db push` and auto-rename the local migration file to match the remote timestamp. Use these instead of bare `supabase db push` for all future migrations. The CLI command for the remote query is `npx supabase db query --linked --agent no --output csv "SELECT version FROM supabase_migrations.schema_migrations ORDER BY version DESC LIMIT 1;"`.

- **`supabase db query --linked --agent no`** is the correct CLI command to query the remote DB without the JSON envelope the CLI adds when it detects an agent context. The `--agent no` flag is required in Claude Code sessions; without it the output is a JSON object with an untrusted-data warning wrapper rather than plain CSV/table.

- **Promote recurring manual steps to scripts before the third session they appear in.** The timestamp drift appeared in sessions Schools-1 through Schools-7 before being automated. The post-session regret note appeared in session-learnings from Schools-6b onward. Rule: if the same manual cleanup step appears in two consecutive session-learnings entries, that is the signal to automate it -- not session 8.

## 2026-04-25 Schools-7 -- DYW (employers + placements), CPD (staff PRD + inspection CPD evidence), CES Networks wired live

- **Files touched:** new migration `supabase/migrations/20260424171731_schools_dyw_cpd.sql` creates 3 tables (`employer_contacts`, `work_placements`, `cpd_records`) + 13 RLS policies + `set_dyw_cpd_updated_at()` trigger; new libs `lib/school/dyw.ts` (19 exports incl. `getDywOverview`, `getSectorCoverage`, `getNetworksCapacity`, `getEmployerPipeline`, `toCsvRow`, academic-year helpers) and `lib/school/cpd.ts` (`listStaffCpd`, `getSchoolCpdSummary`, `getCpdByHgiosIndicator`, `CPD_TYPES`, `GTCS_LABELS`); 15 new API routes under `app/api/school/dyw/*` (overview, employers list/CRUD, employer log-contact, placements list/CRUD, students-for-picker, annual-report HTML, export CSV) and `app/api/school/cpd/*` (list/create, [id] update/delete, summary, prd HTML, export CSV, indicators); 1 new student-facing API `app/api/student/work-experience/route.ts`; new pages `/school/dyw` (5-tab: overview / employers / placements / pipeline / sectors) and `/school/cpd` (3-tab: my CPD / school CPD / by HGIOS4 QI) with modal-based forms; new components `components/school-dashboard/dyw-cpd-widgets.tsx` (overview-tab DYW + CPD widgets) and `components/dashboard/work-experience-card.tsx` (student-dashboard card, silent-when-empty); extended guidance profile `app/school/guidance/[studentId]/page.tsx` with a new `Placements` tab; `lib/school/analytics.ts` Networks capacity now reads live from `getNetworksCapacity` (previously hard-coded `score: 0`); `lib/school/inspection-autogen.ts` added QI 1.4 (Leadership and management of staff — from `cpd_records`) and extended QI 2.3 with a "CPD linked to Learning, Teaching and Assessment" statement; `AUTO_GEN_SUPPORTED` now contains 9 of 15 QIs (was 8); school dashboard gains DYW + CPD quick-link rows (DYW visible to dyw_coordinator / leadership / admin; CPD visible to everyone); `middleware.ts` extends `protectedRoutes` + the non-staff-on-school redirect with `/school/dyw` and `/school/cpd`.

- **Migration drift, eighth consecutive session.** Local file drafted as `20260425110000_schools_dyw_cpd.sql`, MCP applied as `20260424171731`. Renamed post-apply. This is now structural across eight straight school sessions (Schools-1 through Schools-7). **Rule reinforcement (eighth time): the post-apply rename step must be automated before Schools-8 or this identical line will appear there too. A wrapper script around `apply_migration` that (a) calls `list_migrations` immediately, (b) compares the returned version to the local draft filename, and (c) does the `mv` automatically would have saved ~10 minutes across these eight sessions and will save more going forward.**

- **Single shared updated_at trigger function across three tables, rather than one function per table.** The migration defines `set_dyw_cpd_updated_at()` once and attaches it to all three new tables via three `CREATE TRIGGER` statements. The guidance migration did this with `set_guidance_updated_at()` over six tables. Same pattern; zero downside. A single trigger function can be shared across any number of tables whose only touch is `NEW.updated_at := now()`. **Rule: for boilerplate triggers that do not inspect table-specific columns, define one function at the bottom of the migration and attach it to every affected table. Resist the pull toward per-table helper functions — they multiply without benefit.**

- **RLS for CPD reads: "own OR leadership" via one combined policy, not two separate policies.** The `cpd_records` SELECT policy uses a single `USING (EXISTS (SELECT 1 FROM school_staff s WHERE s.user_id = auth.uid() AND s.school_id = cpd_records.school_id AND (s.id = cpd_records.staff_id OR s.is_school_admin OR s.role IN ('depute','head_teacher'))))`. Alternative: two policies ("CPD own" + "CPD leadership") OR-combined by Postgres. Chose the combined form because (a) it's one exists() per query not two, and (b) the OR semantics are explicit in SQL rather than implicit in policy-stacking. The INSERT / UPDATE policies are narrower (own-only) because leadership should not be writing CPD records on other staff's behalf — if a depute wants to log CPD for a colleague, they should discuss it and the colleague should log it themselves. Delete is "own OR leadership" again because cleanup of withdrawn / duplicated records is a leadership task. **Rule: when an RLS policy has "OR leadership" semantics, prefer one combined policy expression over two stacked policies. Combined expressions are easier to reason about in `pg_policies`; stacked policies that OR together look the same but add a second USING expression per query.**

- **CES Networks capacity formula: 4 linear components × 25 points each, full-score thresholds picked for realistic mid-engagement schools.** The scoring thresholds are: 5 active partners → full 25 pts for the active-partners component; 20 completed placements → full 25 pts for the placement component; 50% student reach → full 25 pts for student-reach; 10 of 19 sectors covered → full 25 pts for sector-coverage. Values exceeding the threshold clamp at 25. Chose these thresholds after pilot Edinburgh schools reported 3-5 active partners and 10-15 placements in a typical academic year — a school hitting 100 would be genuinely exceptional. A flat 0-25 per component keeps the maths explainable ("how do I improve my score?") and makes the inspection-evidence statement generate naturally from the four component names. **Rule: for composite capacity scores that need to make sense to non-technical stakeholders (head teachers, inspectors), keep the formula linear and explicit. Favour "X of 25 for Y" over weighted sums with opaque coefficients — the latter is statistically cleaner but unreadable in an evidence statement.**

- **Placement model: single table with `is_group_event BOOLEAN` + CHECK constraint, not two tables.** The `work_placements` table carries both individual placements (S4 work experience at a specific employer) and group events (S2 careers talk for a year group). Table-level CHECK: `(is_group_event = true AND student_id IS NULL) OR (is_group_event = false AND student_id IS NOT NULL)`. Group events get `group_year_groups TEXT[]` and `group_student_count INTEGER` instead of a `student_id`. Alternative shape: `work_placements` for individuals, `careers_events` for groups — two tables, two sets of API routes, two migration headaches. Chose one table because the status workflow (planned → confirmed → in_progress → completed → cancelled) is identical, the employer link is identical, and the CES Networks scoring aggregates both kinds. **Rule: when two entities share ≥80% of their columns AND their lifecycle, model them as one table with a discriminator boolean + CHECK constraint. Two-table splits pay off only when the lifecycle diverges.**

- **"Mask student on read" lives in the API layer, not in RLS.** The `work_placements` SELECT policy is broad (all staff at school see all rows). The `/api/school/dyw/placements` route then filters `student_id` → null for staff without `can_view_individual_students`, returning a `_masked: true` marker so the UI renders `[restricted]` instead of the student name. This mirrors the Schools-5 decision on the analytics Equity tab: masking at the API layer keeps the RLS expression cheap and the permission rule visible in TypeScript rather than buried in a nested EXISTS. The cost: any direct DB client hitting the row sees the full student_id, but direct DB access is gated upstream (anon key + RLS on tables they would join to). **Rule reinforcement (Schools-5): permission-driven field masking belongs at the API layer, not in RLS. RLS is row visibility; column masking is application logic.**

- **CSV export uses a tiny `toCsvRow()` helper + NextResponse with explicit Content-Disposition.** `lib/school/dyw.ts` exports an 8-line CSV helper that handles comma / quote / newline escaping. The three export endpoints (DYW employers, DYW placements, CPD) build headers + rows as strings and return with `Content-Type: text/csv` + `Content-Disposition: attachment; filename=...`. No `csv-stringify` dep, no streaming. For the per-school scale (tens to low hundreds of rows), string concat is fine. **Rule: for CSV exports under ~10,000 rows, write the 8-line quote/escape helper inline and skip the dependency. Install `csv-stringify` / `papaparse` only when you genuinely need streaming or locale-specific separators.**

- **Getting-started checklist section does not exist in the current dashboard.** Task spec 8c asked to add DYW + CPD entries to the getting-started checklist. After grep, no `GettingStarted` component was found — the school dashboard has a StudentsTab with a small "Getting started" hint but no structured per-feature checklist. Logged as Phase-2 rather than invented. **Rule: when a task spec says "add to existing X" and X does not exist in the codebase, do NOT invent X — note as Phase-2 and move on. Fabricating a feature the spec assumed already existed leads to divergent UI conventions between sessions.**

- **Sector coverage colour coding: green ≥1 active, amber ≥1 contact-not-active, grey zero.** The /school/dyw Sectors tab renders 19 cards in a grid, coloured by partnership depth. The colour thresholds are a visual signal for "where should I focus my next employer outreach?" — grey cards get the "Add employer in this sector" quick link implicit from the DYW+ button at the top of the page. The alternative (heatmap with a continuous gradient) was rejected because three buckets map cleanly to three actions: nothing / prospect / nurture. **Rule: for discrete-action heatmaps (19 sectors × "what do I do next?"), 3-4 bucket colours beat a continuous gradient. Gradients are better for ranked comparison; buckets are better for decision-making.**

- **QI 1.4 auto-gen from CPD data closes a 15→8 gap in inspection auto-generators to 15→9.** The new `q14()` function in `inspection-autogen.ts` reads cpd_records aggregated by staff, hours, GTCS standards, and staff-without-CPD. QI 1.4 ("Leadership and management of staff") was the most inspection-visible gap in the earlier 8-of-15 coverage. QI 2.3 also got a second evidence bullet ("CPD linked to this indicator") so schools that tag CPD to QI 2.3 see direct inspection evidence. Remaining unsupported QIs: 1.1 (self-evaluation — no platform data), 1.2 (leadership of learning — no data), 1.3 (leadership of change — no data), 2.5 (family learning — needs parent-engagement tracking), 2.6 (transitions — needs destinations data), 2.7 (partnerships — could be wired to employer_contacts but scoped out this session). **Rule: when ticking off auto-gen QIs, prioritise the ones with existing-table data over the ones that would require a new table. Schools-7 added `cpd_records` which unlocked 1.4 + half of 2.3; Schools-8+ should look at transition / destination / family-engagement data before expanding the auto-gen set further.**

- **DYW / CPD quick-link rows placed INSIDE separate role-gated divs on the school dashboard, not bundled.** The school dashboard landing page now has up to four quick-link rows: (a) guidance (can_view_individual_students), (b) DYW (dyw_coordinator/leadership), (c) CPD (everyone), (d) analytics/inspection (leadership). Each row is its own role-conditional div. Alternative: one flat row with all nine links and per-link conditionals. Rejected because (i) per-row grouping tells the user which tools belong to which domain, and (ii) the "CPD for everyone" row reads awkwardly if it's in the middle of a gated row. The layout reads top-to-bottom as a clear role progression: base → individual-student work → DYW → everyone-CPD → leadership. **Rule: quick-link rows on a role-aware dashboard should group by _domain_, not by role. Users remember tools by what they do, not by what permission unlocks them.**

- **WorkExperienceCard is silent-when-empty by design, matching parent-evening card pattern.** `components/dashboard/work-experience-card.tsx` returns `null` when the student has no placements AND no upcoming group events. The alternative (rendering "No placements yet" placeholder for every student whose school hasn't set up DYW yet) trains students to ignore the card. Placements are quarterly events at most; the card should appear only when something real is there to see. **Rule reinforcement (Schools-6a parent-evening card): dashboard cards for episodic school-run content default to silent-when-empty. Placeholders are for features the student can action themselves (e.g. "save your first course"); episodic school content should be invisible until the school does the work.**

- **Typecheck + lint + build clean.** `npx tsc --noEmit`: 0 errors. `npm run lint`: 0 errors, 178 warnings (+33 vs the 145 baseline from Schools-6b; all 33 are `@typescript-eslint/no-explicit-any` on the 15 new routes + 2 new libs, following the existing school-domain pattern — mirror the file-level disable or inline disable where the service-role client is `as any` per codebase convention). `npm run build`: compiled in 73s; 15 new API routes (`/api/school/dyw/*` and `/api/school/cpd/*`) plus 2 new pages (`/school/dyw`, `/school/cpd`) plus `/api/student/work-experience` all resolved. 13 RLS policies verified via `pg_policies` (4 employer_contacts + 5 work_placements + 4 cpd_records).

- **Phase-2 follow-ups logged this session:** (a) no getting-started checklist component exists on the school dashboard -- build one in Schools-8+ with items for tracking setup / student invites / first report / first DYW employer / first CPD log; (b) placement date-range uses two independent dates with no end>=start DB constraint -- a user can save end_date < start_date today; add CHECK or validation; (c) `risk_assessment_url` accepts any string, no file upload; wire to Supabase Storage for actual risk assessment PDFs; (d) DYW annual report does not include the school logo / brand header (matches existing /school/reports/board-report gap); (e) CPD `reflection` under-50-chars check is a soft confirm() dialog, not a hard block -- some schools will want to enforce min length for GTCS Professional Update evidence; make it configurable per school via `schools.settings.cpd_min_reflection_chars`; (f) `cpd_records` has no `cpd_year_target_hours` column; schools that want to track progress against a local CPD-hours target (e.g. 35 hours GTCS minimum) can't yet -- add a per-staff target column or a `school_staff.cpd_year_target` field; (g) CES Networks thresholds are hard-coded in `lib/school/dyw.ts` -- move to a `schools.settings.ces_networks_thresholds` JSONB so schools with atypical cohort sizes can tune; (h) `getNetworksCapacity` is called sequentially by the analytics CES endpoint AND the DYW overview endpoint -- the two could share a cached result within a request; fine for now, revisit at scale; (i) `work_placements.linked_sector_id` is a free-choice column on the placement rather than being derived from the employer's sector -- accept the duplication (a single placement might bridge two sectors) but the overview counts `linked_sector_id` OR `employer.sector_id`, which can double-count if both are set and differ; single-count dedup logic lives in `getSectorCoverage` but not in `getDywOverview.sectors_covered`; verify if this becomes a support question; (j) student-facing `WorkExperienceCard` polls once on mount with no refresh -- a student who books a placement today won't see it until they reload; acceptable for first pass, add SWR if real-time matters; (k) CSV exports are unpaged -- a school with 10+ years of CPD + 500 placements could produce a 50MB CSV; add a date-range parameter when someone hits the wall; (l) no realtime notification when a placement flips to 'completed' — the guidance teacher should be nudged to collect feedback; wire `placement_completed` notification type in Schools-8.

## 2026-04-25 Schools-6b -- notification system (in-app bell + bulk messaging), branded email templates, auto-reminders, parent contact logging

- **Files touched:** new migration `supabase/migrations/20260424163221_school_notifications.sql` creates `school_notifications` (15 columns + 2 indexes) + 6 RLS policies (staff see-all-for-school, student and parent target-id-matches, staff INSERT, any-authenticated UPDATE for read_by, admin-only DELETE); new helpers `lib/school/email-templates.ts` (8 branded templates: reportReady / parentEveningOpen / parentEveningConfirmation / parentEveningReminder / choiceDeadline / choiceSubmitted / choiceApprovalNeeded / genericSchoolMessage, plus `wrapSchoolEmail`, `escapeHtml`, `ctaButton`, `bookingTableHtml/Text`) and `lib/school/notifications.ts` (`sendSchoolNotification`, `markAsRead`, `getUnreadCount`, `fetchRelevantNotifications`, `hasRecentDuplicate`, branded 10-rps Resend batcher, 500-recipient cap enforced in the route); 8 new API routes under `app/api/school/notifications/*` (list + bulk-send POST, mark-read, mark-all-read, unread-count, generate-reminders) and `app/api/notifications/*` (shared list, mark-read with `all` flag, unread-count); new `components/notifications/NotificationBell.tsx` (60-second poll, dropdown, badge, mark-read, audience-aware endpoints); new pages `/school/notifications` (6 filter tabs + bulk messaging form with leadership-only gate) and `/notifications` (shared student/parent view with all/unread tabs); navbar now renders the bell for staff / parents / school-linked students; intervention form gains a `parent_contact`-conditional fieldset (contact method radio + optional parent name, prepended to `notes` as a `[Phone with Ms Smith]` header); auto-notifications hooked into: reports/generate (report_ready to linked parents), parents-evening PUT (parent_evening_reminder when draft→open), guidance/safeguarding POST (safeguarding_escalation to escalated_to staff); generate-reminders route sweeps tracking deadlines / intervention follow-ups / ASN reviews / tomorrow's parent evenings / choice-round closings with 24h duplicate-guard; school dashboard gains a Notifications quick-link visible to every staff role (not only individual-student viewers); middleware adds `/school/notifications` and `/notifications` to protectedRoutes + the non-staff-on-school redirect block.

- **Migration drift, seventh consecutive session.** Local file drafted as `20260425100000_school_notifications.sql`, MCP applied as `20260424163221`. Renamed post-apply. This is now a named incident across seven school sessions. Codifying it into a wrapper script is overdue — every session confirms the `apply_migration` → `list_migrations` → rename cadence is required, not optional. **Rule reinforcement (seventh time): the drift is structural. If a post-apply rename step isn't automated before the next session, this line will appear in session 8 too.**

- **types/database.ts is stale on `students.school_id` and 7 other columns added post-baseline (scn, registration_class, house_group, eal, has_asn, attendance_pct, last_active_at).** First typecheck blew up on `student.school_id` in navbar.tsx — the generated types file still reflects the pre-6a schema. Per memory: regenerating wholesale drops hand-added rows, so edit manually. Added the 8 missing columns to students.Row only; Insert / Update blocks intentionally NOT updated in this session to keep the diff minimal. Phase-2 item: a one-off pass to align all three blocks (Row + Insert + Update) with the live schema, then pin a `npm run gen:types` script that merges generator output into the manual file rather than overwriting. **Rule: when typecheck fails on a column that is known to exist in the DB, the fix is a manual edit of types/database.ts, not `supabase gen types > ...`. Document the added column in a comment if it's non-obvious.**

- **Bell audience mapping: three audiences, three endpoints, one component.** The `NotificationBell` takes `audience: 'staff' | 'student' | 'parent'` and routes to `/api/school/notifications` (staff) or `/api/notifications` (student/parent) for the list; mark-read routes are similarly split because the authorisation model diverges — staff are trusted for any read-by write on a row at their school, students/parents must prove their id appears in target_*_ids. A single bell endpoint with server-side audience detection was considered and rejected: the `requireSchoolStaffApi` guard already returns the staffId cheaply, and the shared endpoint would have to re-derive audience for every request. **Rule: when a UI component works across three identity models (school staff, signed-in student, signed-in parent), pass audience as a prop and let the component route to the correct endpoint. Don't try to make one endpoint serve all three — the auth shape is different enough that the branching ends up in the endpoint instead.**

- **RLS for staff is `USING (EXISTS staff at school)` with no target-id check; the filter happens server-side in the route.** The staff-side SELECT policy is intentionally broad (all school notifications visible) because the alternative — OR-ing three `jsonb_array_elements_text` subqueries per row per query — would be slow at scale and brittle (target_role + target_staff_ids + catch-all broadcast need to interact). The route's `fetchRelevantNotifications` then filters by audience in JS. Documented inline. **Rule: when RLS expression complexity starts approaching O(rows × jsonb scans), defer the filter to the application layer and keep RLS as the outer gate. In-app filtering is cheap in Node; jsonb subqueries in a USING clause run per row.**

- **RLS for students/parents does use `jsonb_array_elements_text` target-id checks because their selectors are narrow.** A student sees only rows where their id is in `target_student_ids`; same shape for parents. The `jsonb_array_elements_text` + IN clause is fine here because the browser-initiated queries (if any happen) return small result sets and the JSONB lists are short (<100 ids in practice). The staff path above is different because staff see every school-level broadcast whether or not they are individually listed. **Rule: pick RLS complexity to match the query's expected cardinality. Staff-wide reads should filter cheap; student-scoped reads can afford a jsonb lookup because the N is tiny.**

- **Best-effort auto-notifications: every hook is `try { ... } catch {}`.** The report generate, parents-evening PUT, and safeguarding POST routes all fire notifications AFTER their primary insert succeeds, wrapped in try/catch. The rationale: the notification is a signal, not the transaction of record. A report should not fail to save because Resend is down; a safeguarding concern must not fail to escalate because the notification row insert hit a transient DB blip. Downstream consequence: partial-notification states are possible (report exists, notification never created). Mitigation: the generate-reminders sweep is re-run by admins / cron and the `hasRecentDuplicate` guard prevents re-sends. **Rule: notifications attached to an existing business event should be best-effort and idempotently retryable via a separate sweep. Do NOT wrap both the event + the notification in the same transaction unless the notification IS the business event (e.g. a direct user-sent message).**

- **24-hour duplicate guard: type + exact title match, queried before every sweep send.** The `hasRecentDuplicate(schoolId, type, title)` check fetches rows in the last 24h with the same (school, type, title) triple. Critically, the title contains the specifics (e.g. "Tracking entries due in 2 days") so a second sweep the next day, when the window is "1 day", generates a new title and sends again. This is intentional — parents should get one reminder per day of the deadline, not one reminder forever. The downside is that if a reminder is genuinely missed (e.g. rate-limit burnout), the sweep will skip it for 24 hours. Acceptable for weekly-cadence sweeps. **Rule: duplicate guards for deadline reminders should key on (type + title), not just (type). Titles that include the countdown number naturally deduplicate same-day but diverge across days.**

- **Bulk messaging 500-cap lives in the API layer, not the UI.** The `/api/school/notifications` POST returns 400 when `channel !== 'in_app'` and recipient count > 500; the UI shows a "needs confirm" yellow banner at > 200 but the hard block is server-side. Moving the hard cap into the route meant the leadership bypass-via-devtools path couldn't accidentally flood 1000 emails. The UI's soft cap is optional; the API's hard cap is not. **Rule: rate / volume limits that matter for cost or abuse prevention MUST live in the API layer. UI confirmation dialogs are UX, not controls — a sophisticated caller can always bypass them.**

- **Email templates: one `wrapSchoolEmail` wrapper + 8 template-specific body builders, each returning `{ subject, html, text }`.** The wrapper takes `BrandContext` (schoolName, headerColour, logoUrl) and a pre-escaped body HTML string. Every template builds its body by composing `ctaButton`, `bookingTableHtml`, and paragraphs, all running through `escapeHtml` on user-supplied data. The text fallback is always populated — a plaintext-only mail reader still sees the content. The template set covers the specific events (reportReady, parentEveningOpen/Confirmation/Reminder, choiceDeadline/Submitted/ApprovalNeeded) plus `genericSchoolMessage` as the catch-all for bulk-send. The generic template escapes the body and preserves `\n\n` as paragraph breaks + `\n` as `<br />`. **Rule: structured email templates should return `{ subject, html, text }` so callers can pass all three to Resend without post-processing. Returning just an html string forces every caller to re-derive the subject and forget the text fallback.**

- **NotificationBell polls at 60s by default, no Supabase realtime subscription.** Realtime would be cleaner but requires the anon client on the client side to subscribe to `school_notifications` with RLS in place, and the RLS on this table is designed for the API-side filtering path. A realtime subscription would bypass the API filtering and surface too-broad or too-narrow results. 60 seconds is fine for a non-urgent bell; urgent events (safeguarding escalation) use email + in-app together so the recipient gets the email within seconds. **Rule: bell polling at 60s is adequate for school-scale notification volumes. Move to Supabase realtime only if RLS can express the filtering cheaply (i.e. pure column equality, not jsonb membership).**

- **Generic-message wrapping preserves paragraph breaks from the plain-text body, but does NOT render Markdown.** The bulk-message form accepts a plaintext body; the `genericSchoolMessageEmail` template splits on `\n{2,}` to make paragraphs and replaces remaining `\n` with `<br />`. Asterisks / headings / lists are escaped literally. This keeps the template safe (no XSS) and avoids the complexity of a Markdown renderer for a first-pass feature. Phase-2: consider whether schools want Markdown / rich-text; if yes, a sanitised HTML path via `DOMPurify` or `sanitize-html` is the pragmatic answer. **Rule: for user-supplied email bodies, escape + preserve whitespace; do not parse formatting until a real UX need surfaces. Plain-text emails that render correctly beat Markdown emails with XSS risk.**

- **Parent-contact intervention logging: contact method + name get prepended to the notes field as a header, not a new column.** The `parent_contact` intervention type now shows a contact-method radio (Phone / Email / In person / Letter) and an optional parent name field. On submit, a `[Method with Name]` header is prepended to the free-text notes. No schema change. The intervention timeline renders the notes verbatim, so the header is naturally visible. A new column would be structurally cleaner but adds migration cost; deferred to Phase-2 if filtering / reporting on contact method becomes important. **Rule: when a form field is a narrow convention for one specific type (parent_contact among 12 intervention types), prepend it to an existing free-text field rather than adding a new column. Reserve schema expansion for cases where querying on the new value matters.**

- **Typecheck + lint + build all clean.** `npx tsc --noEmit`: 0 errors (one types/database.ts fix to add the 8 missing students columns). `npm run lint`: 0 errors, 145 warnings (+1 vs the 144 baseline from Schools-6a; one unused-directive cleaned up mid-cycle on `lib/school/notifications.ts` so baseline stays parity + 1). `npm run build`: compiled in 54s; 10 new routes all present (`/api/notifications`, `/api/notifications/mark-read`, `/api/notifications/unread-count`, 5 under `/api/school/notifications/*`, `/notifications`, `/school/notifications`). 6 RLS policies verified via `pg_policies`.

- **Phase-2 follow-ups logged this session:** (a) `types/database.ts` students Insert + Update blocks are still stale — this session fixed only Row; a one-off sync pass is overdue; (b) generate-reminders is admin-manual-trigger only — add a cron / pg_cron schedule so the sweep runs nightly without admin intervention; (c) bulk-send recipient previewing is not real — the UI's "sending to X" count comes from a rough estimate, not a server pre-flight; add a `/api/school/notifications/preview-recipients` endpoint for deterministic counts before send; (d) no unsubscribe footer on email notifications — parents with unique-to-pathfinder notification spam can't opt out; add a `school_notification_preferences` table or extend `students.email_preferences` / `parents` equivalent for granular opt-outs; (e) the generic-message template does not render Markdown — upgrade to sanitised rich-text if schools ask; (f) scheduled sends (send_at > now) are written as rows but never auto-dispatched — Phase-2 cron; (g) parent-contact intervention header is a string prefix, not a structured column — if filtering on contact method becomes important, add `interventions.contact_method text` + backfill; (h) bell UI polls 60s — move to Supabase realtime once RLS simplifies or once the feature hits volume; (i) students with `school_id` get the bell but the mobile slide-in menu (lg:hidden) does NOT include a notifications link — if mobile usage climbs, surface the bell count in the slide-in footer; (j) migration-rename automation is still manual after 7 consecutive sessions — codify into a post-apply script this sprint.

## 2026-04-25 Schools-6a -- parent reporting (templates + bulk email) and parents' evening booking (magic-link + prep snapshots)

- **Files touched:** new migration `supabase/migrations/20260424154527_schools_parent_reporting.sql` creates 4 tables (`parent_evenings`, `parent_evening_availability`, `parent_evening_bookings`, `parent_evening_tokens`) + 33 RLS policies incl. a new SELECT policy on existing `parent_reports` for linked parents (`parent_student_links.status = 'active'` as the gate); `lib/school/seed-tracking-defaults.ts` extended from 1 default template to 3 (Standard / Compact / Detailed) with a backfill-aware insert (idempotent per template-name, preserves existing default); new helpers `lib/school/parent-evening-slots.ts` (slot-time math: `parseTime`, `formatTime`, `generateSlots`, `normaliseTime`) and `lib/school/parent-evening-prep.ts` (prep snapshot builder + `generateToken()` uuid helper); new admin API routes under `app/api/school/reports/templates/*` (list/create, get/update/delete, preview with sample data) and `app/api/school/reports/send-all` (bulk send with 10/s rate-limit and parent-email-first resolution); parent-reports `generate` route now accepts `template_id`; `send/[id]` extended with linked-parent email lookup; new admin UI at `/school/reports/templates` (list + editor with live preview + variable-insert chips) and rewritten `/school/reports` (template selector, preview modal, bulk send); new admin API routes under `app/api/school/parents-evening/*` (list/create, get/update/delete, availability POST/DELETE, bookings POST + cancel, schedule print with prep snapshots, token issue with CSV-shaped response); new admin UI `/school/parents-evening` (list + create form) and `/school/parents-evening/[id]` (4-tab detail: Setup / Bookings / Schedule / Summary); new parent-facing API routes under `app/api/parent/parents-evening/*` (list, open, booking, cancel) and token-based `app/api/parents-evening/token/[id]` (no auth, uniqueness-gated); new pages `/parent/parents-evening/[id]` (authed) and `/parent/parents-evening/[id]/book?token=...` (magic-link); shared `components/parent-evening/booking-ui.tsx` with exported type surface used by both; new `components/parent-dashboard/parent-evening-card.tsx` silent-when-none card on the parent dashboard; `middleware.ts` extends `protectedRoutes` + staff-redirect-block with `/school/parents-evening` and `/parent/parents-evening` (kept out of protectedRoutes so the token /book subpath works unauthenticated).

- **Schools-2 already shipped `report_templates` and `parent_reports`, so Schools-6a's DDL for them is a no-op and the session focuses on the *delta*: 3-template seed, new RLS row for linked parents, and the new templates management UI.** The task prompt's DDL blocks have `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` guards which would have silently skipped anyway, but verifying the existing columns against the spec first saved rework: `pdf_url` already exists (not `pdf_path` as the prompt drafts), so the send-all endpoint uses `pdf_url` consistently. **Rule reinforcement (from 5 prior sessions): treat the task prompt's DDL as a draft. Before writing the migration file, run `information_schema.columns` against the named tables to distinguish "table doesn't exist" from "table exists with a slightly different column name". The latter is a silent contract bug if you don't notice.**

- **Parent email resolution lives in three places and must agree: list-route (for UI display), send-one (single click), send-all (bulk).** The GET /api/school/reports joins `parent_student_links.status='active'` -> `parents.email` and falls back to `students.email`. The single-send route does the same resolution. The bulk send pre-loads `parent_email_by_student` once (outside the per-report loop) to avoid N+1 queries when sending to 200 parents. All three code paths must use the same priority order; the list route additionally emits `best_email_source` ('parent' | 'student') so the UI can tag the recipient visually. Getting this inconsistent would mean "Pending" pills in the table that don't match what bulk-send actually does. **Rule: when "best recipient" is computed in more than one endpoint, extract the priority rule into a comment or shared helper -- even if the actual implementation differs because the list version is batched.**

- **Bulk-send rate limiting: 10 requests per 1000ms window, batched with Promise.all inside each window.** Resend's free tier allows 10/sec by default, so the bulk-send endpoint slices the pending rows into batches of 10, fires them in parallel via `Promise.all`, records `Date.now()` at the start of the window, and sleeps the remaining ms at the end. No per-call `setTimeout`s on individual emails -- just one macro-timer per batch. For 200 emails this settles in ~20 seconds. The alternative (`Bottleneck` or `p-queue`) is a dependency we don't need for this scale. **Rule: for bulk-send rate limits under 100/sec, write a 10-line batched `Promise.all` inside a for-loop rather than installing a queue library. The complexity only pays off at higher throughput.**

- **Magic-link booking design: token is a url-safe random string, expiring 30 days from issue, and does NOT get consumed on first use.** The `parent_evening_tokens.used_at` column is stamped on every redemption so analytics can track "parent came back", but the token stays valid until `expires_at`. This is deliberate -- parents want to log back in to add / cancel bookings. A single-use token would force parents back to the school office to request a replacement. Tokens are scoped to (evening, student) so a parent with two children gets two separate URLs. **Rule: for parent-facing magic links that serve an ongoing booking window, use an expiry-based model (TTL) not a use-count-based one. The revocation tool is "delete the row", which is easy for admins to do and invisible to benevolent users.**

- **The token-booking flow has NO user_id -- bookings stored via the token route have `parent_id = null` and `booked_by = 'school'`.** This is structurally correct because the parent isn't authenticated as a user of Pathfinder. The RLS policy "Parents view own bookings" therefore does NOT match these rows (the user has no Pathfinder parent_id). Token-holders only see their bookings by re-visiting the same token URL; the GET endpoint returns the student's bookings at that evening via the token gate, not via `auth.uid()`. **Rule: when a booking can be created by both an authenticated parent AND a token holder, the "view my bookings" path must branch on the auth model too. Don't assume `auth.uid()` is always the identity -- sometimes the identity is the token itself.**

- **Live preview for report-template editor: debounced 400ms, fetches `/api/school/reports/templates/preview` which renders against stock sample data.** The preview endpoint doesn't touch a real student -- it injects a sample subject list with varied grade / on-track / effort values so the editor can see colour coding. Reloading on every keystroke is 20+ fetches/sec at typing speed; debounced to 400ms it's one fetch per thought-pause. The `editorKey` memo (template length + header colour + logo) is a cheap proxy for "editor state changed" that avoids re-fetching when nothing relevant moved. **Rule: debounced live previews should key on a stable derived string (length + key fields), not on the whole component state. Stringifying the entire state JSON on every render is wasteful and occasionally triggers fetches when an unrelated field changes.**

- **Delete-last-template guard must check count and default status, not just count.** The templates delete route blocks deletion when `count <= 1` OR when the row-being-deleted `is_default = true`. The second guard catches the case where a school has 5 templates but the default is the one being deleted -- the UI should offer "set another as default first". Without the default guard, the school ends up with no default, and `POST /api/school/reports/generate` fails silently because the default-template lookup returns null. **Rule: any "last of its kind" delete guard must include both the "is this the last row?" check AND the "is this row load-bearing?" check. The latter is usually a flag like `is_default` / `is_primary` / `is_active`.**

- **Schedule print uses the same `@page { size: A4; margin: 12mm }` + `window.print()` pattern as Schools-4 meeting brief, Schools-2 reports, Schools-5 board report.** Four separate school reports across four sessions now follow this pattern. For the parents' evening schedule, the report iterates per teacher and emits one `<section>` per teacher with their bookings table. Each booked row shows the prep snapshot (subjects line, attendance, saved courses, flags) inline. Page breaks are managed with `.teacher-block { page-break-inside: avoid }` so a single teacher's schedule isn't split mid-table. **Rule (fourth confirmation): for "print or save as PDF" school reports, HTML + @page CSS + `window.print()` is the right answer. Stop considering puppeteer / @react-pdf / pandoc for this use case.**

- **Prep snapshot is captured at booking time, not at render time.** The prep JSONB is written to `parent_evening_bookings.prep_snapshot` on INSERT. When a teacher prints their schedule a week later, the snapshot reflects the student's state at the moment the booking was made -- not the possibly-different state a week on. This is deliberate: teachers prepare from what the parent saw when booking, and a moving target undermines that. The downside is that a student whose grades shift significantly between booking and the evening will have slightly stale prep data; a "refresh prep" button could be added later. **Rule: for scheduled future events where prep data informs the conversation, snapshot at scheduling-time rather than computing live at render. The UI consistency at print time matters more than perfect freshness for 5-minute meetings.**

- **Parent dashboard card is silent when no event is open, not a "no events" placeholder.** `/api/parent/parents-evening/open` returns `{ evening: null }` when nothing's in the window, and the card component returns `null` rather than rendering an empty state. For most of the school year there is no open parents' evening, and a placeholder card on every parent's dashboard would be noise. The card only appears when actionable. **Rule: for dashboard surfaces that surface time-bounded events, default to silent-when-absent rather than a "no upcoming" placeholder. Placeholders for sections that are empty ≥ 80% of the time train users to ignore them.**

- **`parent_evening_tokens` has permissive SELECT (anon OR authenticated) and permissive UPDATE.** This is intentional: the token-validation model is "uniqueness of the token is the auth", and the GET needs to return event/student/teacher info to an unauthenticated browser hitting /book?token=X. INSERT is admin-only (only school admins issue tokens); UPDATE is permissive so the used_at timestamp can be stamped on redemption without login. DELETE has no policy -- nobody can delete tokens through RLS; admins bypass via the service-role client. **Rule: when a table's auth model is "possession of a value", the RLS for SELECT becomes `USING (true)` and the application enforces the check in-route. Document this in a comment on the policy so a future audit doesn't flag it as a misconfiguration.**

- **Typecheck + lint + build all clean.** `npx tsc --noEmit`: 0 errors (one round-trip to fix a ParentEveningBookingUI-exported-type ambiguity between the two Data shapes in authed vs token pages). `npm run lint`: 0 errors, 144 warnings (+9 vs the 135 baseline from Schools-5; one `prefer-const` was fixed during the build cycle). `npm run build`: compiled in 70s; new routes `/school/parents-evening`, `/school/parents-evening/[id]`, `/school/reports/templates`, `/parent/parents-evening/[id]`, `/parent/parents-evening/[id]/book` and 11 new API routes all render. 33 RLS policies verified via `pg_policies` (7 parent_evenings + 10 parent_evening_availability + 10 parent_evening_bookings + 3 parent_evening_tokens + 1 added to parent_reports + 2 pre-existing untouched).

- **Migration history drift, 6th consecutive session. Local file drafted as `20260425100000_schools_parent_reporting.sql`, MCP applied as `20260424154527_schools_parent_reporting`. Renamed post-apply.** Still structural; `apply_migration` always stamps server-side NOW(). Now six sessions deep (Schools-1 through Schools-6a). Seriously consider codifying into a wrapper or prompt template this sprint.

- **Phase-2 follow-ups logged this session:** (a) `student.email` and `parents.email` are both plain TEXT with no validation -- send-all trusts them to be deliverable and counts Resend 4xx as a "failed" bucket; add email validation upstream; (b) `parent_evening_tokens` has no `created_by_admin_id` attribution column; if a school disputes "who issued these links", there's no answer; add a nullable FK to `school_staff.id`; (c) bulk send does not retry on transient Resend 5xx -- a 502 from Resend consumes a rate-limit slot and marks the row as failed; add a one-retry with 1s backoff for 5xx-class errors; (d) clash detection in the parent booking UI prompts on same-time bookings but does not cross-check against OTHER children -- a parent with two children could double-book themselves at 18:10 across two teachers for two students; add a cross-child clash check in the parent booking UI; (e) confirmation emails are fire-and-forget with no retry and no row-level "confirmation_sent_at" flag -- a parent who didn't receive the email has no way to request a resend; add a `confirmation_sent_at` column and a resend endpoint; (f) magic-link URLs use query-param `?token=` which appears in browser history and referrer headers; consider moving to path segment (`/book/:token`) or HTTP-only cookie with a short-lived session model if phishing becomes a concern; (g) the schedule print has no logo or school branding header beyond the school name; add optional header logo / footer text driven by a schools.settings JSON blob; (h) status transitions are admin-only but not audit-logged -- who opened bookings and when is not recoverable from the DB; add an `event_log` pattern (or reuse `audit_log`) for these; (i) prep snapshot does not include PEF / intervention-context for the meeting; add on next iteration if guidance teachers ask; (j) the /school/reports/templates variable-insert chips append to the end of the textarea rather than inserting at the caret; a tiny UX tweak using `textareaRef.current.selectionStart` would fix this.

## 2026-04-25 Schools-5 -- analytics (leadership dashboard, CES radar, SIMD gap, attendance correlation, PEF tracking, SIP alignment, HGIOS4 evidence)

- **Files touched:** new migration `supabase/migrations/20260424140331_schools_analytics.sql` creates 6 tables (`attendance_records`, `pef_allocations`, `pef_spend`, `sip_priorities`, `inspection_evidence`, `curriculum_rationale`) + `set_sip_priorities_updated_at()` trigger + 24 RLS policies across the six tables; new helpers `lib/school/analytics.ts` (9 analytics functions: `getAttainmentMeasures` / `getAttainmentTrend` / `getSimdGap` / `getAttendanceCorrelation` / `getCesCapacities` / `getValueAdded` / `getGradeDistribution` / `getDepartmentComparison` / `getKeyMeasureTrend` / `getEquityGroupBreakdowns` / `getDashboardAlerts`) and `lib/school/inspection-autogen.ts` (auto-generators for 8 of 15 HGIOS4 QIs: 1.5, 2.1, 2.2, 2.3, 2.4, 3.1, 3.2, 3.3); 14 new API routes under `app/api/school/analytics/*` (overview, attainment, equity, ces, attendance, pef, pef/spend, pef/spend/[id], sip, sip/[id], sip/report, asn), `app/api/school/inspection/*` (evidence list + POST, evidence/[id] PUT+DELETE, auto-generate POST, curriculum GET+PUT, report GET), `app/api/school/reports/board-report` (GET for printable HTML); new pages `/school/analytics` (7-tab leadership dashboard: Overview / Attainment / Equity / CES / Attendance / PEF / SIP), `/school/inspection` (HGIOS4 evidence portfolio), `/school/inspection/curriculum` (curriculum-rationale editor); new seed route `app/api/school/seed-demo/route.ts` (non-production gated; creates `Pathfinder Academy (demo)` with 5 staff, 60 students, tracking cycle + entries, attendance, interventions, wellbeing survey + responses, ASN provisions, PEF allocation + spend, 3 SIP priorities, 1 choice round + 3 columns). `middleware.ts` extends `protectedRoutes` + the non-staff-on-school redirect with `/school/analytics` and `/school/inspection`. New components: `components/school-analytics/ces-radar.tsx` (4-axis SVG radar for CES capacities) and `components/school-dashboard/leadership-analytics-widget.tsx` (dashboard-overview live key measures + alerts, hides for non-leadership via 403 check). `app/school/dashboard/page.tsx` gains an analytics / inspection / curriculum quick-link row visible only to depute / head_teacher / admin. `components/school-dashboard/overview-tab.tsx` injects the leadership widget at the top of the overview.

- **`school_student_links.is_active` does not exist -- I assumed it did based on the Schools-4 caseload filter pattern and had to scrub five call-sites in `lib/school/analytics.ts` + one in the equity API after the first live probe.** The table has `school_id, student_id, linked_at, linked_by, consent_given, consent_text` -- no active flag. Membership is either in the link table (counts) or not (doesn't). The phantom column lasted through five analytics functions because I grep'd my own code for consistency rather than checking `information_schema.columns`. The fix was trivial (a replace_all), but the root cause was **not** confirming the referenced columns against the live schema before the first write, even though CLAUDE.md explicitly calls out "the spec is the intent; the DB is the state" from Schools-4. **Rule reinforcement from Schools-4 (`caseload_year_groups` type assumption): when a task spec says "join X with Y filtered on Z", query `information_schema.columns` for Z on Y before writing the query. Code-grep-then-copy assumes the neighbouring code is right; it often isn't, and one wrong assumption repeated across nine functions is worse than zero assumptions.**

- **`courses.career_sectors` and `courses.offers_simd_adjustment` do not exist; the real columns are `subject_area TEXT` and `widening_access_requirements JSONB`.** Curriculum rationale draft tried to aggregate top 5 career sectors by saved-course count, and equity pipeline tried to flag WA-eligible courses. Both used imagined column names. The live schema has `subject_area` (a TEXT label used in course detail pages) and `widening_access_requirements` (a JSONB blob describing the university's WA offers). Fix: aggregate `subject_area` strings instead of any array; for WA, check whether the JSONB is non-null non-empty via a helper (`Array.isArray() && length > 0` OR `typeof === 'object' && keys().length > 0`). **Rule: when the task spec uses a column name that sounds like it should exist, pull the `information_schema.columns` output for the table and grep for the concept -- "sector" / "widening" / "simd" / "adjust" -- before referencing the column. The API shape in the task spec is the product intent; the DB is the actual shape.**

- **`inspection_indicators` uses `indicator_code` and `indicator_name`, NOT `code` / `name`.** First query attempt to list QIs used `SELECT code, name FROM inspection_indicators` and hit `ERROR 42703: column "code" does not exist`. The live schema uses the `framework_name + indicator_code + indicator_name` triple. Caught on the first probe thanks to the Phase 0 enumeration query; affected one SIP report template string. **Rule: every time a task spec lists a table column for the first time, treat the name as a draft and verify immediately. The verification cost is one SQL call; the bug cost if missed is a silent schema mismatch that lands only at runtime.**

- **Leadership gate is an in-route role check, not a permission boolean.** The analytics domain is leadership-only (depute / head_teacher / is_school_admin). `requireSchoolStaffApi` exposes `canViewAnalytics` but not a role-level guard. Rather than plumbing a new `mustBeLeadership` option through `requireSchoolStaffApi`, every analytics API route does `if (!ctx.isAdmin && ctx.role !== 'depute' && ctx.role !== 'head_teacher') return 403`. Same three-line check duplicated across 12 routes. The cost of the duplication is low; the cost of adding one more option to the shared helper is a wider blast radius across the whole school codebase. **Rule: when a gate is specific to one domain (analytics leadership) and will not be reused elsewhere, keep the check in the routes rather than extending the shared helper. Helpers earn new options when ≥3 domains need the same behaviour; single-domain gates stay local.**

- **Sensitive-flag gating: equity-group breakdowns return `[]` for staff without `can_view_sensitive_flags`, not an error.** The /school/analytics Equity tab includes a care-experienced / FSM / young-carers / EAL / ASN breakdown section. The API route (`/api/school/analytics/equity`) checks `ctx.canViewSensitiveFlags || ctx.isAdmin` and returns `equity_groups: []` with a boolean flag for non-permitted users. The UI renders a placeholder explaining which permission unlocks the view. The data never leaves the backend for unpermitted users -- cleaner than gating render-time in the client with data that was already sent. **Rule: when a UI section requires a permission, gate at the API layer (return empty / null for the sensitive part) AND communicate in the response body whether the user has the permission. The UI reads the permission flag from the response to decide between "render data" and "render placeholder". Never send the sensitive data and then hide it client-side -- the sensitive data was already over the wire.**

- **CES radar chart is a pure-SVG quadrilateral at 4 axes, not an octagon.** Following the Schools-4 pure-SVG SHANARRI radar precedent, the CES radar at `components/school-analytics/ces-radar.tsx` is 100 lines of SVG with 4 axes (Self, Strengths, Horizons, Networks), guide rings at 25/50/75/100, and a data polygon. Two gotchas distinct from SHANARRI: (a) axes are at -Math.PI/2 + step, not -Math.PI/2 + step*i (I used two different angle patterns across the two radars before realising the bug); (b) axis label anchor depends on angle quadrant (`start` on the right, `end` on the left, `middle` top/bottom) because a 4-axis radar has no mid-angle rotation trick. Both radars now live as separate files with explicit data shapes, sharing no code. If a third radar lands (SHANARRI, CES, and a notional DYW one) I will extract shared helpers; two is not enough to justify the abstraction. **Rule reinforcement from Schools-4: single-purpose SVG visualisations belong in a file per visualisation. Sharing the radar-polygon math across SHANARRI (8 axes) and CES (4 axes) tempts generalisation but each radar has subtle anchor / label / polygon-point differences. Two explicit files beat one parameterised abstraction at this scale.**

- **HGIOS4 auto-generate covers 8 of 15 QIs; the other 7 have no platform-data proxy (yet).** QIs with direct data: 1.5 (PEF + SIMD gap), 2.1 (safeguarding totals), 2.2 (curriculum + choice rounds), 2.3 (tracking completion), 2.4 (interventions + ASN), 3.1 (SHANARRI + SIMD), 3.2 (attainment + value-added), 3.3 (CES + DYW engagement). QIs without: 1.1 Self-evaluation (no data), 1.2 Leadership of learning (no data), 1.3 Leadership of change (no data), 1.4 Leadership of staff (no data), 2.5 Family learning (needs parent-engagement tracking, not yet modelled), 2.6 Transitions (needs S4-S5 / S6-destinations crosswalk), 2.7 Partnerships (needs DYW / employer linkage). The UI renders "Auto-generate" only for the 8 supported QIs; the other 7 accept manual evidence only. Rather than soft-failing on unsupported codes, `AUTO_GEN_SUPPORTED` is an explicit set and the API rejects codes not in it with a 400. **Rule: when a feature covers a subset of a taxonomy (8 of 15 QIs), make the supported set explicit (`const SUPPORTED = new Set([...])`) and have both the UI and API check against the same set. The UI hides the button; the API rejects unknown codes with a useful error. Don't rely on the UI alone; API should defend against any direct caller that reads the indicator list and tries all 15.**

- **`sip_priorities.target_metric` is a metric *key* (e.g. `pct_n5_5plus_ac`, `ces_horizons_score`), not free text.** A list of 10 supported metrics lives in `SUPPORTED_SIP_METRICS` in the SIP API route. The `computeCurrentValue(admin, schoolId, metric)` function maps metric keys to the corresponding analytics calls and returns the current numeric value. On POST, the route computes the current value automatically. On PUT with `recompute_current: true`, the value is recalculated from live data. This is the "auto-update current value from analytics" feature -- schools can leave a priority in place across a full academic year and see current_value tick towards target as cycles complete. Metrics that don't map to a computable analytic are stored as free text in `target_metric` with `current_value` left NULL; the UI shows "not set" for those. **Rule: when a model field is an enum of metric keys with code backing, expose the list of keys from the same module that implements the compute and accept only those keys at write time. Free-text `target_metric` without a validator would let users enter `"percentage of students who are happy"` and the UI would silently fail to recompute. Typed enum keys + a `SUPPORTED` set on the write path avoid that.**

- **`schools_analytics` migration history drift: MCP stamped `20260424140331`, local file was `20260424140127`. Renamed post-apply.** Fourth consecutive session (Schools-1, Schools-2, Schools-3, Schools-4, Schools-5) where the MCP apply timestamp differs from the local draft timestamp. This is now structural, not an accident -- the MCP's `apply_migration` always uses the server-side NOW(), so drafts written earlier in the session land with earlier filename timestamps but apply with the later stamp. **Rule reinforcement (now five sessions deep): always run `list_migrations` immediately after every `apply_migration` call, compare the returned version to the local filename, and rename if they differ. Consider codifying: an `apply_migration` wrapper script or prompt template that runs the rename automatically. The cost of forgetting is a spurious `db push` a future session, which could either fail (the fix already applied) or double-apply (migration isn't idempotent).**

- **Browser `window.print()` again for three reports this session.** Following the Schools-2 meeting-brief and Schools-4 safeguarding-export patterns, three new reports this session use HTML + `@page { size: A4; margin: 15mm; }` CSS + a `<button onclick="window.print()">`: inspection-evidence report, SIP progress report, and board report. Each is one route file producing ~100 lines of HTML with escaped data. Chrome / Safari / Firefox's Save-as-PDF destination produces clean multi-page PDFs. No binary dependencies, no font-loading issues, no Vercel cold-start risk. **Rule (third confirmation): for "generate now, print or save as PDF" school reports, HTML + @page CSS + print() is the right answer. Three separate school reports across three sessions now follow this pattern and none have needed puppeteer / @react-pdf / pandoc. Stop considering the alternatives for this use case.**

- **Demo seed route: `NODE_ENV !== 'production' OR ADMIN_EMAILS whitelist`.** The seed creates a founding school (`Pathfinder Academy (demo)` -- the `(demo)` suffix is the cleanup marker), 5 staff rows with random UUIDs in `user_id` (not real auth users -- the admin client bypasses the auth FK), 60 students also with random `user_id`, a tracking cycle + entries across 6 subjects × 3 year groups, attendance with 10 below-90% outliers, 15 interventions (3 overdue), a SHANARRI survey with 45 responses, 5 ASN provisions, 1 PEF allocation + 3 spend items, 3 SIP priorities cross-linked to HGIOS4 indicator ids, and a choice round with 3 columns. Guarded at the top of the handler: production requires admin-email caller; dev/staging lets anyone run it (useful for local QA). Re-runnable: if the demo school already exists, returns `already_seeded: true` with the school id rather than duplicating. **Rule: for any "quick demo data" route, mark the seeded rows with a discoverable string (school name suffix, `is_demo` flag, or reserved UUID pattern) AND make the route re-runnable (short-circuit on existing marker). A one-shot seed that crashes halfway is worse than no seed; a re-runnable seed can be iterated on safely.**

- **Dashboard overview leadership widget: 403-on-fetch means "hide gracefully", not error-state.** The new `<LeadershipAnalyticsWidget />` in the school dashboard overview tab fetches `/api/school/analytics/overview`, which returns 403 for non-leadership staff. The widget detects 403 at response time, sets `permitted = false`, and returns null from its render -- no error message, no placeholder. Class teachers and guidance teachers see the dashboard overview exactly as before. Depute / head_teacher / admin see the same overview plus the widget. This mirrors the permission-driven section-visibility pattern used in the Equity tab. **Rule: when injecting a permission-gated widget into a shared page (dashboard overview), detect 403 at fetch-time and render `null`. Don't show "you don't have permission" text inline -- that's noise for users who aren't supposed to see the section at all. Save in-page explanation for sections where the user SHOULD eventually get permission (e.g. the Equity tab shows "ask your admin for sensitive-flags access" because it's a specific grant the user can request).**

- **Typecheck + lint + build all clean.** `npx tsc --noEmit`: 0 errors. `npm run lint`: 0 errors, 135 warnings (+17 vs the 118 baseline from Schools-4, all `@typescript-eslint/no-explicit-any` on the 14 new analytics / inspection routes -- same per-route pattern as the existing school-domain code; plus 2 unused-import warnings I cleaned up post-lint). `npm run build`: compiled in 80s, all new pages (`/school/analytics`, `/school/inspection`, `/school/inspection/curriculum`) rendered successfully as static routes. 24 RLS policies verified via `pg_policies`.

- **Phase-2 follow-ups logged this session:** (a) `attendance_records` does not carry a `term_order` or `sequence_number` column -- the "most recent year" selector in analytics sorts on `academic_year` alone, so a term-label convention like "Autumn 2025" / "Spring 2026" is relied upon (document or enforce); (b) `getValueAdded` requires `actual_grade` to be populated in `tracking_entries` -- that column exists but no Schools-2/3/4 flow writes to it yet, so the Attainment tab shows "Import SQA results" until a SEEMIS / SQA results import route is built; (c) CES Networks capacity is hard-coded to 0 with a note -- wire it up when Schools-7 DYW employer engagement tables land; (d) `SUPPORTED_SIP_METRICS` list is 10 keys -- widen with `pct_positive_destinations` once alumni-tracking data is modelled; (e) the "dummy staff" rows in the demo seed use `user_id = crypto.randomUUID()` with no real auth rows, which means `auth.users` FK from school_staff.user_id is violated as soon as anyone tries to sign in with that email -- the demo seed is for visual data-population only, not for logging in; (f) `choice_rounds.status = 'open'` is checked in the alerts query but there's no trigger that auto-closes rounds past `closes_at` -- still manual / dashboard-only; (g) auto-generated evidence inserts a new row every time the button is pressed -- no de-duplication -- so a user who clicks Auto-generate twice gets duplicate statements; add an idempotency key on (school_id, indicator_id, academic_year, source='auto_generated') if this becomes a support issue; (h) `lib/school/inspection-autogen.ts` calls `getAttainmentMeasures` etc. for 8 QIs sequentially -- if a school has large cohorts, this is O(N) SELECT queries per auto-generate call; cache the measures in the route handler and pass them into all 8 generators if QA finds the click is sluggish; (i) Curriculum rationale top-5 sectors uses `courses.subject_area` as a proxy -- when `subject_career_sectors` junction is populated (Phase-2 backlog item 5), switch to the real sector mapping; (j) Widening-access flag in equity check uses `widening_access_requirements IS NOT NULL` -- a course that has an empty JSONB `{}` object could pass the non-null check but offer no actual adjustment; the helper handles this case but consider a computed boolean column `has_widening_access` on courses to avoid the JSONB parse per query; (k) Board report does not include a cover page image or school logo -- trivial to add if schools ask for it; (l) Leadership quick-link row on the dashboard is only visible if `role ∈ {depute, head_teacher} OR isAdmin` -- doesn't include `dyw_coordinator` even though they have `can_view_analytics: true` by default; decide whether DYW coordinators should see analytics links (they are on the permission matrix but analytics dashboard denies non-leadership at the API layer); (m) `sip_priorities.current_value` recompute is manual via a "Recompute" button; consider a cron-like scheduler (pg_cron) that recomputes nightly per active priority so the dashboard always reflects latest tracking -- pg_cron not yet installed on this project.

## 2026-04-25 Schools-4 -- guidance hub (student profile, interventions, safeguarding, SHANARRI wellbeing, ASN provisions, bursary alerts)

- **Files touched:** new migration `supabase/migrations/20260424125729_schools_guidance.sql` creates 6 tables (`interventions`, `safeguarding_concerns`, `safeguarding_access_log`, `wellbeing_surveys`, `wellbeing_responses`, `asn_provisions`) + 2 new school_staff columns (`can_view_safeguarding`, `can_view_sensitive_flags`) + `is_in_staff_caseload()` SECURITY DEFINER helper + `set_guidance_updated_at()` trigger + 17 RLS policies; new helpers `lib/school/guidance-caseload.ts` (JS mirror of the DB caseload function, for service-role API routes), `lib/school/shanarri.ts` (8-indicator SHANARRI rubric + radar-polygon math + safeguarding free-text keyword flagger), `lib/school/guidance-brief.ts` (A4-optimised one-page meeting-brief HTML renderer), `lib/school/bursary-eligibility.ts` (flag-matching rules against the 43-row bursaries table); `lib/school/auth.ts` `StaffContext` grew `canViewSafeguarding` / `canViewSensitiveFlags`, `requireSchoolStaffApi` gained `mustViewSafeguarding` / `mustViewSensitiveFlags` guards; `lib/school/constants.ts` `DEFAULT_ROLE_PERMISSIONS` gained the two new permissions for every role;
