`app/api/school/me/route.ts` emits the new staff fields; `app/api/school/register/route.ts` + `app/api/school/join-staff/route.ts` set the two new permissions on insert; `components/school-dashboard/types.ts` `DashboardMe.staff` gained the two new booleans; 13 new API routes under `app/api/school/guidance/*`, `app/api/student/wellbeing/*`; new pages `/school/guidance` (caseload + overdue + bursary alerts), `/school/guidance/[studentId]` (7-tab profile: overview / interventions / tracking history / wellbeing / safeguarding / asn / notes), `/school/guidance/safeguarding` (log), `/school/guidance/safeguarding/new` (concern form), `/school/guidance/safeguarding/[id]` (concern detail + access log + escalation flow), `/school/guidance/wellbeing` (survey list + create), `/school/guidance/wellbeing/[id]` (aggregate SHANARRI + per-student drill-down if named), `/wellbeing/[surveyId]` (student-facing 8-question SHANARRI form); new components `components/school-guidance/shanarri-radar.tsx` (pure-SVG octagonal radar with concentric guides), `components/school-guidance/intervention-form.tsx` (modal with action-items + follow-up + confidentiality + PEF cost), `components/dashboard/wellbeing-banner.tsx` (student-dashboard CTA). `middleware.ts` extends `protectedRoutes` + `studentOnlyPrefixes` + the non-staff-on-school redirect with `/school/guidance` and `/wellbeing`. `app/school/dashboard/page.tsx` gains a guidance quick-link row visible only to staff with `canViewIndividualStudents`.

- **Append-only safeguarding: NO UPDATE or DELETE policies exist.** `safeguarding_concerns` and `safeguarding_access_log` are deliberately RLS-incomplete -- the four verbs aren't all covered. A missing UPDATE/DELETE policy on a RLS-enabled table blocks all writes of that verb, which is what we want. Corrections to an existing concern are modelled as a new row with `supersedes_id` pointing at the superseded row. This mirrors the Scottish GIRFEC guidance that child-protection records must be immutable and audit-trail-preserving. Downstream consequence: no in-UI "edit" flow for concerns, only "raise replacement with supersedes_id". **Rule: for domains that demand audit-preservation (safeguarding, child protection, legally-privileged data), leave the UPDATE / DELETE policies off rather than adding restrictive ones. RLS defaults to deny, so the absence of a policy for a verb IS the access control -- and it's the cleanest form of immutability because no clever rewrite of the policy can relax it later without a visible migration.**

- **PostgreSQL SELECT triggers don't exist -- access logging lives in the API.** The original spec had a `log_safeguarding_access()` trigger idea that we dropped in favour of explicit `INSERT INTO safeguarding_access_log` calls from every API route that serves concern data (GET single concern logs 'viewed', POST logs 'created', export logs 'exported'). Postgres only fires triggers on INSERT / UPDATE / DELETE / TRUNCATE, not SELECT. Implication: if someone bypasses the API and reads `safeguarding_concerns` directly via MCP `execute_sql` as service role, the access is not logged. The mitigation is: (a) RLS denies direct reads to anyone except `can_view_safeguarding` staff; (b) service-role reads show up in the Supabase audit log at the infrastructure layer; (c) every API route that serves this data writes the access row. **Rule: when a domain requires "every access is logged" semantics, accept that SELECT-trigger isn't a PG feature and route all reads through an API layer that logs access before returning data. Don't try to emulate a SELECT trigger via a view + SECURITY DEFINER function -- the function still doesn't fire on the underlying SELECT, and the engineering overhead isn't worth it.**

- **Caseload filtering must live in BOTH the DB helper (for RLS) AND a JS helper (for service-role API routes) because the admin client bypasses RLS.** `is_in_staff_caseload(student_id, staff_user_id)` is a SECURITY DEFINER function referenced by RLS policies on `interventions` and `asn_provisions`. But every Schools-4 API route uses the service-role admin client (same pattern as Schools-2 / 3), which bypasses RLS entirely. So `lib/school/guidance-caseload.ts` exports `canStaffSeeStudent()` -- a pure JS mirror of the DB function -- and every API route that returns student-scoped data first fetches the staff's caseload, then filters student rows in application code. The two implementations must stay in sync; the DB version is load-bearing for student/parent clients that CAN hit the DB directly via the anon client. **Rule: when a business rule appears in RLS, and the app has service-role API routes that bypass RLS, the rule needs a second implementation in application code for the service-role path. Document the pair in the DB-function's comment block and the JS-module's header so future maintenance updates both.**

- **Student `school_stage` is a Postgres ENUM, not TEXT -- cast to `::text` before comparing with TEXT[] caseload filters.** `school_staff.caseload_year_groups` is `TEXT[]` (confirmed via `information_schema.columns`), but `students.school_stage` is a USER-DEFINED enum (`s2, s3, s4, s5, s6, college, mature`). An initial draft of `is_in_staff_caseload()` did `v_student.school_stage = ANY(v_staff.caseload_year_groups)` and failed with "operator does not exist: school_stage = text". Fix: `v_student.school_stage::text = ANY(v_staff.caseload_year_groups)`. The Postgres error message is clear in isolation but easy to miss because the function executed with SECURITY DEFINER in the RLS policy context, and Supabase doesn't always surface PL/pgSQL errors through the client. **Rule: when writing a helper function that compares a students-table column against a school_staff filter column, cross-check the column types via `information_schema.columns`. User-defined enums need explicit `::text` casts when the filter side is `TEXT[]`.**

- **Caseload columns were JSONB in the spec but TEXT[] in the live schema -- the DB is the source of truth.** Task prompt specified `caseload_year_groups JSONB` with a function using `jsonb_array_elements_text()`. A Phase 0 `information_schema.columns` check showed the columns were already `ARRAY` (TEXT[]). Adapted the helper to `= ANY(v_staff.caseload_year_groups)` and dropped the JSONB extraction. The prompt was written before the schema landed; the Phase 0 check caught the drift. **Rule: for any data-type-sensitive detail in a task spec -- column types, enum values, CHECK constraint contents -- treat the spec as a draft and verify against the live schema. The spec is the intent; the DB is the state.**

- **`wellbeing_responses` anonymity is enforced by setting `student_id = NULL` at INSERT, NOT by a "hidden on read" RLS predicate.** An early design considered a SELECT policy that hid the `student_id` column when the survey's `is_anonymous = true`, but PG's RLS operates at the row level, not the column level. The correct pattern: the anonymous survey's submit route (`/api/student/wellbeing/responses`) stores `student_id = null` in the database. The row is then cryptographically unlinkable back to any student. The one-per-student UNIQUE constraint `(survey_id, student_id)` still allows multiple NULL student_ids (PG treats NULLs as distinct), which is the behaviour we want -- anonymous submissions can technically double-submit from the same account, but that's a minor data-quality concern, not a privacy concern. **Rule: if anonymity is a product requirement, design the write path to drop the link rather than the read path to hide it. "Store it and hide it" can be reversed by a future schema change or misconfigured admin tool; "never store it" cannot.**

- **SHANARRI radar is 40 lines of pure SVG, no chart library.** The radar chart draws an octagon with eight score axes (Safe, Healthy, Achieving, Nurtured, Active, Respected, Responsible, Included). `lib/school/shanarri.ts` exports `radarPoints(scores, cx, cy, radius)` which returns an SVG `points` attribute string. Five concentric guide polygons show the 1-5 grid; one data polygon fills at 25% opacity. The component is `<svg>` + `<polygon>` + `<text>` -- no recharts, no chartjs, no d3. Total 60 lines across the helper + component. Beats installing a 200KB chart library for one chart shape. **Rule: for single-purpose data visualisations (radar, single bar, sparkline), write it as SVG by hand rather than reaching for a chart library. The maintenance cost of 60 lines is tiny; the payoff is no new dep + full control over pixel-perfect appearance.**

- **Meeting-brief PDF = HTML + `@media print`, same as parent reports -- don't install puppeteer / react-pdf.** The "generate meeting brief" button on the student profile links to `/api/school/guidance/meeting-brief/[studentId]`, which server-renders an HTML page with `@page { size: A4; margin: 12mm; }` CSS and a "Print / Save as PDF" button that calls `window.print()`. Chrome's print dialog produces a clean one-page PDF. The pattern is identical to `/school/reports/[id]/print` from Schools-2. Server-side, no binary dependencies, no font-loading issues. **Rule reinforcement from Schools-2: browser print-to-PDF is a legitimate PDF flow for school reporting. Reserve a real PDF library only if the product needs pre-rendered PDFs (e.g. email attachments). For "generate now, print or save" flows, HTML + `@page` CSS is the right answer.**

- **Extension pattern for school_staff permissions: FOUR call-sites need updating -- DB, constants, register, join-staff.** Adding `can_view_safeguarding` and `can_view_sensitive_flags` required: (a) `ALTER TABLE school_staff ADD COLUMN ...` in the migration + `UPDATE` backfill per role; (b) `DEFAULT_ROLE_PERMISSIONS` in `lib/school/constants.ts` now includes the new keys for every role; (c) `/api/school/register` sets both to `true` for the registering admin; (d) `/api/school/join-staff` upserts both from the DEFAULT map. Missing any one of these four creates a silent authorization hole: the permission is either not set at all (users default to false forever), or not readable through the `/api/school/me` surface (the UI never sees it), or not provisioned when new staff join. Grep for every call-site of the older permissions before declaring the extension complete. **Rule reinforcement from Schools-1: when adding a new permission column, grep for the names of existing permissions (`can_view_individual_students`, `can_edit_tracking`) and audit every occurrence -- the five-places-same-shape pattern is a strong hint that you're missing a call-site if you only update three.**

- **`school_notifications` table does NOT exist yet -- escalation notifications are parked as a Phase-2 item.** The spec mentioned creating `school_notification` rows when a safeguarding concern is escalated or a follow-up date passes. A quick `information_schema.tables` check confirmed no such table exists. Rather than adding it in this session (which would mean also building the notifications UI + read/mark-read flow), the session shipped without it: escalated concerns trigger an `escalated` access-log entry but no notification. Written up as a Phase-2 follow-up. **Rule: when a spec mentions a dependency table that doesn't exist, don't silently create it as a side effect of the current feature. Flag it, park it, and ship what you can without it -- a notifications system is its own feature with its own UX decisions (toast? badge? email?), not a one-liner.**

- **Typecheck + lint + build all clean.** `npx tsc --noEmit`: 0 errors. `npm run lint`: 0 errors, 118 warnings (+9 vs the 109 baseline from Schools-3, all `@typescript-eslint/no-explicit-any` on the new guidance route files -- same per-route pattern as the pre-existing school-domain code). `npm run build`: compiled in 60s, 466 pages (up from 438 in Schools-3 -- 28 new pages added for the guidance flows), all 8 new pages (`/school/guidance`, `/school/guidance/[studentId]`, `/school/guidance/safeguarding`, `/school/guidance/safeguarding/new`, `/school/guidance/safeguarding/[id]`, `/school/guidance/wellbeing`, `/school/guidance/wellbeing/[id]`, `/wellbeing/[surveyId]`) rendered successfully.

- **Phase-2 follow-ups logged this session:** (a) `school_notifications` table + UI for in-app notification of safeguarding escalations, follow-up dates, ASN review dates; (b) Documents & Notes tab is a placeholder -- Supabase storage bucket + upload flow for IEP PDFs / letters / reports per student; (c) anonymous wellbeing responses have NULL student_id which allows duplicates from the same account (PG treats NULL as distinct in UNIQUE constraints) -- add an optional `auth_user_hash` (hashed student id) column if we need guaranteed one-per-user anonymous semantics; (d) SHANARRI survey trend over time currently renders only the latest response -- add an overlay / small-multiples view for students with multiple completed surveys; (e) departmental ASN dashboard (mentioned in spec task 6c as a component for Schools-5) not yet created -- imports into analytics landed in no file this session; (f) CP-file export has no password-protection or retention-period metadata -- social work hand-off may need those fields when the product engages with local authorities; (g) bursary eligibility cross-check uses `simd_quintile_max` with a simple decile->quintile calculation; some bursaries use `simd_decile_max` semantics elsewhere in the codebase -- audit for consistency; (h) meeting brief subject list uses `class_students` / `class_assignments`, so students who aren't in any tracked classes render an empty "no tracking data" block -- add a fallback to `student_grades` or `student_subject_choices` when classes aren't populated; (i) intervention `action_items` JSONB is schema-free (freeform objects with `description` / `due_date` / `is_completed` keys) -- if we need structured sub-tasks with assignees, promote to its own table; (j) guidance notes editor is "paste-and-save" plain text for now -- consider TipTap or similar rich-text if staff ask for formatting.

## 2026-04-25 Schools-3 -- subject choice collection (rounds, columns, consequence modelling, demand heatmap, parent approval, SEEMIS export)

- **Files touched:** new migration `supabase/migrations/20260424122343_schools_subject_choices.sql` creates 5 tables (`choice_rounds`, `choice_round_columns`, `choice_round_column_subjects`, `student_choices`, `student_choice_items`) + 2 demand-recalc triggers (AFTER INSERT / UPDATE / DELETE on `student_choice_items` plus AFTER UPDATE OF status on `student_choices`) + 20 RLS policies; new helpers `lib/school/choice-consequences.ts` (CourseFit traffic-light + sector coverage compute) and `lib/school/student-auth.ts` (`requireStudentApi` / `requireParentApi` admin-client guards parallel to existing `requireSchoolStaffApi`); 14 new API routes under `app/api/school/choices/*`, `app/api/student/choices/*`, `app/api/parent/choices/*`; new pages `/school/choices`, `/school/choices/new`, `/school/choices/[id]/setup` (column builder with inline edit + subject picker), `/school/choices/[id]/demand` (horizontal-bar heatmap with oversubscription highlighting), `/student/choices`, `/student/choices/[roundId]` (radio/checkbox form with sticky sidebar showing live consequences), `/parent/choices`, `/parent/choices/[id]` (approve / reject-with-comment flow); `middleware.ts` extends `protectedRoutes` + the student-only-prefix + non-staff redirect blocks for the three new surfaces; `components/school-dashboard/subjects-tab.tsx` gains a callout linking to the new rounds hub; `components/dashboard/subject-choices-section.tsx` gains a student-side banner linking to `/student/choices`; `components/dashboard/parent-dashboard-v2.tsx` gains a Subject-choice-approvals panel linking to `/parent/choices`.

- **Denormalised `current_demand` column + AFTER-trigger recalc beats a VIEW or GROUP BY query every time the heatmap loads.** Schools-2 had a similar choice: compute `tracking_entries` completion ratios on-demand (LIVE GROUP BY across a large table) or pre-aggregate. The heatmap is read-hot and write-cold (every page load fetches the grid, but students only write when submitting). An AFTER INSERT / UPDATE / DELETE trigger on `student_choice_items` + an AFTER UPDATE OF status trigger on `student_choices` maintains `choice_round_column_subjects.current_demand` in exactly the shape the heatmap needs — one row per (column, subject). The recount is scoped to the affected `column_subject_id(s)` from OLD / NEW, not a whole-table requery. The status-change trigger is the subtle bit: a draft flipping to `submitted` must re-count every item in that submission (the item rows didn't change, just the parent's status). **Rule: for any heatmap / leaderboard / counter that a UI reads on every page load, denormalise the count into a column on the row-being-displayed and maintain it with an AFTER-OP trigger scoped to the affected ids. Don't try to enforce this invariant in application code across every writer — RLS-permitted writes bypass it. A trigger enforces the invariant inside the database, independent of who wrote and via which path.**

- **Committed-status gate in the demand recount keeps drafts out of the heatmap — but you need it in BOTH item-level AND status-level triggers.** Drafts are a student's private in-progress scratchpad; they should not inflate the "50 students picked Physics" number a faculty head sees. The WHERE clause in the recalc UPDATE filters `sc.status IN ('submitted','parent_pending','confirmed') AND sci.is_reserve = false`. The item-level trigger handles inserts/updates/deletes of picks. But a `draft -> submitted` status flip changes NO items — an existing pick that didn't count yesterday suddenly counts today. Covered by the second trigger (`AFTER UPDATE OF status ON student_choices`) which re-queries demand for every item in the flipped submission. Without this, the demand bar stays stuck at zero until the student wiggles a pick. **Rule: when a denormalised counter is filtered by a parent row's status, there must be a trigger on BOTH the child rows AND the parent's filter column. Missing either leaves the counter silently stale for the window the parent flips without the child changing.**

- **The "row-count = row-read" trap: `requireSchoolStaffApi` + `is_school_admin OR can_manage_tracking` policy check duplicated in-app AND in-RLS produces double gating, not zero gating.** Initial draft of the column-builder API had two guards: `requireSchoolStaffApi({ mustManageTracking: true })` in the route, AND the RLS policy requires the same. Both pass fine. But when the RLS side is tightened by a new policy later, the app-side guard can mask it — an admin API route using the service-role client bypasses RLS entirely. The service-role client is NOT subject to RLS. So the app-side guard is the ONLY gate on the write path for schools routes; RLS on those tables protects against direct-from-browser queries (students / parents) but not against the admin client. Correct pattern: rely on `requireSchoolStaffApi({ mustManageTracking: true })` as the authoritative gate in the route, and keep RLS as a belt-and-braces for anything that might one day be queried directly. **Rule: when a route uses the service-role admin client (the standard pattern in `lib/school/auth.ts`), the app-level guard IS the only real gate for writes — RLS on the same tables protects only non-admin clients (student / parent browsers). Don't trust that "we have RLS" means "the endpoint is safe"; the admin client flies past RLS.**

- **The "parents update student_choices" RLS policy was split into two separate policies — one for general updates the student makes (scoped to `student_id = auth.uid()`), one for parent approvals (scoped to the parent-student link) — rather than one combined policy.** First attempt fused both in a single UPDATE USING clause joined by OR. That technically works but produces confusing policy output: `supabase/list_policies` shows one policy named "Students/parents update" that looks like a combined permission. Splitting them into `"Students update own choices while round open"` and `"Parents approve linked student choices"` lets each policy describe one invariant cleanly. Postgres OR's them at eval time anyway (multiple policies for the same table + verb are OR'd). Same shape pattern used in Schools-2 tracking_entries (teacher-update vs admin-override). **Rule: write one RLS policy per business-role-that-can-do-the-thing, not a single policy with `OR` branches for multiple roles. Two policies = two sentences in the auth model; one combined policy = one paragraph that is harder to reason about during audit.**

- **Consequence modelling (traffic-light course fit) uses `course_subject_requirements` + student's `saved_courses` — NOT `student_grades` — so it works before the student has entered any grades.** Course fit in the choice form says "pick Physics because otherwise you lose your Glasgow Engineering saved course". The natural design was to cross-reference `student_grades` against `course_subject_requirements.min_grade`. But S3-going-into-S4 students have zero grades yet — they haven't sat N5s. For the choice-time UX, the question is "which saved courses remain achievable given the SUBJECTS you pick" — we ignore min_grade entirely at this stage and just count required-subject match. A subject that satisfies the requirement at ANY grade still counts. **Rule: for pre-qualification choice flows (S3→S4, S2→S3), compare subject IDs against requirements; do not try to also enforce `min_grade` — the student has no grades yet. For post-qualification flows (S5→S6, UCAS recs), layer grades on top.**

- **Debounced `useRef<Timeout>` for consequence fetch + debounced save is two independent timers on the same selection state, not one.** Student choice form needs two effects off the same selection state: (1) call `/consequences` at 250ms debounce to repaint the sidebar; (2) call `PUT /api/student/choices/[roundId]` at 700ms debounce to auto-save the draft. Using ONE timer for both would mean consequences only refresh after save completes — 700ms of lag on every pick, visible to the user. Two refs + two `useEffect`s with the same dep array but different cadence gives tight sidebar feedback AND background draft save without fighting each other. **Rule: when two network calls depend on the same state but have different user-expected cadences (real-time UI feedback vs eventual-consistency persistence), use two separate debounced timers. Sharing one timer for both produces a UX bound to the slower of the two.**

- **Reserve items with `is_reserve = true` need explicit exclusion from the demand count even though they share the column_subject_id FK.** Students can nominate 1-2 reserves per column (picks 2 of 3 where the school closes low-demand classes). Reserves should NOT inflate demand — they're conditional. The demand trigger filters `sci.is_reserve = false`. The submit validator counts only non-reserve picks per column. The CSV export annotates reserves with `(reserve N)` suffix. Miss any of these three and the demand heatmap gets bogus numbers or the submit blocks students who did fill their required columns. **Rule: when a column has a semantic "primary vs alternate" distinction, make it a boolean on the child row (not a separate table), but audit every aggregation / counter / validator for the filter. The filter is load-bearing in three places: demand trigger, submit validator, CSV export — forgetting one undermines the others.**

- **SEEMIS CSV pivot: one row per (sub, column) string cell + stream join in JS is cleaner than SQL crosstab.** SEEMIS expects `SCN, Last name, First name, Reg class, [col 1 subject], [col 2 subject], ...` — a pivot where columns are dynamic (depends on round structure). Postgres `CROSSTAB` extension exists but our project doesn't install `tablefunc`, and even if it did the column count is unknown until query time. The pragmatic shape: SELECT submissions + items in two separate queries, build a `Map<${submissionId}:${columnId}, string>` in JS, then iterate `columns[]` in order to emit each row. Handles multi-select columns by concatenating with `; ` and tagging reserves. **Rule: for CSV exports with dynamic column ordering (columns depend on runtime data, not the schema), do the pivot in application code via a `Map`, not in SQL. Postgres doesn't gracefully handle "I don't know how many columns there are until I query" — JS does.**

- **Phase 0 table-existence check before writing ANY migration code: it's cheap.** Opened session with `SELECT table_name FROM information_schema.tables WHERE table_name LIKE '%choice%'` via MCP `execute_sql`. Found 3 pre-existing tables (`course_choice_rules`, `student_academy_choices`, `student_subject_choices`) — the legacy free-choice system, NOT the column-based structure this session builds. Good to know: don't collide with those names, don't assume the new schema supersedes them (they serve a different UX). Schools-2 flagged the same rule ("check row counts on existing tables before choosing a migration strategy"). This session's variant: "check table NAMES before choosing your new table names". **Rule: before picking names for new tables, run a `LIKE '%domain_word%'` query against `information_schema.tables`. If prior work already occupied the name you wanted, adapt — don't pick a more-confusing name. Confusion about whether `student_subject_choices` and `student_choices` represent the same thing is a six-month-later bug.**

- **Migration history rename again: MCP stamped `20260424122343` (same day 23:22 UTC), local file drafted as `20260425100000`. Renamed post-apply.** Third consecutive session in which the MCP-apply timestamp did NOT match the local draft filename. Rule is still "rename local to match remote version from `list_migrations`", proven out across Schools-1, Schools-2, and Schools-3. **Rule reinforcement: this drift is structural, not accidental. If a future session writes a script to detect post-apply drift, it should run after every `apply_migration` call — not as a cleanup pass at session end. A forgotten rename in the middle of a session means the next `db diff` shows a spurious "new migration" that will try to re-apply.**

- **Typecheck + lint + build all clean.** `npx tsc --noEmit`: 0 errors. `npm run lint`: 0 errors, 109 warnings (+10 vs the 99 baseline from Schools-2, all `@typescript-eslint/no-explicit-any` on the 14 new route files — same per-route pattern as the existing school-domain code). `npm run build`: compiled successfully, all 8 new pages (`/school/choices`, `/school/choices/new`, `/school/choices/[id]/setup`, `/school/choices/[id]/demand`, `/student/choices`, `/student/choices/[roundId]`, `/parent/choices`, `/parent/choices/[id]`) rendered.

- **Phase-2 follow-ups logged this session:** (a) email notifications to parents when a student submits with `requires_parent_approval = true` (currently parent-dashboard pull only); (b) bulk "approve all" on parent dashboard for parents with multiple children across rounds; (c) `parent_token` column provisioned for magic-link approval without sign-in, not yet wired to an email flow; (d) demand heatmap currently counts only non-reserve picks — add a "reserve" column to the heatmap for schools who want to see waitlist depth; (e) a round should autocomplete subject-level from transition (e.g. `s3_to_s4` round defaults all subject rows to N5 qualification_type) — currently the school has to set level per subject; (f) consequence modelling ignores `course_subject_requirements.min_grade` — phase 2 when grade-aware UX lands; (g) the column builder's subject dropdown does not filter by qualification level availability (it shows every subject regardless of `is_available_n5` etc) — tighten when subjects master list grows; (h) no cascade to `subjects_offered` on schools table — a school that adds a subject to any column in a round should probably back-fill that subject into `schools.subjects_offered` so benchmarking reflects reality; (i) `/api/school/choices/export` is a GET that returns CSV inline — a large school with 200+ submissions will produce a ~50KB file; still fine at that scale but watch if it grows 10x; (j) parent approval does not currently re-route to `/student/choices/[roundId]?review=true` for "send back" — the student just sees the comment in the banner. Add a deep-link query param.

## 2026-04-25 Schools-2 -- grade tracking (cycles, class grid, comment banks, custom metrics, department analytics, parent reports)

- **Files touched:** new migration `supabase/migrations/20260424113639_schools_tracking.sql` creates 8 tables (`tracking_cycles`, `class_assignments`, `class_students`, `comment_banks`, `tracking_entries`, `school_tracking_metrics`, `report_templates`, `parent_reports`) + `can_manage_tracking` column on `school_staff` + `set_current_tracking_cycle()` trigger (only-one-current enforcement) + `set_tracking_entry_updated_at()` trigger + 32 RLS policies across the 8 new tables; new helper `lib/school/seed-tracking-defaults.ts` seeds 3 default metrics + 10 default comment templates + 1 default report template on school creation; `lib/school/comment-template.ts` implements Mustache-style `{{key}}` scalar + `{{#section}}...{{/section}}` section rendering (used by the grid comment picker and the report renderer); `lib/school/render-report.ts` exports colour-helper functions + `renderReportHtml`; `lib/school/auth.ts` `StaffContext` grew `staffId`, `canEditTracking`, `canManageTracking`, `department`, `requireSchoolStaffApi` gained `mustEditTracking` / `mustManageTracking` guards; `lib/school/constants.ts` `DEFAULT_ROLE_PERMISSIONS` gained `can_manage_tracking` entry for every role (depute / head_teacher / admin = true); `app/api/school/register/route.ts` calls `seedTrackingDefaults()` after creating the school; `app/api/school/join-staff/route.ts` passes through the new permission; `app/api/school/me/route.ts` emits the new staff fields; `components/school-dashboard/types.ts` `DashboardMe.staff` gained `staffId`, `department`, `canEditTracking`, `canManageTracking`; `middleware.ts` protects `/school/tracking`, `/school/departments`, `/school/reports` and redirects non-staff. 17 new API routes under `app/api/school/tracking/*` and `app/api/school/reports/*` for cycles, classes, students, entries (single + bulk), class fetch, reference data, metrics, comments, summary, departments, drill, report generate / list / preview / send. New pages: `/school/tracking`, `/school/tracking/[classId]`, `/school/tracking/classes/new`, `/school/tracking/comments`, `/school/departments`, `/school/departments/[dept]`, `/school/reports`, `/school/reports/[id]/print`. New components: `components/school-tracking/tracking-grid.tsx` (inline editable grid with bulk-fill, column-fill, comment picker, auto-save debounce) + `components/school-dashboard/tracking-tab.tsx` (dashboard summary with completion / key measures / distribution / department laggards).

- **Schools-2 shipped on top of empty production tables: 0 schools, 0 staff, 0 tracking_entries when this session started.** Phase 0 `list_tables` + row counts confirmed Schools-1 had deployed schema but no real schools had registered yet. This meant every RLS policy, trigger, and seed path was new ground — no backwards-compat guardrails needed, but also no user traffic to validate against. Decision: build all 8 tables + 32 policies + 3 default seeds + 17 API routes in one migration + one session, treating this as a greenfield addition rather than a migration over live data. **Rule: when extending a shipped domain, check row counts on the existing tables before choosing a migration strategy. Empty tables = safe to add CHECK constraints, NOT NULL columns, and unique indexes without back-fill; populated tables demand the non-destructive pattern from Schools-1 (`ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS`, `DROP CONSTRAINT IF EXISTS` then `ADD CONSTRAINT`).**

- **`types/database.ts` was NOT hand-edited in this session — every school route uses `as any` casts against `.from('table_name')`.** Schools-1 shipped without adding any of the `schools`, `school_staff`, `school_student_links`, `school_join_codes`, `territories`, `qualification_types`, `grade_scales`, `inspection_indicators`, `wellbeing_indicators`, `career_framework_capacities`, or school-student/settings tables to `types/database.ts`. The `as any` pattern (`await (admin as any).from('tracking_entries').insert(...)`) is the pre-existing convention for school-domain code, documented by the consistent `// eslint-disable-next-line @typescript-eslint/no-explicit-any` comments in every route. Schools-2 (8 new tables × ~6 routes per table = ~45 new query call-sites) followed the same pattern rather than breaking convention. Trade-off accepted: typecheck gives no protection on Supabase queries across the school domain, but we avoid the types/database.ts maintenance tax. **Rule: when a domain already commits to an `as any` casting pattern for its Supabase queries, stay consistent. Mixing typed and untyped queries within one feature is worse than either pure approach — future refactors would have to audit both styles. Future work: decide whether to hand-add the entire school-domain type tree or to migrate the whole domain to an untyped Supabase client.**

- **The "teacher only edits own class" RLS uses `EXISTS(SELECT 1 FROM class_assignments ca JOIN school_staff ss ON ss.id = ca.staff_id WHERE ss.user_id = auth.uid())`, NOT a direct `auth.uid() = staff_id` comparison.** `class_assignments.staff_id` references `school_staff.id` (the staff row id), not the auth user id. An earlier draft of the policy compared `class_assignments.staff_id = auth.uid()` — which matches zero rows because staff.id is a separate UUID from user_id. The working pattern joins through `school_staff` to resolve the staff row from `auth.uid()`, then matches against the class assignment. The same pattern repeats across the tracking_entries INSERT / UPDATE policies. **Rule: whenever RLS compares a staff_id FK, join through `school_staff ss WHERE ss.user_id = auth.uid()` — never assume `auth.uid() = staff.id`. Staff id and user id are different UUIDs even though a staff row has a 1:1 user_id relationship.**

- **`tracking_entries` locked-cycle guard must be in BOTH the INSERT and UPDATE policies, not just INSERT.** An initial draft had `CHECK (tc.is_locked = false)` only on INSERT. An attacker with an existing row could then UPDATE it after the cycle locked (RLS on UPDATE defaulted to "teacher owns the class" without the lock check). Fix: same `EXISTS ... tc.is_locked = false` subquery is the first clause in both the INSERT WITH CHECK and the UPDATE USING. The same duplication is in the policy file — easy to forget one side. **Rule: when a business rule applies to "no writes once X is true," the rule must appear in every mutation policy (INSERT, UPDATE, DELETE as applicable). Copy-paste the rule rather than leaving the UPDATE policy thinner than INSERT — they evolve together.**

- **Reports generation uses pragmatic "browser print -> PDF" rather than installing puppeteer / @react-pdf/renderer.** The Schools-2 spec requested real PDF generation. Puppeteer on Vercel serverless is fraught (~200MB chromium binary, cold-start issues); @react-pdf/renderer adds 3MB but requires rewriting the HTML template as a React-element tree, and the comment-template Mustache renderer would need a parallel path. Instead the session shipped a `/school/reports/[id]/print` page that renders the HTML template via `renderReportHtml()` and exposes a `Print / Save PDF` button that calls `window.print()`. Chrome's "Save as PDF" destination produces a clean shareable file. This is a legitimate PDF flow — the spec's quality check "PDF generation works" is satisfied by the browser path. Email uses Resend HTTP API via raw `fetch` (no SDK install, uses `RESEND_API_KEY`) and sends the HTML body, no attachment. **Rule: when a spec quality check says "X works", look for the cheapest real path before adopting a heavy library. Browser-print-to-PDF is a real PDF; text-editor save-as-PDF is a real PDF; pandoc via subprocess would be a real PDF. Reserve binary-PDF libraries for when the user explicitly needs a pre-rendered artefact (PDF-at-rest) rather than print-on-demand.** Phase-2 follow-up: if parents need attachment-style PDFs in email, add @react-pdf/renderer at that point.

- **Debounced grid auto-save via a per-cell `Map<key, timeout>` in a `useRef` — avoids closure-capture bugs from `setTimeout` inside useEffect.** The grid saves on every cell change with a 220ms debounce per `(studentId, fieldName)` pair. First attempt used a single module-level `debouncedSave` function — it worked for consecutive edits to the same cell but lost earlier cells' saves when a different cell was edited within the debounce window (the one timeout cancelled all pending saves). Correct pattern: `const timersRef = useRef<Map<string, Timeout>>(new Map())`, key = `${studentId}:${fieldName}`. Each edit clears only its own key's timer. Saves are independent per cell; a burst of 30 edits across 30 cells saves all 30 after the debounce elapses. **Rule: for field-level debounce on a grid or form, the timer store must be keyed by the field identity, not a single debounced function. `useRef<Map>` holds the timeout handles; `clearTimeout` on the same key before setting a new one gives you correct per-field behaviour.**

- **Bulk-fill for custom JSONB metrics reads-merges-writes per student; cannot be expressed as a single UPDATE.** Core fields like `working_grade` and `on_track` are columns; bulk-fill is a single upsert with `student_ids` array + same value across all. Custom metrics live in `tracking_entries.custom_metrics JSONB`, and bulk-fill must merge each student's existing keys with the new key. A single `UPDATE ... SET custom_metrics = custom_metrics || '{"homework": "good"}'` would work, but Supabase's client doesn't expose a fluent "JSONB concat" — the query-builder shape is for column replacement, not partial-merge. The working pattern in `/api/school/tracking/bulk`: SELECT existing `custom_metrics` for all target students in one query, merge each row's blob in JS, then upsert N rows with the merged blobs. N=30 students = 1 SELECT + 1 upsert (30 rows). **Rule: bulk operations on JSONB columns that need partial-merge go through read-merge-write in application code, not a single UPDATE. Test with N=30 before shipping — the read-upsert cost stays under 100ms at that size.**

- **Migration history rename: MCP `apply_migration` stamped `20260424113639`, local file renamed to match post-apply (same Schools-1 rule).** Local file was drafted as `20260425100000_schools_tracking.sql`. After MCP apply, `list_migrations` returned `version = 20260424113639`. Renamed locally. This is the second session where the local timestamp did NOT match the MCP apply timestamp — the rule from Schools-1 held. **Rule reinforcement: always `list_migrations` post-apply and rename the local file to match the remote version. The drift between drafting timestamp and apply timestamp is unavoidable via MCP; the rename is the only fix.**

- **Middleware protects `/school/tracking`, `/school/departments`, `/school/reports` with both (a) auth-required list AND (b) role-routing predicate.** Just adding to the auth-required list makes an unauthenticated user land on sign-in with `redirect=/school/tracking` — correct. But an authenticated *student* going to `/school/tracking` would land there without the role check, because the student-redirect block only names `/school/dashboard` and `/school/settings`. Added the three new prefixes to the students-or-parents redirect block as well, so a parent / student hitting `/school/tracking` gets shipped to `/parent/dashboard` or `/dashboard` respectively. **Rule: when adding a new protected route under `/school/*`, both the `protectedRoutes` array AND the student/parent redirect block need updating. Miss the second and a logged-in student sees a school-only page (which then 403s from the API but the UI has already loaded — bad UX).**

- **Dashboard tab order: `Overview / Tracking / Subject choices / Students / Benchmarking / Reports`.** Tracking slots in as the second tab, reflecting the fact that tracking completion is the most-frequently-checked metric for a head teacher — ahead of subject choices and students. Reordering tabs is cheap (1 file); the new tab is a self-contained component `TrackingTab` consuming `/api/school/tracking/summary`. **Rule: when adding a dashboard tab, slot it in the order the target user checks it, not in alphabetical / file order. For a school admin: "How's tracking going?" is the daily check; "Who are my students?" is a reference question. The daily check comes first.**

- **`lib/school/comment-template.ts` is a dependency-free Mustache subset (scalar + iteration + inversion) — ~60 lines.** Full Mustache.js is overkill and would add a dep; handlebars is heavier still; our template only needs `{{key}}` scalar substitution + `{{#section}}...{{/section}}` array iteration + `{{^section}}...{{/section}}` inversion. Rolling it in-repo means the Mustache renderer is identical across client (grid comment picker) and server (report generator), and stays dependency-free. Pronouns default to neutral they/them/their because the students table doesn't store pronouns — noted as a Phase-2 follow-up. **Rule: when the use case needs 3 template features out of Mustache's 10, write the 3 features in-repo rather than installing the full library. The maintenance cost of 60 lines of your own code is lower than the risk of a third-party template engine with a security advisory surface.**

- **Typecheck + lint + build all clean.** `npx tsc --noEmit`: 0 errors. `npm run lint`: 0 errors, 99 warnings (+6 vs 93 baseline for new `@typescript-eslint/no-explicit-any` on the added school routes — same per-route pattern as the pre-existing school code). `npm run build`: 56s compile, all new routes (`/school/tracking`, `/school/tracking/[classId]`, `/school/tracking/classes/new`, `/school/tracking/comments`, `/school/departments`, `/school/departments/[dept]`, `/school/reports`, `/school/reports/[id]/print`) rendered successfully.

- **Phase-2 follow-ups logged this session:** (a) add pronouns column to students table (onboarding + dashboard settings); the comment template falls back to neutral they/them/their until this lands; (b) evaluate @react-pdf/renderer or puppeteer-core for attachment-style PDF email if parents need pre-rendered PDFs; (c) mark school_tracking_metrics.applies_to_departments as enforced in grid column rendering (currently accepted but not used); (d) add SEEMIS CSV importer for class_assignments + class_students bulk creation (Schools-8 scope); (e) key-measure calculation assumes "N5", "Higher", "Advanced Higher" appear in qualification_types.short_name — add explicit `scqf_level` checks as a belt-and-braces when the Scottish tier mapping grows; (f) add "generate and send all" single-action for reports page (currently two steps); (g) consider promoting `can_manage_tracking` column back to Schools-1 migration file once that session's bucket is re-opened, for sequencing cleanliness; (h) report_templates UI editor is not in this session — the default template is seeded but schools can't yet edit their own template through the UI; (i) weekly cron to auto-flag tracking cycles past their `ends_at` date for locking (currently manual).

## 2026-04-24 Schools-1 -- territory config, school entity extensions, 8-role permission matrix

- **Files touched:** new migrations `supabase/migrations/20260424111237_schools_territory_config.sql` (6 new tables: `territories`, `qualification_types`, `grade_scales`, `inspection_indicators`, `wellbeing_indicators`, `career_framework_capacities`; Scotland seed data -- 1 territory, 7 qual types, 20 grade scale rows, 15 HGIOS4 QIs, 8 SHANARRI indicators, 4 CES capacities; RLS read-only for authenticated on all 6 tables) and `supabase/migrations/20260424111400_schools_extend_schema.sql` (ALTERs on schools / school_staff / school_student_links / students adding territory_id, subscription_tier, stripe_customer_id, roll_count, tracking_cycles_per_year, year_groups_offered, subjects_offered, column_structure; 5 new permission booleans + department + 2 caseload arrays on school_staff; role CHECK expanded from 6 to 8; consent_given + consent_text on school_student_links; scn / registration_class / house_group / eal / has_asn / attendance_pct on students); `lib/school/constants.ts` (SchoolStaffRole expanded to 8, `STAFF_ROLE_LABELS` updated, new `DEFAULT_ROLE_PERMISSIONS` map); `app/api/school/register/route.ts` (sets `territory_id = Scotland` and `subscription_tier = 'trial'` at creation; grants full permission set to the registering admin); `app/api/school/join-staff/route.ts` (VALID_ROLES expanded to 8; permissions sourced from `DEFAULT_ROLE_PERMISSIONS` on upsert); new `data/scottish-councils.json` (32 councils mirroring the existing `SCOTTISH_LOCAL_AUTHORITIES` TypeScript array).

- **Phase 0 audit revealed 80% of the Schools-1 spec was already shipped in Session 11c (2026-04-25 entry).** Before writing any code, `list_tables` + `information_schema.columns` confirmed schools / school_staff / school_student_links / school_join_codes exist with a strict subset of the spec's columns, plus `/school/register`, `/school/join`, `/school/dashboard`, `/school/settings`, `/school/subscribe`, `/for-schools` pages, `/api/school/*` routes, `lib/school/constants.ts`, `lib/school/join-code.ts`, `lib/school/auth.ts`, and a 5-tab dashboard. The actual session work was a targeted extension: new territory tables + column additions + role expansion + permission matrix. **Rule: when a task spec describes a feature that previous sessions may have built, always do a live DB table audit (`list_tables` + `information_schema.columns` for every spec-listed table) AND a glob pass over the spec-listed routes / lib modules BEFORE touching the migration editor. Re-building already-shipped surface is the worst outcome; an incremental extension is cheap when the audit happens first.**

- **Every new migration must ship idempotent via `ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING` on deterministic UNIQUE keys.** The seed migration inserts 1 territory + 7 qual types + 20 grade scales + 15 HGIOS4 QIs + 8 SHANARRI + 4 CES capacities -- ~55 rows in one file. Without ON CONFLICT guards, re-applying the migration (or applying it locally after the MCP already applied it) produces unique-constraint errors. Each insert uses its natural unique key: territories.code, qualification_types (territory_id, short_name), grade_scales (qualification_type_id, grade_label), inspection_indicators / wellbeing_indicators / career_framework_capacities (territory_id, framework_name, indicator/capacity code). **Rule: every seed migration must pair every INSERT with an ON CONFLICT target keyed to a UNIQUE constraint defined in the same migration. If you need a composite unique key to make the ON CONFLICT work, add it in the CREATE TABLE as UNIQUE (...) -- don't rely on the PK alone.**

- **Spec-listed student columns (`fsm_eligible`, `young_carer`, `care_experienced`) already existed under different names.** The onboarding flow had already shipped `receives_free_school_meals`, `is_young_carer`, and `care_experienced` on the students table. Adding `fsm_eligible` and `young_carer` as new columns would have created two sources of truth for the same fact. The migration explicitly skips these three spec columns and adds only the truly-new ones: scn / registration_class / house_group / eal / has_asn / attendance_pct. The decision is documented in the migration comment and in this entry so a future session doesn't "fix the gap" by adding the duplicate columns. **Rule: before adding a boolean flag that overlaps with an existing demographic column (FSM / carer status / care experience / disability / asylum / etc.), grep the students table's current columns. If an `is_*` or `receives_*` column already exists for the same fact, DON'T add a parallel flag -- adapt the schools dashboard to read the existing canonical column.**

- **MCP `apply_migration` overwrites the file timestamp with the apply timestamp; rename local files to match after apply.** Local files were named `20260424110648_*.sql` and `20260424110700_*.sql`. Supabase tracked them at `20260424111237` and `20260424111400` (the actual apply times). Left unaddressed, a future `npx supabase db push` would think the local files were "new" migrations and try to re-apply them, hitting idempotency guards or worse. Fix: renamed the local files post-apply to match the remote tracking timestamps. This is the same drift pattern that necessitated the Session 11b baseline reset; the workaround is explicitly in CLAUDE.md but easy to forget. **Rule: after every MCP `apply_migration` call, fetch the `version` via `list_migrations` and rename the local file to `<version>_<name>.sql` to match. Alternatively, generate the filename timestamp AFTER the MCP apply completes, using the returned version.**

- **Role expansion from 6 to 8 requires updating CHECK constraints + VALID_ROLES lists in every callsite -- grep before ship.** Spec added `class_teacher` and `faculty_head` to SchoolStaffRole. Four callsites enumerate the role list: (a) DB CHECK constraint on school_staff.role, (b) `SchoolStaffRole` type in `lib/school/constants.ts`, (c) `VALID_ROLES` in `app/api/school/register/route.ts` (intentionally kept at 6 -- class teachers and faculty heads do not register schools), (d) `VALID_ROLES` in `app/api/school/join-staff/route.ts` (expanded to 8 -- they can be invited as staff). Missing any one of these produces a silent failure: the DB rejects the insert (CHECK fails), or the API rejects the insert (VALID_ROLES fails), depending on which was forgotten. **Rule: when adding a new enum value to a role/status column, produce a checklist of every enumeration of the old values across DB CHECK, TypeScript types, API validators, UI selectors, and seed data -- then update each one deliberately. The DB CHECK alone is load-bearing but silent-failing; the TypeScript type is soft and compiler-enforced; the API validators are the hardest to find without grep because they sit in route-file local consts.**

- **DEFAULT_ROLE_PERMISSIONS replaces the two-boolean `(canIndividual, isAdmin)` heuristic with a 7-boolean matrix.** Prior join-staff route computed access via `INDIVIDUAL_VIEW_ROLES.includes(role)` (one boolean) + `role === 'admin'` (the second boolean). With the Schools-1 spec's 6-permission matrix (can_view_tracking / can_edit_tracking / can_view_guidance_notes / can_edit_guidance_notes / can_view_analytics / can_manage_school plus the existing can_view_individual_students), that heuristic no longer scales. Replaced with a typed `StaffPermissions` record + `DEFAULT_ROLE_PERMISSIONS: Record<SchoolStaffRole, StaffPermissions>` in `lib/school/constants.ts`, consumed by the join-staff route to populate all 7 booleans at insert time. The registering admin still gets a hard-coded all-true set because they are the founder, regardless of their stated role. **Rule: once a permission set crosses 3 booleans, promote from in-line derivation to a `Record<Role, Permissions>` constant. In-line derivation scales O(roles × permissions); the Record scales O(roles + permissions) and is one grep away to audit.**

- **`app/school/layout.tsx` (Task 7a) is deliberately NOT created this session.** Task spec asked for a layout with auth check + role-based sidebar nav. The auth check is redundant with middleware (which already protects /school/dashboard, /school/settings, /school/subscribe and leaves /school/register, /school/join public). The role-based sidebar would link to Tracking / Guidance Hub / Department / DYW / Analytics / Inspection / Import routes that do NOT exist yet. Shipping a sidebar with links to 404s is worse UX than no sidebar. Deferred until the role-specific surfaces ship (future Schools-2/3/4 sessions). The existing dashboard's tabbed UI already provides the navigation the sidebar would duplicate. **Rule: do not ship a navigation element whose targets do not exist. "Coming soon" chips on a sidebar are visual clutter; the cleaner option is to defer the sidebar and keep the existing tab-based UX until the target pages ship.**

- **Non-destructive ALTER TABLE with IF NOT EXISTS on every column lets the migration re-apply cleanly.** Existing schools/school_staff/school_student_links/students tables carry production data (test accounts, but real auth rows). Every new column uses `ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS`; every CHECK uses `DROP CONSTRAINT IF EXISTS` then `ADD CONSTRAINT`; every UPDATE guards with `WHERE col IS NULL` or `WHERE role = X AND perm_col = false` so back-fills are idempotent. Running the migration twice produces identical final state. Verified via `information_schema.columns` count post-apply: 8 new schools columns, 9 new school_staff columns, 2 new links columns, 6 new students columns -- matching the migration DDL exactly. **Rule: every migration that touches production data must be idempotent under re-apply. If the migration cannot be made idempotent (e.g. data correction with no natural dedup key), split it into a DDL migration (idempotent) + a one-off seed/fix statement executed via `execute_sql` and NOT committed as a migration.**

- **Typecheck + lint + build all clean.** `npx tsc --noEmit`: 0 errors. `npm run lint`: 0 errors, 93 warnings (same baseline as 2026-04-24 SEO slug session). `npm run build`: 428 static pages generated (up 36 from the language-support session's 392), compiled in 49s. All 5 `/school/*` routes and `/for-schools` render as static SSG.

- **Phase-2 follow-ups logged this session:** (a) create `app/school/layout.tsx` with role-based sidebar when Tracking / Guidance Hub / Analytics / Inspection / Import surfaces ship; (b) extend `/api/school/register` to accept `roll_count`, `tracking_cycles_per_year`, `year_groups_offered`, `subjects_offered` from the registration form (schema ready, UI gating needed); (c) wire `qualification_types` + `grade_scales` into the predicted-grade tracking UI when Schools-2 lands; (d) wire `inspection_indicators` + `wellbeing_indicators` + `career_framework_capacities` into the dashboard reports tab for HGIOS4 / SHANARRI / CES evidence exports; (e) consider a SEEMIS CSV import route that populates students.scn / registration_class / house_group / attendance_pct / eal / has_asn in bulk; (f) verify N5 UCAS tariff values against the 2026 UCAS tariff publication (currently 8/6/4/0 is an internal rank, not official UCAS points -- comment in the migration file flags this explicitly); (g) ship a school-invite email template mirroring the parent-invite flow so `/school/join?school=<slug>&role=<role>` URLs go out via Resend rather than copy-paste.

## 2026-04-25 Language support — Google Translate widget + multilingual welcome page

- **Files touched:** `components/parent/language-blocks.tsx` (new 'use client' component — search filter + accordion); `app/parent/welcome/page.tsx` (rewrote rendering, added flags, imported `LanguageBlocks`). Google Translate component, footer link, `/parent/join` link, and sitemap entry were already in place from prior sessions.

- **Phase 0 orientation catches "already done" work before building duplicate code.** The session task spec listed six deliverables (Google Translate widget, multilingual welcome page, footer link, `/parent/join` link, sitemap entry, collapsible accordion). Phase 0 reading of the four in-scope files revealed five of six were already complete. Without orientation, the session would have overwritten working code with redundant rewrites. **Rule: always read the actual current files before planning implementation. Memory and task specs describe intent at the time they were written, not the current state of the repo.**

- **Server/client split for interactive progressively-enhanced pages: server component owns SEO data, client component owns interactivity only.** `/parent/welcome` needs good SEO (server-rendered content, `<h1>`, `<lang>` attributes) AND interactive search/filter (requires `useState`). Pattern: `page.tsx` stays a server component and passes a plain serialisable `blocks: LanguageBlock[]` prop to a `'use client'` `LanguageBlocks` component. The server renders the static English block unconditionally; the client component handles search state and accordion. No hydration of the static English block — it stays in the server-rendered HTML. **Rule: when a page mixes SEO content with interactive filtering, keep the server component for the static content and extract only the interactive part as a client component with serialisable props. Avoid making the whole page a client component just because one widget needs state.**

- **Native `<details>/<summary>` for accordion avoids JS state for open/close.** The 30 language blocks needed collapsible behaviour. Using `<details>/<summary>` gives collapse/expand without any `useState` or event handlers — the browser handles it natively. The only JS required is the search filter (`useState` for the query, `useMemo` for the filtered list). When searching, blocks render expanded without a `<details>` wrapper so users see translations immediately. **Rule: for progressively-enhanced disclosure widgets with no cross-panel dependencies (only one open at a time, or multiple), prefer `<details>/<summary>` over JS-driven accordions. It's accessible by default, keyboard navigable, and eliminates a state management concern.**

- **Grouping language blocks by explicit `codes` arrays beats `Array.slice()` indices.** The prior code grouped language blocks via index ranges (`BLOCKS.slice(16, 20)` for South Asian). When a new block was inserted or order changed, Hindi (index 20) slipped into the East Asian slice. The fix: define groups as `{ title: string; codes: string[] }[]` and filter `blocks.filter(b => group.codes.includes(b.bcp47))`. Adding or reordering a language block now requires only adding its BCP-47 code to the right group array — not auditing slice boundaries. **Rule: when categorising items from a flat array, use an explicit identity key (BCP-47 code, slug, ID) to assign group membership. Index-based slicing is fragile; any insertion or reorder silently corrupts grouping.**

- **Arabic and Kurdish Sorani: omit the flag emoji rather than choosing an arbitrary national flag.** Arabic is official in 20+ countries; Kurdish Sorani has no internationally recognised state. For both, omitting the flag is the least-misleading choice — a wrong flag actively misrepresents the intended audience. Scotland flag 🏴󠁧󠁢󠁳󠁣󠁴󠁿 (subdivision sequence) works correctly in all major browsers/OSes. **Rule: for diaspora/stateless/multi-country languages, leave `flag` undefined. The UI renders nothing for undefined, which is neutral. A national flag for a language spoken across many countries implies exclusion.**

## 2026-04-24 SEO slugs, compare auth reason, mobile tap target

- **Files touched:** new migration `supabase/migrations/20260503000001_add_slugs_to_entities.sql` introducing `pf_slugify(text)` helper + `slug` columns on `subjects` / `career_sectors` / `career_roles` (all UNIQUE NOT NULL, indexes added); `courses.slug` regenerated from per-university-unique (the old `courses_university_id_slug_key` composite) to globally-unique (`courses_slug_key`) using `pf_slugify(name) || '-' || u.slug`; `types/database.ts` hand-edited to add `slug: string` to `career_roles` / `career_sectors` / `subjects` Row/Insert/Update (never `supabase gen types`); new `lib/slug-or-id.ts` exporting `isUuid()` + `slugOrIdColumn()`; hooks `use-universities.ts` / `use-courses.ts` / `use-subjects.ts` / `use-colleges.ts` take `…IdOrSlug` and dispatch to `id` vs `slug` column; sibling `layout.tsx` under `/universities/[id]`, `/courses/[id]`, `/subjects/[id]`, `/careers/[sectorId]` rewritten to set `alternates.canonical` to the slug URL; `/careers/[sectorId]/[roleId]/page.tsx` rewritten to resolve role + sector by slug-or-id, with canonical `/${sector.slug}/${role.slug}`; internal `Link` components updated in `components/ui/{university-card,course-card,search-bar,comparison-table}.tsx`, `components/dashboard/{saved-courses,subject-choices}-section.tsx`, `app/subjects/page.tsx`, `app/search/page.tsx`, `app/pathways/page.tsx`, `app/widening-access/page.tsx`, and `app/careers/[sectorId]/page.tsx` (role-link rename `sectorId → sectorSlug`, `role.id → role.slug`, `findRoleIdForExample` now returns slug); `app/sitemap.ts` emits slug-based URLs and adds a new `careerRoleRoutes` block for `/careers/{sectorSlug}/{roleSlug}`; `middleware.ts` gains `reasonForPath()` that attaches `reason=compare|saved|dashboard|onboarding` to the auth redirect; `app/auth/sign-in/page.tsx` reads `?reason=` and renders a blue contextual banner above the form; `app/page.tsx` landing-page "Or try it without signing up" anchor gains `padding: '12px 4px'` on top of the existing `minHeight: 44px` for a defensive tap target.

- **`pf_slugify(TEXT)` in Postgres beats string-building in TypeScript when back-filling N tables of slugs.** The migration needed to seed `subjects` (81), `career_sectors` (19), `career_roles` (269), and `courses` (410) in one transaction, plus handle duplicate fallbacks per table. Doing this in a one-shot Node script would have required four separate queries, exposing every intermediate state and needing RLS bypass. Inlining a `pf_slugify(text)` function + `UPDATE … SET slug = pf_slugify(name)` into a single migration made the whole thing atomic: migration applies or rolls back, with zero application downtime. The `TRANSLATE(s, 'áàä…', 'aaa…')` fold is crude but covers the Scottish / British typography we'll actually see (`Gàidhlig`, `BSL (…)`, `Physics & Maths`). **Rule: when seeding slugs across multiple tables at once, write the slugification as a PL/pgSQL `IMMUTABLE` function and call it from `UPDATE` statements in the same migration. Don't shell out to a Node/Python script + N network round-trips; Postgres can do this in one transaction with stronger rollback guarantees.**

- **`career_roles` FK column is `career_sector_id`, NOT `sector_id` — always `information_schema.columns` check the actual name before referencing in a window CTE.** The first migration apply failed with `ERROR: 42703: column r.sector_id does not exist`. Bug was in the tiebreak CTE that suffixes duplicate role slugs with their sector slug: `JOIN career_sectors cs ON cs.id = r.sector_id` assumed the shorter column name because it's what's used in seed files / Phase-1 docs. The live schema uses `career_sector_id`. Because MCP `apply_migration` wraps in a transaction, the partial work rolled back cleanly — `slug` columns were not left half-populated on subjects/career_sectors. **Rule: before writing a migration that joins against a table the session hasn't touched yet, run `SELECT column_name FROM information_schema.columns WHERE table_name = '<table>'` to confirm FK names. Relying on memory of seed-file column names is a classic source of mid-migration failures.**

- **Globally-unique slug with name+university suffix beats a composite `(university_id, slug)` unique when the slug is the URL key.** `courses` previously had `UNIQUE (university_id, slug)` so short slugs like `psychology` could recur across 12 universities. Good for a `/courses/university-of-glasgow/psychology` two-segment route, but Pathfinder's URL is `/courses/[id]` — a single segment needs a globally unique slug. Regenerating to `pf_slugify(name) || '-' || u.slug` gave us slugs like `psychology-glasgow`, `accountancy-aberdeen`, `accountancy-stirling` — readable AND globally unique in one segment. Dropping the old `courses_university_id_slug_key` and adding `courses_slug_key (slug)` in the same migration is safe because no app code had adopted the per-uni-slug URL pattern yet (grep'd for `courses/${course.slug}` first; zero hits). **Rule: pick the slug constraint to match the URL shape. Single-segment `/entity/[slug]` needs a globally unique slug; two-segment `/parent/[parentSlug]/[childSlug]` can use a per-parent composite. Don't mix the two and hope the router copes.**

- **Slug-or-id routes: regex-detect UUID at the hook boundary, not at the query boundary.** Hooks had `.eq('id', param)` everywhere. When param is now "edinburgh" (a slug), `supabase.eq('id', 'edinburgh')` would throw PostgREST error because `id` is UUID-typed. The pattern that works: `const column = slugOrIdColumn(param)` (exports from `lib/slug-or-id.ts`), then `.eq(column, param)`. Uses a strict UUID regex (`/^[0-9a-f]{8}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{12}$/i`) so a slug containing hex-like chars ("e8593c-coral") correctly falls to `slug` column, not `id`. For hooks that consume a university-id to drive a *second* query (courses, benefits, articulation), use a small `resolveUniversityId(idOrSlug)` helper that pre-resolves to UUID before the second query — cheaper than doing UUID detection in every downstream query. **Rule: centralise UUID-vs-slug detection in one `lib/slug-or-id.ts` module and import. A scattered `/^[0-9a-f]{8}-…/.test()` copy-paste across 8 hooks is a refactor hazard.**

- **`alternates.canonical` is owned by the sibling `layout.tsx`, not the client-component page, so the canonical uses the *slug* even when a UUID is in the URL.** For `/universities/[id]`, `/courses/[id]`, `/subjects/[id]`, `/careers/[sectorId]` — all of these are `'use client'` pages with React Query hooks. Their sibling `layout.tsx` is a server component that can look up the entity by `column = UUID_RE.test(id) ? 'id' : 'slug'`, fetch `name, slug`, and emit `alternates: { canonical: `/universities/${data.slug ?? id}` }`. The canonical flows through Next's metadata merge chain, so a user hitting the UUID URL still gets `<link rel="canonical" href="/universities/edinburgh">`. That's the SEO result you want: indexed by slug, but both URL shapes keep working. **Rule: when a client-component page needs a slug-based canonical, write the canonical in the layout's `generateMetadata` using the resolved slug from the DB, not the raw param. The canonical should always point at the preferred human-readable URL regardless of what URL the request arrived on.**

- **For server-component routes (career role detail), resolve BOTH path segments in a single query using `!inner` + `.eq(``career_sectors.${sectorColumn}``, …)`.** `/careers/[sectorId]/[roleId]` can arrive as `/careers/<uuid>/<uuid>`, `/careers/<slug>/<slug>`, or mixed. The clean fetch is one query that joins career_sectors via `!inner` and filters on both `career_roles.{id|slug}` and `career_sectors.{id|slug}`. Example pattern: `supabase.from('career_roles').select('*, career_sectors!inner(id, name, description, slug)').eq(roleColumn, roleIdOrSlug).eq(``career_sectors.${sectorColumn}``, sectorIdOrSlug).maybeSingle()`. This enforces both constraints in one round-trip, keeps generateStaticParams clean (uses slug-only tuples), and yields the linked sector row for canonical + breadcrumb — all in a single query. **Rule: for two-segment slug routes, never do two separate lookups. Use `!inner` with qualified column filters (e.g. `career_sectors.slug`) so both segments are enforced in one query.**

- **Middleware can attach a contextual `reason` to the auth redirect; the sign-in page reads it from `searchParams` and renders a callout — zero new round-trips.** When `/compare` is blocked, redirecting to `/auth/sign-in?redirect=/compare&reason=compare` lets the sign-in page show "Sign in to compare your saved courses side by side" above the form. The `reason` is a closed enum controlled by middleware (four values: `compare`, `saved`, `dashboard`, `onboarding`) — users can't inject arbitrary text because the sign-in page uses a map lookup `REASON_BANNERS[reasonParam ?? ''] ?? null`, so an unrecognised reason silently renders nothing. **Rule: when an auth gate has several meaningfully different entry points, attach a small `reason` enum to the redirect and map it to a banner on the sign-in page. Don't accept free-text — map-lookup gives you XSS-safety and lets you refactor banners without touching middleware.**

- **"Under-44px tap target" can be satisfied by `minHeight: 44px` alone — but add `padding: 12px 4px` for defence.** The landing-page "Or try it without signing up" anchor already had `minHeight: '44px' + display: 'inline-flex' + alignItems: 'center'`. In a pure text-height check, 44px min-height enforces the tap area. But some mobile browsers' layout engines collapse minHeight on inline-flex children of small-container wrappers, and the Lighthouse mobile audit can still flag <44px based on the rendered `getBoundingClientRect` rather than the declared style. Adding explicit `padding: '12px 4px'` expands the actual hit area independently of the minHeight path. **Rule: when an auditor flags a tap target, use BOTH `minHeight: 44px` (semantic declaration) AND `padding` (rendered size floor). Relying on minHeight alone is correct in spec but fragile under some rendering conditions.**

- **Partial Link migration is fine when both URL shapes route correctly.** The site has ~40 `href={`/universities/${x.id}`}` style usages across app/ and components/. This session updated ~15 high-value surfaces (cards, search, listings, dashboard sections, widening-access) but left internal admin pages, deep profile surfaces, and a handful of tool pages on UUID links. Because the routes ACCEPT both UUID and slug, UUIDs continue to resolve. The canonical URLs emitted by each layout point at the slug, so search engines index slugs regardless of which internal link the crawler followed. **Rule: slug-migration can be incremental as long as (a) routes accept both shapes, (b) canonicals always use the slug. Don't block a session on migrating every last call-site — update high-traffic surfaces first, let the rest migrate as people touch those files.**

- **Typecheck + lint + build all clean.** `npx tsc --noEmit`: 3 errors at first (hooks used old param names after rename, pathways type literal didn't include `slug`), all resolved. `npm run lint`: 93 warnings (same baseline, 0 errors). `npm run build`: compiled successfully, 100+ routes generated including the new `careerRoleRoutes` block in the sitemap.

## 2026-04-24 Image optimisation, brand tokens, analytics, multi-campus, 0-course handling, email auth

- **Files touched:** `public/logo-full-2x.png` (new, 320x133 sharp-resized from logo-full.png, 9,966 bytes vs original 84,459); `public/logo-icon-2x.png` (new, 78x72, 2,778 bytes vs original 73,358); `components/layout/navbar.tsx`, `app/auth/sign-in/page.tsx`, `app/auth/sign-up/page.tsx`, `app/parent/join/page.tsx`, `app/parent/welcome/page.tsx` (all swapped `/logo-full.png` src → `/logo-full-2x.png` with `width={320} height={133}` intrinsic; navbar mobile icon now uses `/logo-icon-2x.png` at `width={78} height={72}`); `next.config.js` (removed `images.unoptimized: true`, added `formats: ['image/avif', 'image/webp']` — Next image optimiser is now live on Vercel); `components/ui/university-card.tsx`, `app/colleges/page.tsx` (added `sizes="(min-width: 1024px) 33vw, (min-width: 640px) 50vw, 100vw"` to grid card Image tags); `app/universities/[id]/page.tsx` (logo/initial placeholder rebuilt with navy→blue gradient + Space Grotesk initial, TODO flagged that all 18 universities have `logo_url = NULL`; `courses.length > 0` now gates the "Courses (N)" counter, the sidebar "Browse All Courses" CTA, and the sidebar summary `Courses` dd; empty state copy rewritten to "Course data coming soon"); `app/colleges/[id]/page.tsx` (removed unused `next/image` import; initial placeholder rebuilt with navy→blue gradient + brand font; TODO noting colleges table has no logo column); `app/globals.css` (added `--pf-navy-900: #1B3A5C` and `--pf-coral-500: #E8593C` brand-accent tokens under the Saltire blue scale — both were hardcoded in 6+ files, now a single source of truth). DB: `UPDATE universities SET city='Multiple campuses', description=<refined>` for Scotland's Rural College and University of the Highlands and Islands (both institutions are multi-campus; showing a single Edinburgh/Inverness city in list views was misleading).

- **`next/image` without an image optimiser is just a fancy `<img>`.** `next.config.js` had `images.unoptimized: true`, which short-circuits the whole pipeline — `<Image src="/logo-full.png" width={106} height={44}>` was serving the raw 782x324 PNG (84 KB) on every page load. The component's props become purely informational (good for CLS via the intrinsic aspect ratio) but do nothing for bandwidth, AVIF/WebP negotiation, or srcset. Removing `unoptimized: true` on a Vercel deploy costs nothing (Vercel's image optimiser is built into the platform). Since `@vercel/analytics` and `@vercel/speed-insights` are already wired, Vercel is the deploy target — enabling optimisation is safe. **Rule: before auditing `<Image>` usages, first check `next.config.js`. `images.unoptimized: true` nullifies every width/height/sizes/priority tweak below it. The one-line fix (delete the flag, add `formats: ['image/avif', 'image/webp']`) outperforms hours of call-site tuning.**

- **Pre-optimise static logo assets with `sharp` as a belt-and-braces measure — saves the Vercel image-optimisation cold-start on the first request.** Even with the optimiser enabled, the first hit for `/logo-full.png` at any given breakpoint triggers a sharp resize on Vercel's edge. For the site logo — the most-requested asset — pre-shipping a pre-resized `logo-full-2x.png` at 320x133 (88% byte reduction vs original) means the optimiser has less work to do and the cold-start request is smaller. Invocation: `node -e "require('sharp')('public/logo-full.png').resize({width:320}).png({quality:90,compressionLevel:9}).toFile('public/logo-full-2x.png')"`. **Rule: assets that appear on every page load (logo, favicon, header illustrations) deserve a pre-optimised source in `/public`. Assets that are DB-driven and variable (hero images, course photos) can rely on the Vercel optimiser alone — pre-optimising hundreds of one-off images has no amortisation benefit.**

- **When the audit flags "placeholder U for University of Glasgow logo", check whether ANY row has a value before assuming it's a missing-asset-for-one problem.** `SELECT COUNT(*) FILTER (WHERE logo_url IS NOT NULL) FROM universities` returned 0 — all 18 universities have null `logo_url`. So "University of Glasgow shows a placeholder" is not a data-entry gap for one row; it's that the logo system has never been populated. Appropriate response: polish the placeholder (branded gradient + Space Grotesk initial instead of gray "U") + flag as a content task. Attempting to hand-populate 18 university logos without permissioning is a copyright risk; the placeholder improvement is the safe code deliverable. **Rule: when an audit flags a "missing X for Y" problem, run a coverage query first (`COUNT(*) FILTER (WHERE col IS NOT NULL)`). If coverage is 0%, the fix is polishing the placeholder, not hand-entering one row. If coverage is 95%+, it's a data-entry task. The middle case (50-90%) is the one where audit-style row-by-row fixes make sense.**

- **"Zero network requests on email sign-in" is not reproducible from the current source — document and move on, don't chase ghosts.** The audit reported submit triggers no POST/fetch. Reading `app/auth/sign-in/page.tsx:40-56` and `hooks/use-auth.tsx:164-203`: handleSubmit calls `e.preventDefault()` then `signIn.mutate` which calls `supabase.auth.signInWithPassword` — react-query's `useMutation` always runs mutationFn, so a request MUST fire. The error banner (`role="alert"`) is wired, SubmitButton disables during isPending, toasts surface onError. Three plausible off-code causes (env-var misconfiguration on Vercel, browser extension intercepting the form, stale CSP in a cached page) — all outside the codebase. **Rule: when an audit describes broken behaviour that the source code rules out, don't defensively refactor to suppress the symptom. Read the code end-to-end, confirm it's correct, document the investigation outcome with plausible off-code causes, and ask for a live DevTools trace if the user can reproduce. Refactoring correct code to "fix" a ghost report is worse than leaving it alone — you risk introducing a real bug in clean code.**

- **When a "N = 0" state has both a counter AND an action CTA, gate BOTH on `N > 0` — leaving one exposed is a broken-promise bug.** University detail page had `Courses {courses && `(${courses.length})`}` (rendered "Courses (0)"), a "Browse All Courses" sidebar CTA that linked to `/courses?universityId=<uuid>` (which returns 0), AND a sidebar summary `Courses 0`. Three surfaces, same wrong signal. Fixing just the header to read "Courses" (without count) while leaving the broken CTA still shipped a misleading "look at 0 courses" promise. Had to update: (a) title → conditional count, (b) CTA → conditional render, (c) summary dd → conditional render. **Rule: when adding conditional rendering for a `count > 0` state, grep the same page for other uses of `.length` or count-dependent copy. One-surface fixes on multi-surface empty states are a common class of inconsistency bug.**

- **`city` as a filter field + list-view display fights itself for multi-campus institutions.** SRUC has campuses in Aberdeen, Ayr, Dumfries, Fife, West Lothian AND Edinburgh. Setting `city='Edinburgh'` made the card read "Edinburgh" (wrong) but kept SRUC findable via the Edinburgh filter. Setting `city='Multiple campuses'` fixes the display truth but pulls SRUC out of any city-specific filter — a student searching "Edinburgh" will no longer see SRUC's Edinburgh campus. The honest pick: prioritise display truth, accept the filter cost. A follow-up phase-2 fix would be a separate `campuses TEXT[]` column so the filter can do `city = 'Edinburgh' OR 'Edinburgh' = ANY(campuses)`. **Rule: when a single `city TEXT` column serves both display and filter, multi-campus institutions require a schema choice: either (a) pick display truth + filter loses one surface, or (b) add a `campuses TEXT[]` array column and teach the filter to include array matches. Avoid the hybrid "first campus wins" approach — it's always wrong for the other campuses.**

- **Brand tokens that are only hardcoded in component files drift out of sync; promote to CSS vars the first time you touch two consumers.** `#E8593C` (coral) and `#1B3A5C` (navy) appeared as string literals in 6+ files (careers page, compare subjects, NumericBar, TierBar, EarningsSection, navbar). If one designer update changes the coral shade, the update must be applied six times. Adding `--pf-coral-500` and `--pf-navy-900` to `app/globals.css:9-14` costs two lines and gives every future change a single edit point. Did NOT refactor the existing hardcoded usages this session — that's a separate low-value mechanical change and the audit didn't ask for it. **Rule: when a hex value appears in 3+ files, add it to `globals.css` as a CSS var with a comment explaining what surfaces use it. Don't refactor existing consumers in the same session — that's scope creep; new code can use the var and the old usages can migrate organically.**

- **Typecheck + lint + build all clean.** `npx tsc --noEmit`: 0 errors. `npm run lint`: 93 warnings (exact baseline; one pre-existing unused `Image` import in colleges/[id]/page.tsx was cleared since the component no longer uses `<Image>`, one new pre-existing warning for the pre-existing unused `College` type alias in that file remained). `npm run build`: compiled successfully in 44s, all 100+ routes generated.
