## 2026-04-23 Dashboard settings -- postcode editing, email preferences, subject choice editing, funding profile fix, menu cleanup

- **Files touched:** `app/(main)/dashboard/settings/page.tsx` (new `PostcodeSection` that reuses `onboardingPostcodeLookupAction`, persists `postcode` / `simd_decile` / `local_authority` via `useUpdateStudent`; new `EmailPreferencesSection` with three toggles backed by `students.email_preferences` JSONB; helper note + `/bursaries` link beneath the funding-profile CTA; `useEffect`, `useTransition`, and `Link` imports added); `components/dashboard/subject-choices-section.tsx` (added per-subject remove buttons on the active transition only, plus a dynamic "GOING INTO S{n+1}" pill derived from `student.school_stage`; new `useSaveSubjectChoices` + `useCurrentStudent` + `useToast` imports); `components/auth/user-menu.tsx` (merged duplicate "Profile" + "Account Settings" menu items into a single "Settings" entry pointing at `/dashboard/settings`); `types/database.ts` (manually added `email_preferences: Json | null` to `students` Row/Insert/Update — never regenerate wholesale); new migration `supabase/migrations/20260502000001_add_email_preferences_to_students.sql` adds `email_preferences JSONB` with defaults for the three keys.

- **Reuse `onboardingPostcodeLookupAction` for the settings postcode editor — it already handles the "missing SIMD" + postcodes.io fallback path.** Rather than writing a second lookup action, the settings `PostcodeSection` imports the same `app/actions/onboarding-postcode-lookup.ts` server action and consumes its `OnboardingPostcodeResult` union. The `ok` branch persists all three derived fields (postcode / simd_decile / local_authority); the `missing_simd` branch still saves the postcode but clears SIMD (so widening access can be reassessed once the seed refreshes); any other status surfaces the inline error "We couldn't find this postcode in our database. Please check and try again." **Rule: when building a settings-page equivalent of an onboarding step, always check whether the onboarding flow's server action is reusable before writing a parallel one. Server actions written as pure functions of their input (not tied to onboarding-specific session state) are the easy win — the postcode lookup is the template.**

- **`email_preferences JSONB` with a full-object default is simpler than three separate boolean columns for GDPR opt-out UIs.** Adding `email_preferences JSONB DEFAULT '{"results_day_reminders": true, "platform_updates": true, "tips_and_guidance": true}'::jsonb` lets the UI toggle individual keys via a single column update. The alternative (three boolean columns: `email_results_day_reminders`, `email_platform_updates`, `email_tips_and_guidance`) would balloon the `students` Row type by three and require three migrations next time a new email category is added. The JSONB approach reads each key with a defensive `typeof r.xxx === 'boolean' ? r.xxx : DEFAULT` guard in a `readPrefs()` helper so rows where the column is NULL or malformed still render correctly. **Rule: for "N independent opt-in toggles" storage, prefer a single JSONB column with defaults over N boolean columns. Adding a fourth toggle later is a UI-only change; boolean-per-column requires a migration each time.**

- **Per-subject remove buttons on the dashboard should only appear for the student's active transition.** The subject-choices card lists every saved choice grouped by transition (s2→s3, s3→s4, s4→s5, s5→s6). Letting a student remove a historical s2→s3 choice would rewrite their past planning — more confusing than useful. Gating the remove button behind `STAGE_TO_ACTIVE_TRANSITION[student.school_stage] === t.value` means the current upcoming transition (e.g. a current-S4 student sees s4→s5 remove buttons, not s3→s4) is the only editable row. Add flow still uses `/pathways` — the dashboard remove is a lightweight un-pick, not a full editor. **Rule: when exposing inline edit/remove controls over historical data, gate them to the current-active record. Past records are reference, not editable surface — editing them silently corrupts the user's planning history.**

- **Dynamic "GOING INTO S{n+1}" pill uses the school_stage → transition map; S6/college/mature gets a "Senior Phase" pill with no suffix.** Hardcoded "GOING INTO S4" on the card was wrong for any student not entering S4 next. A `STAGE_TO_NEXT_LABEL` map handles s2/s3/s4/s5 → the matching "Going into Sn+1" text, plus an explicit `s6 → 'Senior Phase'` entry. College/mature returns no label (the map lookup is `??` null so the span is suppressed). **Rule: any stage-derived label on the dashboard should lookup through a `Record<stage, label>` map, never hard-code. The dashboard is the one surface where every student's stage is visible at once — hardcoded labels alienate whichever stages they don't match.**

- **Type-generated `database.ts` needed a manual `email_preferences: Json | null` addition on `students`; never regenerate wholesale (per `feedback_types_regen.md`).** The app already uses the pattern where `types/database.ts` is hand-edited when a column is added. I added the new key to Row, Insert, and Update in that order, using the existing `Json` export at the top of the file. Running `supabase gen types` against this project would drop 13 tables and 8 functions that were manually added previously — so edits continue to be manual. Typecheck stayed clean because the new JSONB column's value type (`Record<string, boolean>`) is compatible with `Json` at the `UpdateTables<'students'>` boundary. **Rule: when adding a JSONB column to a table whose Row/Insert/Update is already hand-maintained in database.ts, add the field in all three shapes and reuse the file's existing `Json` alias. Don't introduce a narrower type at the DB boundary — the UI can cast to its own shape (`EmailPrefs`) via a `readPrefs()` guard on read.**

- **`/grades` already had a permanent redirect to `/dashboard` from an earlier session; the user-menu "Profile" + "Account Settings" duplication was the only menu fix needed.** Confirmed `next.config.js:98-101` has the redirect. Both "Profile" (href `/dashboard/settings`) and "Account Settings" (href `/dashboard/settings`) in `components/auth/user-menu.tsx` pointed to the same page; merged to a single "Settings" entry with the cog icon (kept) and dropped the person-silhouette icon (was the Profile entry). Mobile nav doesn't surface Profile/Settings separately (it has the nav groups + dashboard link + sign-out), so no mobile edit was needed. **Rule: before adding a redirect as a QA fix, grep `next.config.js` for `source: '/<path>'` — the redirect may already exist from an earlier session. Duplicate redirects don't break but they do clutter the config diff.**

- **Career interests editing deferred — no `student_career_interests` table or `students.career_interests` column exists.** Confirmed via `information_schema.columns WHERE column_name ILIKE '%career%' OR '%interest%' AND table_schema='public'`: only `career_role_subjects`, `career_roles`, `riasec_career_mapping.example_careers`, `role_profiles.career_progression`, and `subject_career_sectors` turned up — all non-student tables. Onboarding captures `care_experienced`, `is_carer`, and `first_generation` but not career interests. Logged as an inline TODO in `dashboard/settings/page.tsx` noting that the quiz-results flow is the right place to surface this when storage lands. **Rule: before building a settings edit surface for user preference data, confirm storage exists via `information_schema`. If the spec asks you to edit data that isn't stored, log a TODO and move on — don't guess at where the data "should" live.**

- **Typecheck + lint clean.** `npx tsc --noEmit`: 0 errors. `npm run lint`: 93 warnings (same baseline as the 2026-04-23 Accessibility session).

## 2026-04-23 Accessibility, content gaps, data fixes -- page titles, nav aria, password checklist, GBP->£, career placeholders, RMPS copy

- **Files touched:** `app/search/layout.tsx` (new, static metadata with `title: 'Search'` + `alternates.canonical: '/search'`); `app/(main)/dashboard/layout.tsx` (new, static metadata `title: 'Dashboard'`); `app/courses/[id]/layout.tsx`, `app/universities/[id]/layout.tsx`, `app/colleges/[id]/layout.tsx`, `app/subjects/[id]/layout.tsx`, `app/careers/[sectorId]/layout.tsx` (all new, each `generateMetadata({params})` server helper that calls `getAnonSupabase()` and returns the entity's name as `title` plus a relative `alternates.canonical`); `app/careers/[sectorId]/[roleId]/page.tsx` (existing `generateMetadata` changed from ``${role.title} | ${sector.name}`` to just `role.title`; unused `sector` local removed to clear lint); `app/search/page.tsx` (added `aria-label="Search Pathfinder Scotland"` to the search `<input>`); `components/layout/navbar.tsx` (both desktop + mobile dropdown triggers now emit `aria-haspopup="menu"` + `aria-controls={dropdownId}` with a slug-derived id; matching `id={dropdownId}` added to each expanded panel); `app/auth/sign-up/page.tsx` (validation refactored: `validatePassword` returning first-match string replaced with `collectValidationErrors(): string[]` that accumulates unmet-rules summary + mismatch + unaccepted-terms; error box renders `<ul>` when >1 error; new visible `<ul aria-label="Password requirements">` checklist below the password field with 4 rules + tick/circle SVG indicators + `.sr-only` prefix so screen readers hear "Met:" / "Not yet met:"); `app/careers/[sectorId]/page.tsx` (27 new `JOB_BLURBS` entries for Retail & Customer Service, Transport & Logistics, and Armed Forces example cards; two TODO comments added above `<AiFutureSection>` and `<CareerRealities>` noting the Armed Forces data gaps). DB: `UPDATE career_sectors SET salary_range_entry/experienced = REPLACE(val, 'GBP ', '£')` applied to all 18 populated sectors; `UPDATE subjects SET why_choose = REPLACE(why_choose, OLD_RMPS_TEXT, NEW_RMPS_TEXT)` applied to the single RMPS row.

- **`layout.tsx` is the cleanest way to give a client-component page a dynamic `<title>`.** Pages like `/courses/[id]`, `/universities/[id]`, `/subjects/[id]` are all `'use client'` components using `useQuery` hooks. Converting them to server components just to export `generateMetadata` would ripple through every hook and component they use. Instead, a sibling `layout.tsx` at the same segment (which IS a server component by default) owns the metadata via its own `generateMetadata({params})`. Next.js merges metadata from the layout into the child page's response head automatically — deepest-segment fields win, so a layout's `title` flows through unless the page overrides it. **Rule: for client-component dynamic pages that need a DB-driven `<title>`, add a sibling `layout.tsx` with an async `generateMetadata({params})` that pre-fetches the minimum fields via `getAnonSupabase()`. Do not convert the page itself to a server component just for metadata.**

- **Strip brand-suffix from `layout.tsx` `title` too — the root `title.template` wraps it regardless of which segment set the title.** The root layout declares `title: { template: '%s | Pathfinder Scotland' }`. A child layout/page returning `title: 'Healthcare & Medicine Careers'` renders `"Healthcare & Medicine Careers | Pathfinder Scotland"` — the template applies at every depth. Returning `${role.title} | ${sector.name}` as the child title would produce `"Doctor / GP | Healthcare & Medicine | Pathfinder Scotland"` (bad). The fix for the role detail was to drop the sector from `generateMetadata` (returning just `role.title`) and let the template do its job. **Rule: when a child layout/page sets `title`, the root template wraps it once. Do not hand-concatenate the brand or a parent segment in the child — that double-wraps. Keep each segment's title to the leaf value only.**

- **`aria-haspopup="menu"` (not `"true"`) is the correct value when the popup is semantically a menu.** The task spec said "menu or true", but `aria-haspopup` accepts a role-like string: `menu`, `listbox`, `tree`, `grid`, `dialog`, or `true` (which defaults to `menu`). Since the panel already has `role="menu"` and each item has `role="menuitem"`, `aria-haspopup="menu"` is the most specific + consistent value. Screen readers announce "has menu" rather than the generic "has popup", which matches the user's mental model when Tab moves into the dropdown. **Rule: when a dropdown panel is `role="menu"`, its trigger should carry `aria-haspopup="menu"`, not `"true"` — match the value to the panel's role.**

- **`aria-controls` needs the dropdown's own `id` set in the same render.** A common mistake is adding `aria-controls="foo"` to the button without ever rendering an element with `id="foo"`, which silently does nothing (browsers don't warn). Building the id as `nav-dropdown-${group.name.toLowerCase().replace(/\s+/g, '-')}` gave a stable per-group id that I set on both the button's `aria-controls` and the expanded panel's `id` in the same map iteration. Mobile got its own id namespace (`nav-mobile-dropdown-…`) to avoid a collision when both layouts are in the DOM simultaneously (desktop is hidden via CSS, not unmounted). **Rule: every `aria-controls` attribute must have a matching `id` on an element currently in the DOM. When the same component has desktop + mobile variants that may both render, namespace the ids to prevent collisions; CSS `display:none` does not remove ids from the accessibility tree.**

- **Password rules checklist belongs BELOW the strength meter, not in place of it.** The strength meter measures security ("Very Weak → Strong" based on diversity of char classes); the rules checklist tracks policy compliance ("at least 8 chars, upper, lower, number"). They answer different questions: strength is "how safe is this password", rules are "will the submit button let me through". Showing both serves both questions at the cost of ~40px of vertical space. **Rule: keep the strength meter and rules checklist as separate UI elements. A password that meets all 4 rules can still be "Fair" strength (e.g. `Password1`), and a password can be "Strong" without meeting all 4 rules (e.g. `!!!pinkelephant!!!`). Conflating them hides information either way.**

- **Form-validation redesign: return `string[]` not `string | null` when you need simultaneous display of multiple errors.** The original `validatePassword` returned the first violating rule's message, and `handleSubmit` called it then fell through to `password !== confirmPassword` then `!acceptTerms` with early returns — each later error was only reachable once the earlier one was fixed. Refactored to `collectValidationErrors(): string[]` that builds up all violations in one pass, then the render conditionally shows a single `<span>` for one error or a `<ul>` for several. The terms-unaccepted case now surfaces alongside a password error so the student can fix both in one iteration. **Rule: for multi-field form validation, always collect errors into an array and render all on submit. Early-return validators train the user to fix errors serially; collecting-then-rendering trains them to scan the form once.**

- **Salary-format "GBP 25,000" in a DB column needs a data-level UPDATE, not a display-layer formatter.** The `career_sectors.salary_range_entry` column stored the literal string "GBP 25,000 - GBP 32,000" — which renders as given. Adding a UK-ified formatter (`replace(/GBP /g, '£')`) in `app/careers/page.tsx` and `[sectorId]/page.tsx` would have hidden the ugliness at render time without fixing the underlying data. The right call is the data fix: `UPDATE career_sectors SET salary_range_entry = REPLACE(salary_range_entry, 'GBP ', '£')` — now every consumer of that column (current pages, future analytics, future exports) gets the correct £ symbol. **Rule: when a display bug is caused by the literal string stored in a DB column, prefer a one-shot `UPDATE ... REPLACE(col, OLD, NEW)` over a display-layer formatter. Formatters accumulate; data corrections are one-and-done.**

- **A "Works within this career sector." placeholder on an example-job card is a hardcoded-map fallback, not a DB gap.** The first instinct was to look for `career_roles.description` — which doesn't exist (the column lives on `role_profiles.description`). The actual source was `JOB_BLURBS: Record<string, string>` in `app/careers/[sectorId]/page.tsx` — a static map keyed by exact example_job title, with `getJobBlurb(title) → JOB_BLURBS[title] || 'Works within this career sector.'`. Adding 27 new entries for Retail, Transport, and Armed Forces example jobs eliminated the placeholder render without any DB migration. **Rule: before writing a SQL UPDATE to fix a "generic description" bug, grep the codebase for the placeholder string first. A surprising amount of static copy lives in typed lookup maps rather than the DB, and the fix is a hand-edit not a migration.**

- **`example_jobs` is a denormalised `text[]` on `career_sectors` — titles don't auto-match `career_roles.title`.** The Armed Forces sector's `example_jobs` array has `'RAF Airman / Airwoman'` (with spaces around `/`), while the `career_roles.title` values for the same role would typically be `'RAF Airman/Airwoman'` (no spaces). Writing JOB_BLURBS keyed by the task-spec form (no spaces) created a silent miss: the card rendered the placeholder because `JOB_BLURBS['RAF Airman / Airwoman']` was undefined. Caught by running `SELECT name, example_jobs FROM career_sectors WHERE name ILIKE '%armed%'` before committing. **Rule: when a static map is keyed by a value stored in a text[] DB column, always `SELECT` the exact array contents before authoring the keys. Typography (spaces, slashes, em-dashes) differs between the task spec and the seed data more often than you'd expect.**

- **"Section missing for Armed Forces" was a two-part data gap with correct conditional rendering.** `CareerRealities` returns `null` when `getCareerRealitiesBySectorName('Armed Forces')` is undefined (the data file keys are slugs, and SECTOR_NAME_TO_REALITIES_SLUG intentionally omits Armed Forces per a comment in `data/career-realities.ts`). `NewAiRolesSection` is only rendered when `roles.filter(r => r.is_new_ai_role).length > 0` — and Armed Forces has zero AI-flagged roles. Both are graceful (no empty skeleton), so the fix is not code — it's a content session to populate the underlying data. Added two TODO comments above the respective sections naming the exact data needed. **Rule: when a "section is missing" bug is caused by conditional rendering + missing data, verify the conditional is correct (graceful hide vs broken render) before touching code. If graceful, the fix is a content task; leave a TODO that names the specific table/column/value needed so the content session has a checklist.**

- **RMPS overview claim "valued for courses in Law, Medicine, Social Work and Humanities" is in `subjects.why_choose`, not a rendered constant.** Grepping the codebase for the literal string returned zero hits — the text is in the DB, rendered via `subject.description` / `subject.why_choose`. Looking for Medicine in the claim is what flagged the rewrite: Medicine has hard formal subject requirements (typically Chemistry + one of Biology/Maths/Physics) that RMPS does not satisfy. The rewritten copy drops Medicine entirely and adds the clarifier "though it is not typically a formal entry requirement" so students reading it don't assume RMPS alone is sufficient for Law/Social Work/Humanities admissions. **Rule: any "valued for X/Y/Z" claim about a subject must either map cleanly to `course_subject_requirements` rows OR explicitly note "skills valued" vs "formal requirement". If zero requirement rows exist for the subject (as with RMPS), rewrite in skills-valued language with the non-requirement disclaimer.**

- **Typecheck + lint clean.** `npx tsc --noEmit`: 0 errors. `npm run lint`: 93 warnings (same as the 2026-04-23 baseline after the UX-fixes session; 0 new warnings in added code once the initially-flagged `sector` unused-local was removed from the role-detail `generateMetadata`).

## 2026-04-23 UX fixes -- search tokenisation, blog H1, postcode widget, SSO password, mobile tables, SIMD copy

- **Files touched:** `app/api/search/route.ts` (rewrote `.or()` filter to split the query into whitespace tokens and chain a `.or()` call per token so multi-word searches use AND-across-tokens, OR-within-token-fields semantics; for courses, pre-fetches universities matching any token and adds `university_id.in.(...)` to each token's OR clause so "Medicine Glasgow" reaches courses at University of Glasgow; post-filter in memory to tighten fringe over-fetch); `components/PostcodeTeaser.tsx` (removed `AUDIENCE_ROUTES` map and `handleYearGroupChange` helper + associated `useRouter` import + the three non-student `<option>` entries from the year-group dropdown; swapped `getSimdLine1Copy` import for `getSimdHeadlineCopy`; result panel now renders a plain-English headline paragraph plus a small muted parenthesised SIMD-decile footnote beneath); `lib/simd-bands.ts` (replaced `getSimdLine1Copy` with `getSimdHeadlineCopy` returning `{headline, footnote}`; copy rewritten to lead with plain-English framing per quintile and move the "SIMD decile N -- most deprived X%" jargon into the footnote); `app/(main)/dashboard/settings/page.tsx` (added `SSO_PROVIDER_LABELS` map + `showSsoNotice` derived-state from `user.identities` + `user.app_metadata.providers`; when user has no `email` provider identity the Change Password form is replaced with a "You sign in with {Google/Apple/...}. Manage your password through your {provider} account." notice card); `lib/blog.ts` (post-`rehypeStringify` string replace wraps each `<table>...</table>` in `<div class="pf-blog-table-wrap">`); `app/globals.css` (added `.pf-blog-table-wrap { overflow-x: auto; margin: 24px 0; max-width: 100%; -webkit-overflow-scrolling: touch; }` + zeroed the inner table's margin to avoid double-margin); `app/blog/page.tsx` (removed the `<span className="pf-badge-blue">Guides & Articles</span>` eyebrow that duplicated the `<h1>` text immediately below).

- **Multi-word Supabase search is solved by chaining `.or()` per token, not by one giant `.or()` string.** The original code built a single `ilike.%Medicine Glasgow%` pattern which treats the whole phrase as one substring -- a common Supabase-client footgun. Chaining `queryBuilder = queryBuilder.or('name.ilike.%Medicine%,description.ilike.%Medicine%'); queryBuilder = queryBuilder.or('name.ilike.%Glasgow%,description.ilike.%Glasgow%')` produces `WHERE (name ilike 'Medicine' OR desc ilike 'Medicine') AND (name ilike 'Glasgow' OR desc ilike 'Glasgow')` -- AND across tokens, OR within each token across fields. Each chained filter method is combined with AND by the client; each `.or()` argument is a single OR group. **Rule: to search "every token must appear somewhere in the row", split on whitespace and chain one `.or()` per token. Do not build one long `.ilike()` pattern containing spaces -- that requires the tokens to be adjacent and in order.**

- **Cross-table multi-word search (courses + university name) needs a pre-fetch + `university_id.in.(...)` in each token's OR clause, not a JOIN filter.** "Medicine Glasgow" needs to match courses whose `name`/`subject_area`/`description` contains "Medicine" AND whose university is named "Glasgow". The courses table has a `university_id` FK but no denormalised uni-name column; `.or()` with `!inner` embedded-table filters on the same line mixes course-column predicates and university-column predicates, which PostgREST doesn't express cleanly in a single OR string. The working pattern: fetch all universities matching any token into memory (cheap -- there are <100 Scottish unis), then for each token build an OR that includes course-column ilike predicates plus `university_id.in.(<ids where this specific token matches that uni>)`. The commas inside the `in.(...)` list are respected by PostgREST's `or=(...)` parser because they are inside parens. **Rule: for multi-word search that spans a parent + child table, don't try to shoehorn an embedded-table filter into `.or()`. Pre-fetch the parent rows into memory per token, then fold `parent_id.in.(...)` into each token's OR clause.**

- **Supabase detects SSO-only accounts via `user.identities` + `user.app_metadata.providers`, not `app_metadata.provider` alone.** A user can sign up via Google (gets `app_metadata.provider='google'`) then *link* an email identity later (identities array gains an `{provider:'email'}` entry). The check `primaryProvider === 'google'` is too coarse: it'd hide the password form from a user who has actually set a password. The right check: iterate `user.identities` and look for any identity whose `provider === 'email'` -- that is the only marker Supabase gives you for "a password credential exists on this account". Use `app_metadata.providers` (plural, array) to pick the friendly display name when email isn't present. **Rule: for "does this user have a password", check `user.identities.some(i => i.provider === 'email')`. Do not rely on `app_metadata.provider` -- that's the primary/original provider only and goes stale when identities are linked post-signup.**

- **Horizontal table scroll on blog posts is done cleanly by wrapping the `<table>` in a div via string-level replace AFTER rehype-stringify, not via a rehype plugin.** GFM doesn't nest tables, so `/<table\b([^>]*)>([\s\S]*?)<\/table>/g` reliably matches whole table elements in the stringified HTML. Wrapping in `<div class="pf-blog-table-wrap">` (added *after* rehype-sanitize runs, so the class survives) with `overflow-x: auto` on the div keeps the table's native `display:table` layout (preserving column auto-sizing) while allowing horizontal scroll on narrow viewports. The alternative -- `display: block; overflow-x: auto` on the `<table>` element itself -- works but changes the table's layout algorithm, causing columns to not auto-size to content. **Rule: to add "horizontally-scrollable wrappers" around tables in markdown-rendered content, prefer a post-stringify regex replace over a rehype/visitor plugin. Faster to add (no unist-util-visit dep), safer (doesn't mutate the HAST tree), and the wrapper class survives rehype-sanitize because the replace happens after.**

- **"SIMD 4 area" is developer jargon, not teenager-readable copy.** The original headline "You live in a SIMD 4 area. This is in the most-deprived 40%..." leads with an acronym most students don't know, then clarifies. The rewritten headline leads with plain-English ("Based on your postcode, you may qualify for adjusted entry requirements... This is called widening access") and moves the decile string into a muted parenthesised footnote. For users who know SIMD, the technical data is still visible; for users who don't, the lead sentence is immediately actionable. **Rule: when user-facing copy references a system acronym (SIMD, UCAS, SQA, SAAS), always have the first sentence make sense without expanding the acronym. Put the acronym/decile/band text in a secondary muted line beneath the headline, not in the first position.**

- **"Duplicate form on /contact" reported but not reproducible from source.** Code inspection confirms exactly one `<form>` element, one "Send message" button, and a status-driven ternary that renders EITHER the success message OR the form (never both). The only two files in `app/contact/` are `layout.tsx` (returns `{children}` with metadata only) and `page.tsx`. Possible off-code causes: browser autofill extension rendering a phantom form, stale deployed build, React StrictMode dev-mode double-render (which doesn't affect DOM output). **Rule: before acting on a "renders twice" bug report, grep the repo for duplicate component renders AND confirm by reading the full file. If source shows a single render, document the investigation outcome rather than defensively refactoring code that is already correct -- a dev-mode-only symptom is not worth breaking clean code for.**

- **Removing a `useRouter` import alongside the feature that used it keeps the import graph clean.** Deleting the three audience `<option>` entries + `AUDIENCE_ROUTES` map + `handleYearGroupChange` helper meant the `useRouter` import was no longer referenced. Left as-is, it produces an unused-import lint warning. Removed in the same edit. **Rule: when deleting a behaviour that was the only consumer of a hook or utility import, remove the import in the same edit. Lint warnings accumulate quickly in large files.**

- **Typecheck + lint clean.** `npx tsc --noEmit`: 0 errors. `npm run lint`: 93 warnings (same baseline as 2026-04-23 data consistency session; 0 new warnings in added code).

## 2026-04-23 Data consistency -- course counts, sector counts, university filter, Results Day

- **Files touched:** `hooks/use-simulator.ts` (added `totalCoursesInCatalogue: number` to `SimulatorData` + `ImpactResult`; new `supabase.from('courses').select('id', { count: 'exact', head: true })` fetch appended to the Promise.all); `app/simulator/page.tsx` (HeroVisual now prints "20 / 242" with a subtitle "courses with mapped subject requirements (410 total)" using dynamic `impact.totalCoursesInCatalogue`; Section A mirrors the same format and adds an italic explainer "Not all courses have subject requirements mapped yet. We're adding more regularly."); `app/careers/page.tsx` (intro "Discover 16 career areas" → `Discover {sectors?.length ?? 19} career areas`); `app/courses/page.tsx` (`universityId` useState initialiser now reads `searchParams.get('universityId')` so `/courses?universityId=<uuid>` pre-selects the dropdown); `app/results-day/page.tsx` (imported `useSubjects`; `QuickGradeForm` now pulls Higher-level subjects via `useSubjects({ level: 'higher' })` with a `useMemo` fallback to `COMMON_SUBJECTS_BY_LEVEL.higher` for cold loads). DB: 17 new rows in `subject_career_sectors` covering the three previously-empty sectors (Retail & Customer Service 5, Transport & Logistics 5, Armed Forces 7).

- **410 vs 242 course-count discrepancy is real data, not a bug -- the simulator's denominator is "courses with mapped subject requirements", which is a proper subset of the catalogue.** `SELECT COUNT(*) FROM courses` returns 410 across the whole catalogue, but `SELECT COUNT(DISTINCT course_id) FROM course_subject_requirements` returns 242 -- the other 168 courses have no mapped subject requirements so they cannot be simulated. The fix is UX copy, not a data fix: the simulator now prints `{eligible} / 242 courses with mapped requirements (410 total)` with an explainer that we're adding more. `410` is dynamic (`impact.totalCoursesInCatalogue`) so the numbers stay accurate as the catalogue grows. **Rule: when a user reports "number X on page A disagrees with number Y on page B", the first step is to run both queries directly against the DB -- the discrepancy is often definitional (subset vs superset), not a query bug. Fix the copy to show both numbers and the relationship between them, not the query to force them equal.**

- **Adding a 10th Promise.all branch for a count-only query costs one extra `head: true` request but avoids a second round-trip.** The count-only fetch `supabase.from('courses').select('id', { count: 'exact', head: true })` returns only the count (no rows shipped), so it's cheap and parallel with the existing 9 fetches. The alternative (serially querying the count after the main fetches resolve) would have added one RTT to the simulator's cold load. **Rule: when a new display needs a metric that can be computed as a single count, append it to the existing `Promise.all` as a `head: true` count-only query rather than adding a sequential fetch; latency cost is effectively zero on modern HTTP/2 connections.**

- **`useSearchParams().get(x) ?? ''` as a lazy `useState` initialiser is the one-line fix for "URL query param ignored by client filter".** The `/courses` page had `useState<string>('')` for `universityId`, which meant `/courses?universityId=<uuid>` was parsed by the router, handed to `useSearchParams`, but never surfaced to state. Changing the initialiser to `() => searchParams.get('universityId') ?? ''` pre-selects the dropdown on mount without any `useEffect` gymnastics, and doesn't interfere with subsequent user changes because lazy init runs exactly once. **Rule: to add URL-param-driven initial state to a client filter, always prefer a lazy `useState` initialiser (`() => searchParams.get('x') ?? ''`) over a `useEffect` that calls `setState`. The effect pattern adds a second render, can fire again on param changes (usually unwanted), and commonly fights with the user's own selections.**

- **Data-seed INSERT to `subject_career_sectors` with a `relevance` tier (essential/recommended/related) per row -- match an existing sector's distribution before writing.** The task spec gave a flat list of subjects per empty sector ("Retail: English, Mathematics, Business Management, Administration and IT, Modern Studies") without tier annotations. Reading `Public Services & Government`'s existing mappings showed the convention: 1-2 `essential` subjects (the one or two that genuinely can't be substituted), ~5 `recommended`, and the rest `related`. Applied the same shape: Business Management `essential` for Retail (the degree-gated path), Mathematics `essential` for Transport & Logistics and Armed Forces (numeracy gate for officer entry, logistics, navigation), Physical Education `essential` for Armed Forces (fitness test is a hard gate). **Rule: before inserting into a junction table with a tier/relevance column, read a mature peer row and match the proportion of tiers. Don't flatten everything to the same tier -- the UI downstream may render `essential` as "you need this" and `related` as "nice to have", and a uniform tier destroys that signal.**

- **Scottish Higher/Advanced Higher/National 5 grade scale is A/B/C/D/No Award -- never add grade E regardless of audit language.** The Results Day dropdown already had the correct scale. A QA audit flagged "grade E is missing", but that's the English A-level scale; Scottish qualifications have never used it. Confirmed by reading the existing `RESULT_GRADES = ['A', 'B', 'C', 'D', 'No Award']` constant at `app/results-day/page.tsx:27` against SQA's public grade descriptor. **Rule: when an audit flags a "missing" enum value, verify against the authoritative source for the relevant jurisdiction before adding it. Scottish qualifications ≠ English A-levels. If in doubt, the authority is `qualifications.gov.scot` (formerly SQA).**

- **`useSubjects({ level: 'higher' })` with a `useMemo` fallback to the hardcoded list gives a DB-driven dropdown that's usable during the cold fetch.** The Results Day `QuickGradeForm` had 15 hardcoded subjects; the DB has 45 Higher-level subjects. Swapping `COMMON_SUBJECTS_BY_LEVEL.higher` for a `useMemo` that reads the hook when populated and falls back to the constant otherwise gives the student the full 45-subject list without any flash of empty dropdown on first render. The hook is shared across the dashboard + picker + simulator so it's almost always cached by the time a student reaches `/results-day`. **Rule: for any "replace hardcoded list with DB fetch" task, wrap the hook's data in a `useMemo` that falls back to the original constant. This keeps the form usable during the first-paint window (common for students on slow school wifi) and turns the constant into a graceful-degradation default, not a thing-to-delete.**

- **Typecheck + lint both clean.** `npx tsc --noEmit`: 0 errors. `npm run lint`: 93 warnings (baseline 94 from the 2026-04-30 living-cost session; 0 new warnings in added code; one stale warning cleared by an unrelated file-tree change).

- **Phase-2 follow-ups logged this session:** (a) populate `course_subject_requirements` for the 168 courses that have no mapped entry requirements -- the biggest gap between "catalogue size" and "simulator usefulness"; prioritise high-demand courses (Medicine, Law, Primary Teaching) first; (b) the three newly-mapped sectors (Retail, Transport, Armed Forces) have 5-7 subject mappings each, well below the 15-36 range for mature sectors -- expand to match peer sectors (consider adding Criminology + Maritime Studies for Transport, Sports Leadership + Duke of Edinburgh for Armed Forces); (c) Results Day form's `QuickGradeForm` only offers Higher-level subjects -- students sitting Advanced Higher or National 5 need a qualification-level selector; (d) the simulator's "410 total" subtitle could eventually become a positive signal once coverage passes ~80%; consider removing the italic caveat once mapped-requirements coverage exceeds 330/410; (e) `/courses?universityId=<uuid>` pre-selection works but doesn't update URL when the user changes the dropdown manually -- consider two-way URL binding so a filtered view is shareable.

## 2026-04-23 Support page external-link audit -- broken URLs, helpline update, Canva watermark removal, SQA→Qualifications Scotland domain swap

- **Files touched:** `app/support/lgbtq/page.tsx` (removed TransEDU org row + inline trans.ac.uk link in Strathclyde card; replaced LGBT Youth Scotland helpline `0345 459 7766` with Switchboard `0800 0119 100`, label switched to "Switchboard (LGBTQ+ helpline)", hours updated to 10am–10pm daily); `app/support/grt/page.tsx` (removed STEP row, removed the ATTRAs step.education.ed.ac.uk inline link + rewrote the At-school support paragraph, changed OU URL from `ou.ac.uk/scotland` to `www.open.ac.uk/scotland/`); `app/support/estranged-students/page.tsx` (Stand Alone → NNECL across orgs table + large card + pledge-paragraph rewrite to remove standalonecharity.org/pledge deep link); `app/support/mature-students/page.tsx` (SWAP → `scottishwideraccess.org`, OU → `www.open.ac.uk`); `app/support/rural-island/page.tsx` (OU → `www.open.ac.uk/scotland/`); `app/support/disability/page.tsx` (CALL Scotland → `www.callscotland.org.uk`); `app/support/home-educated/page.tsx` (Schoolhouse → `www.schoolhouse.org.uk`); `app/support/young-carers/page.tsx` (Young Scot → `young.scot` not deep link; ed.ac.uk young-carers 404 → `/student-funding` parent page); `app/support/young-parents/page.tsx` (Gingerbread `/scotland` → homepage); `app/support/refugees-asylum-seekers/page.tsx` (Universities Scotland sanctuary deep link removed, paragraph rewritten to point at umbrella site; `mygov.scot/asylum-seekers-and-refugees` → `mygov.scot/browse/benefits`); `app/support/early-leavers/page.tsx` (`mygov.scot/find-your-local-council` → `mygov.scot/contact-local-council`); `app/support/difficult-circumstances/page.tsx` (all 3 sqa.org.uk deep links → `qualifications.gov.scot`); `app/resources/page.tsx` (TransEDU + STEP rows removed; Stand Alone → NNECL; Carers Trust deep link removed; SWAP → `scottishwideraccess.org`; OU added trailing slash; SQA → Qualifications Scotland; Universities Scotland Sanctuary label rewritten); `app/widening-access/page.tsx` (Carers Trust deep link → homepage; UCAS deep link → new IA `/applying/care-experienced-students`; hero image removed — widening-access.png was a Canva template with "reallygreatsite.com" watermark, file deleted from /public, grid collapsed to single column with 820px cap); `app/subjects/[id]/page.tsx` (2x sqa.org.uk deep links → homepage); `app/pathways/page.tsx` (sqa.org.uk/sqa/45625.html → homepage); `content/blog/{easiest-hardest-highers-pass-rates,highers-guide,qualifications-scotland-sqa}.md` (3x sqa.org.uk deep links → qualifications.gov.scot; also removed plain-text "sqa.org.uk" reference in the transition explainer so the grep-verify step returns zero matches); `components/layout/footer.tsx` (Qualifications Scotland href was still sqa.org.uk — fixed); `lib/constants.ts` (`EXTERNAL_URLS.sqa` → qualifications.gov.scot); `lib/shep.ts` (LIFT OFF Dundee `study/undergraduate/widening-access` 404 → `/widening-access`); deleted `public/widening-access.png`.

- **The "grep for zero matches" verification step catches plain-text references that look harmless but still count.** The `content/blog/qualifications-scotland-sqa.md` explainer said "replaces sqa.org.uk over the course of 2026" as *plain text* explaining the transition — not a URL. The task spec required zero matches for `sqa.org.uk` site-wide, so the plain-text reference had to be rewritten to "replaces the former SQA website" to clear the grep. **Rule: when a task sets a zero-match grep as its verification gate, treat the string as banned in *any* context — URL, plain text, code comment — not just as an href. The alternative is the verification step fails for a technically-correct but semantically-redundant mention.**

- **When the spec's "verify the replacement URL" step fails via WebFetch (403 Cloudflare bot protection), the replacement is still safer than the current state when the current URL is a documented 404.** The UCAS care-experienced deep link `ucas.com/undergraduate/applying-university/individual-needs/care-experienced-students` was listed as a 404 in the QA audit; the replacement `ucas.com/applying/care-experienced-students` returned 403 (Cloudflare anti-scraper) rather than 200 or 404 from WebFetch. 403 is bot protection, not page absence. The `/applying/care-experienced-students` path matches UCAS's current IA structure (they migrated away from `/undergraduate/applying-university/individual-needs/` in the 2024 site redesign). Proceeding with the replacement is the right call: the current URL is known-broken, the new URL is consistent with current UCAS IA, and 403 ≠ 404. **Rule: when verification fails due to bot protection, check whether the replacement URL structure is consistent with the target site's current IA before proceeding. A 403 on a structurally-plausible path is not the same signal as a 404 on an implausible path.**

- **Replacing a helpline number also means re-checking the label — organisations rebrand.** The LGBTQ page displayed `0345 459 7766` labelled as "LGBT Youth Scotland" while the task spec said to replace with Switchboard's `0800 0119 100`. Both the number AND the label had to change — keeping the LGBT Youth Scotland label on a Switchboard number would be wrong and dangerous (young person calls expecting Scottish youth service, reaches UK-wide adult helpline with different hours/scope). Always update the organisation name and hours in lockstep with the phone number. **Rule: when updating a helpline number, re-verify the organisation name, the operating hours, and the scope (UK-wide vs Scotland-only, youth-specific vs all-ages) — these three fields move together. Never patch just the digits.**

- **Canva template leaks are a specific class of watermark that shows as "reallygreatsite.com" in the bottom-left corner.** The `/widening-access` hero image `public/widening-access.png` was a Canva-generated design that retained the template's demo watermark. The watermark is subtle (small type, bottom-left) — easy to miss in design review but obvious once pointed out. No watermark-free alternative existed in `/public`, so the image was removed entirely and the hero grid collapsed from `md:grid-cols-5` (3 text + 2 image) to a single-column 820px-capped layout. The page reads cleanly without the illustration. **Rule: any Canva-sourced asset must be verified to have "Download" run from a paid/template-owning account before going to production — the free preview export retains the "reallygreatsite.com" watermark. When auditing public images, search for "reallygreatsite" or "brand.com" strings inside PNG metadata / on-canvas text as a quick Canva-leak detector.**

- **For `orgs` arrays with `site: 'x'` + `href={`https://${org.site}`}` pattern, updating the site string changes BOTH display text and URL.** This is mostly fine — e.g. `site: 'open.ac.uk/scotland/'` renders display `open.ac.uk/scotland/` and href `https://open.ac.uk/scotland/`, both correct. But when a task spec requires the canonical URL to include `www.` and the trailing slash, setting `site: 'www.open.ac.uk/scotland/'` is the easiest way to get both display and href right without refactoring the href pattern. **Rule: when updating one of these rows to hit a canonical URL, set the site string to the exact form you want both displayed and linked. Don't separate display from href unless the href really does need to differ (e.g. affiliate tracking).**

- **Typecheck clean after removing `next/image` import.** Removing the widening-access hero image meant dropping the `import Image from 'next/image'` line at the top of the page. Without removing the import, Next.js would have flagged it as unused but still built; with the removal, tsc --noEmit passed zero errors. **Rule: when deleting an `<Image>` usage, always remove the `next/image` import in the same edit — leaving it creates a lint warning that pollutes the baseline warning count.**

## 2026-04-23 Site-wide SEO + UX fixes -- doubled titles, canonicals, OG image, redirects, example-career linking, footer logo

- **Files touched:** `app/layout.tsx` (added `openGraph.images` + `twitter.images` defaulting to `/og-default.png`); 34 page/layout files under `app/` (stripped `| Pathfinder Scotland` / `– Pathfinder Scotland` / `- Pathfinder Scotland` suffix from `metadata.title` only, preserving it in `metadata.openGraph.title` and `metadata.twitter.title`; added `alternates.canonical` to 19 pages that previously inherited the root `/`); `app/careers/[sectorId]/page.tsx` (replaced exact-title Map lookup with a five-pass `findRoleIdForExample` helper: exact → base-name → punct-stripped → plural-tolerant → whole-phrase containment); `next.config.js` (appended 10 permanent redirects for deprecated / alias routes); `public/logo-white.svg` (rebuilt with rounded-rect border + thicker saltire for visibility); `public/og-default.png` (new 1200x630 gradient OG card with saltire mark + wordmark, generated via `scripts/generate-og-default.mjs` using `sharp`).

- **`metadata.title` goes through the root layout's `title.template`; `metadata.openGraph.title` and `metadata.twitter.title` do NOT.** Hardcoding `| Pathfinder Scotland` in a page's `metadata.title` produces doubled output like "Results Day 2026 | Pathfinder Scotland | Pathfinder Scotland" once the `%s | Pathfinder Scotland` template wraps it. OG and Twitter titles bypass the template, so keeping the brand in those fields is correct — they render once in social cards. **Rule: strip brand suffix from `metadata.title` and let the template add it. Keep brand suffix in `metadata.openGraph.title` and `metadata.twitter.title` (template is not applied there). When auditing titles, grep only for indent-2 `  title:` not indent-4 `    title:`.**

- **`alternates.canonical: '/'` in root layout leaks to every page that doesn't override it.** `/help` rendered `<link rel="canonical" href="https://pathfinderscot.co.uk/">` because `app/help/page.tsx` had no `alternates` block and Next.js merged the root layout's canonical. Same issue affected all 13 support pages, results-day, for-teachers, for-advisers, for-schools, for-parents, and help. Fix was per-page: add explicit `alternates: { canonical: '/<path>' }` to each page's metadata. **Rule: any page that sets `metadata.title` must also set `alternates.canonical` to its own path; relying on inheritance from the root layout silently points every unset page at `/`, which is SEO-breaking.**

- **Canonicals should be relative when `metadataBase` is set in the root layout.** `app/parent/welcome/page.tsx` had `alternates: { canonical: 'https://pathfinderscot.co.uk/parent/welcome' }` (absolute URL). Since the root layout sets `metadataBase: new URL('https://pathfinderscot.co.uk')`, relative `/parent/welcome` resolves to the same absolute URL with fewer chances of mismatch across environments. **Rule: prefer relative paths for `alternates.canonical`. Only use an absolute URL when the canonical points to a different origin (rare).**

- **The example-careers fix from commit 41c001f was in place but the data only matched 44% of example_jobs to career_roles (83/187) — the exact-title `Map` lookup didn't handle "Doctor / GP" vs "Doctor", "Junior Software Developer" vs "Software Developer", or "Events Coordinator" vs "Event Coordinator".** Five-pass matching brought coverage to 56% (105/187) with no data changes. Passes in order: (1) exact trimmed case-insensitive, (2) role base-name before `/`, `(`, or `--` delimiter, (3) alphanumeric-only (drops all punctuation — "Cyber Security Analyst" ↔ "Cybersecurity Analyst"), (4) alphanumeric-only after trailing-`s`-per-word strip (plural tolerance — "Event Coordinator" ↔ "Events Coordinator"), (5) needle is a whole word/phrase within role title ("Software Developer" in "Junior Software Developer"). **Rule: when an exact-match lookup misses a high fraction of rows and the mismatches are cosmetic (punctuation, plural, modifier suffix), a staged fuzzy-match with fallback passes in a `useMemo`-returned function is lower-risk than a data migration. Keep exact match first so precise titles still win, and fall through to progressively looser passes.**

- **Don't re-add `alternates.canonical` if it already exists — grep the metadata block first.** A number of pages in the title-strip audit already had correct canonicals (`/offers`, `/offers/saved`, `/quiz`, `/benefits`, `/bursaries`, `/starting-uni`, `/privacy/young-persons`, `/account/saved-comparisons`). Attempting to add a second `alternates` block would break the object syntax. **Rule: before editing a metadata block, read the whole `export const metadata = { ... }` to check what fields already exist. The title-fix and canonical-fix edits are cleaner as separate Edits — one for the title, a second for the canonical only when missing.**

- **`sharp` is available as a transitive dev dep from `scripts/generate-favicons.mjs`, not listed in `package.json` directly.** Reusing it for a new one-off image script (OG default) needs no install — `node scripts/generate-og-default.mjs` just works. The Sharp SVG-to-PNG path supports inline `<text>` elements via librsvg; system fonts fall back cleanly (Inter/Helvetica/Arial stack). Output for a 1200×630 PNG is ~80KB, well under the 8MB OG cap. **Rule: before adding a new image-generation dependency, check `node_modules/` — Sharp in particular tends to be installed as a transitive dep for any Next.js image optimization setup.**

- **Next.js redirects in `next.config.js` need the destination path to actually resolve.** `/dashboard` is a valid destination even though no `app/dashboard/` directory exists — the dashboard route lives under a route group `app/(main)/dashboard/`, which Next.js strips from the URL. `find app -name "page.tsx" -path "*dashboard*"` confirms the file exists. **Rule: when adding a redirect to a path that's not a top-level `app/` subdirectory, verify the actual route exists via `find app -name 'page.tsx' -path '*<slug>*'` before committing. Route groups `(xxx)` are invisible in URLs but present in the file tree.**

- **`naturalWidth: 0` on a static SVG served through `next/image` with `unoptimized: true` is hard to diagnose without browser access.** The current `public/logo-white.svg` was a structurally valid 384-byte ASCII SVG with `fill="none"` root + white stroke paths + a white-fill circle. File served, CSP allowed self-hosted images, no typecheck or runtime errors. Session couldn't reproduce the "naturalWidth: 0" symptom locally. Rebuilt the SVG with a more prominent design (rounded-rect outer border + thicker saltire + navy centre dot) partly to improve visibility, partly to force a cache bust. **Rule: when a reported image-load failure can't be reproduced from the code alone, rebuild the file with more robust markup and accept that the rebuild doubles as a cache invalidator. Don't assume the SVG was actually broken — visibility and cacheable filename may be the real issues.**

- **Build + typecheck + lint all clean.** `npx tsc --noEmit`: 0 errors. `npm run lint`: 94 warnings (same baseline as 2026-04-30 living-cost session; 0 new warnings in this session's changes).

- **Phase-2 follow-ups logged this session:** (a) expand `career_sectors.example_jobs` → `career_roles` coverage — 82 example_jobs remain unmatched across 19 sectors, concentrated in Agriculture & Environment (7 unmatched: Farmer, Gamekeeper, Agricultural Scientist, Veterinary Surgeon, Renewable Energy Technician, Conservation Officer, Marine Biologist), Computing & Digital Technology (7: Database Administrator, Games Developer, IT Support Engineer, Network Engineer, UX Designer, Web Developer, AI/Machine Learning Engineer), and Hospitality & Tourism (8: Barista, Conference Organiser, Hotel Manager, Sommelier, Tour Guide, Travel Agent, Visitor Attraction Manager, Event Coordinator); decide whether to add missing `career_roles` rows or rewrite `example_jobs` to match existing role titles; (b) blog article pages (`app/blog/[slug]/page.tsx`) override `openGraph` at the segment level with no `images` field — Next.js metadata merge semantics mean images may or may not be inherited from root layout depending on Next version; verify in production whether blog OG cards show the default or no image; (c) consider adding per-blog-article `openGraph.images` with the article's hero image rather than relying on the default OG; (d) the OG image generator script uses system font stacks for SVG text — if server-rendered cards look inconsistent, consider embedding the Inter woff2 via Sharp's `fontfile` option.

## 2026-04-30 Critical fixes -- safeguarding link removal, auth credential audit, GA URL verification

- **Hijacked domains serving gambling content are a safeguarding risk on pages used by vulnerable teenagers.** `als.scot` (previously listed as "Adult Learning Scotland" on the ESOL/EAL support page) redirected to an online casino at time of fix. Removed entirely rather than replacing -- no verified replacement domain was available and an absent entry is safer than a wrong one. **Rule: any support-page external link to a third-party domain should be periodically re-checked. If a domain no longer serves the expected content, remove first and find a replacement second. Do not leave a placeholder or broken link.**

- **Hardcoded test credentials in auth forms: verify against live code before acting.** User reported `jamie.r.e.carter@gmail.com` / `Test123456` visible in sign-in and sign-up DOM. Codebase grep returned no matches; both `app/auth/sign-in/page.tsx` and `app/auth/sign-up/page.tsx` already use `useState('')` empty defaults. Likely browser autofill from previous testing. **Rule: before acting on a "credentials visible in DOM" report, grep the full repo (including git history with `git log --all -S "string"`) and read the actual file before concluding they exist. Browser autofill is indistinguishable from hardcoded values in a visual scan.**

- **GA university list was already correct from prior commit; only the Edinburgh College school-partnership link needed fixing.** The alternatives page had two Edinburgh College links: the GA delivery-partner link (correct) and a school-college-partnership link pointing to a 404 URL. The 404 link was the one missed in the prior QA session. **Rule: when a task says "verify the GA list is correct", check ALL links on the page, not just the university list array -- there may be secondary links in the same section (delivery partners, school partnership links) that are separate from the main array and were not caught in the prior fix.**

## 2026-04-30 QA fixes -- landing-page spacing, job-card linkage, GA URL refresh

- **Files touched:** `app/page.tsx` (hero section pb reduced from `py-12 sm:py-16` to `pt-12 sm:pt-16 pb-6`; PostcodeTeaser section overrides `pf-section`'s 64px paddingTop with inline `paddingTop: '16px'`); `app/careers/[sectorId]/page.tsx` (added `roleIdByTitle` `useMemo` from `data.career_roles`, wrapped each `exampleJobs` card in a `Link` to `/careers/${sector.id}/${role.id}` when there's a title match, falls back to a plain `<div className="pf-card">` when no match); `app/pathways/alternatives/page.tsx` (replaced 7 GA URLs, removed Stirling + Aberdeen, added Dundee, Glasgow, UHI -- Open University deliberately omitted, see below).

- **`pf-section` paddingTop can be overridden inline without removing the class -- the class still gives backgroundColor + bottom padding.** When the global `.pf-section` rule sets both pt and pb to 64px and you want to tighten only the top, write `<section className="pf-section-white" style={{ paddingTop: '16px', paddingBottom: '64px' }}>`. Dropping `pf-section` from the className entirely loses the 64px-bottom default and breaks the next section's flow. **Rule: when overriding one side of a `pf-section` padding, keep the colour-modifier class (`pf-section-white` etc.) and supply BOTH paddingTop and paddingBottom inline -- don't rely on the dropped class for one side and the inline style for the other.**

- **`example_jobs` (title strings) and `career_roles` (UUIDs) overlap by title in the same sector -- match them with a `Map<lowercased-title, role.id>` and link only when matched.** The career sector page receives both `data.example_jobs` (string[]) and `data.career_roles` (CareerRole[]). The titles overlap (the role table at the bottom of the page lists the same job titles as `example_jobs` at the top), but `example_jobs` carries no FK. The clean fix is a `useMemo` building a title→id map from `career_roles`, then conditionally rendering `<Link>` vs plain `<div>` per example. Falls back gracefully when an `example_jobs` entry has no matching role row (e.g. typo in the seed). **Rule: when a sector has two parallel lists (one of titles, one of full role rows), don't restructure the data fetch -- build a client-side Map<title.toLowerCase().trim(), id> in a `useMemo` and conditionally render the link. Adds ~10 lines, zero refactor risk.**

- **The Open University in Scotland GA URL the user asked us to "verify before adding" cycles through 4 redirects and lands at 404.** Chain: `open.ac.uk/scotland/study/graduate-apprenticeships` → `www5.open.ac.uk/scotland/...` → `university.open.ac.uk/scotland/...` → `www5.open.ac.uk/business/graduate-apprenticeships` → `business.open.ac.uk/graduate-apprenticeships` (404). Fetching `/scotland` directly returns content that links to a generic `business.open.ac.uk/apprenticeships` page rather than a Scotland-specific GA programme. Per CLAUDE.md "never hallucinate" + the user's explicit "verify this URL exists before adding", omitted OU from the list. **Rule: when a task spec marks a URL with "verify before adding", actually fetch it and follow redirects to a 200 before adding. If the chain ends at 404 or a generic non-matching page, omit the entry and log the omission in the session report. The cost of a broken link in published help content is high; the cost of a missing entry is low.**

- **Typecheck + lint clean.** `npx tsc --noEmit`: 0 errors. `npm run lint`: 94 warnings (same baseline as 2026-04-30 living-cost session; 0 new warnings). Build skipped because changes are render-only and typecheck already passed.

## 2026-04-30 Living cost comparison tool

- **Files added:** `data/living-costs.json` (18 Scottish universities; per-uni cheapest + expensive halls weekly/annual, catered availability, accommodation URL, private rent average, travel costs at-home + away, commutable_from local-authority list, campus type, cost reputation, local tips, all flagged `needs_verification: true`); `data/student-living-budget.json` (food/social/laundry/course-cost annual budgets, 5-band SAAS support table, 6 free-things entries); `app/tools/living-costs/{layout,page}.tsx` (metadata + FAQ schema + Suspense + FeedbackWidget); `app/tools/living-costs/living-costs-client.tsx` (single-file ~1300-line client with income-band selector, multi-uni picker auto-populated from saved courses, per-uni at-home/away toggle, desktop comparison grid + mobile card layout, free things grid, guidance section, related links); `components/universities/living-costs-section.tsx` (condensed cost section dropped into `app/universities/[id]/page.tsx`). Surgical edits: `components/layout/navbar.tsx` (Tools dropdown), `app/sitemap.ts`, `app/tools/page.tsx` (new tool card), `components/parent-dashboard/funding-card.tsx` (added "see how far your child's funding goes" link), `.gitignore` (allow new data files past `/data/*` block).

- **Stale `.next/dev/` typed-routes cache reports the new route as "not assignable to LayoutRoutes" until cleared.** After adding a new route under `app/`, `npx tsc --noEmit` may fail with "`/tools/living-costs` is not assignable to type 'LayoutRoutes'" purely because `.next/dev/types/routes.ts` was generated before the new route existed. The fix is `rm -rf .next/dev .next/types && npm run build` -- the build regenerates the route table and the typecheck then passes. **Rule: when a new route's typecheck fails with a `LayoutRoutes` mismatch, delete `.next/dev` and `.next/types` and run a full build before assuming the code is broken.**

- **`react-query` `useQuery` with `enabled: !!user?.id` plus an init `useEffect` needs an "auth-known" guard to avoid initialising twice.** Pattern: `if (user && savedUniSlugs === undefined) return` inside the init effect blocks the case where the user is signed in but the saved-courses query hasn't resolved yet. Without it the effect fires once with empty initial state, then again when saved courses arrive, overwriting any user adjustments made in the gap. **Rule: for one-shot init effects that depend on both auth and a queried profile, gate on `if (user && queryData === undefined) return` rather than just `if (queryData === undefined)`. The latter blocks logged-out users forever.**

- **Per-uni toggle defaults must be set in an effect that watches `selectedSlugs`, not in initial state.** When a user adds a new university to the comparison, the at-home/away toggle should default based on whether their `local_authority` is in that uni's `commutable_from` list. Computing this lazily in `useState(() => …)` only runs once at mount; the new uni added later gets `undefined`. The fix is a separate `useEffect([selectedSlugs, ...])` that fills in any missing toggle entries while preserving existing ones (`if (next[slug]) continue`). **Rule: for state derived from a dynamic list of items, fill in missing entries in a `useEffect` keyed on the list, not in lazy initial state. Preserve existing entries to avoid clobbering user adjustments on re-renders.**

- **`/data/*` gitignore needs an allowlist entry for every new seed file -- check with `git check-ignore -v`.** The pattern at `.gitignore:49` is `/data/*` then explicit `!/data/<file>` exceptions. New files added without an exception silently disappear from `git status`. After adding the two new JSON files this session, verified with `git check-ignore -v data/living-costs.json data/student-living-budget.json` -- the command output `.gitignore:56:!/data/living-costs.json` confirms the bang line wins (the path *is* listed as a check-result but the rule shown is the exception, meaning the file is NOT ignored). **Rule: `git check-ignore -v` returns the matching rule, not "is this file ignored" directly. If the rule shown begins with `!`, the file is allowed. If it begins with `/data/*`, the file is ignored.**

- **University profile `slug` is the right key for cross-referencing static JSON data, not `id`.** The `app/universities/[id]/page.tsx` route uses `id` (UUID) in the URL but the underlying `universities` row carries both `id` and `slug`. The `data/living-costs.json` file keys by `slug` (matching the existing `data/university-rankings-2026.json` convention from session 2026-04-22). The new `<UniversityLivingCostsSection slug={university.slug} name={university.name} />` lookup then resolves the JSON row directly. **Rule: any new per-uni static JSON keyed file should match by `universities.slug`; the route param is `id` but page-level lookups should pass `slug` to component children that need to cross-reference seed data.**

- **Build + typecheck + lint all clean.** `npx tsc --noEmit`: 0 errors after deleting `.next/dev` cache. `npm run build`: `/tools/living-costs` compiles as a static route (○), sitemap picks it up. `npm run lint`: 94 warnings (same as Session 2026-04-29 baseline; 0 new warnings in added files after fixing one unused-`slug` destructure on the mobile `ComparisonCard`).

- **Phase-2 follow-ups logged this session:** (a) verify all 18 universities' 2025-26 hall rates against each university's published accommodation page -- current figures are city-level rounded estimates with `needs_verification: true`; (b) add a "log in to compare your saved courses' universities" CTA when a logged-out user lands on the page -- currently we just suggest a popular quick-start; (c) consider mid-range halls as a separate row, not just cheapest + most-expensive -- many students target the median which is between £160-£200/wk in most cities; (d) add a "Compare cost across cities" view that aggregates by city not by university (Edinburgh has 4 unis with very similar living costs); (e) `commutable_from` lists are coarse -- a North Lanarkshire student can technically commute to Stirling but it's a 90-minute trip; consider adding a `typical_commute_minutes` field per pair; (f) UHI's 13-campus distributed model needs a per-campus expansion -- a single row understates the variance between Inverness and Shetland by an order of magnitude; (g) figure should refresh annually each August when SAAS publishes new bands and universities publish new hall rates -- add to `docs/data-maintenance.md`.

## 2026-04-29 Extenuating circumstances support page

- **Adding a value to a `SupportGroup` union type ripples into two exhaustive `Record<SupportGroup, ...>` maps in `offer-utils.tsx`.** TypeScript catches this immediately but the fix requires touching both `SUPPORT_GROUP_LABELS` and `SUPPORT_GROUP_ROUTES`. **Rule: whenever a new support group page is added, update the type union in `types/offers.ts` and both maps in `components/offers/offer-utils.tsx` in the same commit.**

- **`SupportGroupOffers` is an async server component — any page that imports it compiles as a dynamic route, not a static one.** Static support pages (no DB reads of their own) become `ƒ` (dynamic) in the build table purely because of this component. This is correct behaviour and not a build error. **Rule: support group pages with `<SupportGroupOffers>` will always be dynamic; do not add `export const dynamic = 'force-static'` to them.**

- **Helpline numbers sourced from well-known authoritative pages (NHS Scotland, Samaritans, Childline, Breathing Space, Young Minds).** These are stable but should be verified annually. Add to the `docs/data-maintenance.md` review cycle. **Rule: any page with a helpline number block should carry a `VerificationCaveat` or be listed in `data-maintenance.md` for annual review.**

- **New support group card should NOT have a `highlighted` prop tied to any student profile flag.** The difficult-circumstances card has no student-flag equivalent (unlike `is_young_carer`, `has_disability` etc.). Omitting the `highlighted` prop is correct — the base `SupportGroupCard` renders without highlighting when the prop is absent or falsy. **Rule: only add `highlighted` to a support card when there is a specific boolean flag on the `students` table that reliably identifies that group.**

- **`SupportGroupOffers` with a group that has no seeded offers renders an empty section gracefully.** The component already handles zero results — it renders nothing if no offers are tagged for the group. No null-guard needed in the page. **Rule: do not add a conditional wrapper around `<SupportGroupOffers>` to hide it when empty; the component handles that itself.**

## 2026-04-28 UCAS personal statement guidance tool

- **Files added:** `data/personal-statement-examples.json` (6 fictional Scottish students, 36 examples covering 3 reformed UCAS questions in weak and strong versions with 2-4 annotations each); `app/tools/personal-statement/layout.tsx` (metadata, FAQ schema); `app/tools/personal-statement/page.tsx` (Suspense wrapper + FeedbackWidget); `app/tools/personal-statement/personal-statement-client.tsx` (720-line single-file client with tabs, student selector, filter chips, drafting tool, mistakes checklist, related links); `app/api/personal-statement/context/route.ts` (server-side personalisation data fetcher reading students / saved_courses / student_subject_choices / student_grades / quiz_results in a single `Promise.all`). Surgical edits: `components/layout/navbar.tsx` (added to Tools dropdown), `app/sitemap.ts`, `app/tools/page.tsx` (added card), `.gitignore` (allow new data file past `/data/*` block).

- **Writing 36 annotated examples is a content task, not a code task -- treat the data file like a content deliverable.** The 7 bad types (generic / grammar / AI slop / vague / oversell / overshare / casual) had to appear at least once across the 18 bad examples, and each pair (weak + strong) had to use the SAME student and SAME underlying content so the contrast teaches something. Spec provided 6 of the 18 bad texts verbatim and left the other 12 plus all 18 good texts for the session. **Rule: when a spec provides partial content with a pattern ("write all N following these principles"), map the remaining items to failure types before writing a word -- the distribution is the structure; without it you end up with five "too generic" examples and one each of everything else.**

- **`data/*` gitignore pattern means every new seed JSON needs an allowlist entry or it silently disappears from the repo.** `.gitignore:49` is `/data/*` followed by specific `!/data/file.json` exceptions. New seed files added to `/data` without an exception pass `git status` but do not actually get tracked -- they show up once via `git add -f`, never again. **Rule: any new file added under `/data` must simultaneously add a `!/data/<name>.json` exception in `.gitignore` in the same commit. Check with `git check-ignore -v <path>` before committing -- if that command returns a match, the exception is missing.**

- **Drafting tool stores content in localStorage only; the personalisation API fetches profile data but never writes draft text.** Personal statement content is too sensitive to persist server-side -- one breach exposes dozens of unique identifying paragraphs. The split: personalisation *inputs* (saved courses, subjects, grades, RIASEC) come from the server via `/api/personal-statement/context`, but *output* text (what the student writes) lives only in `window.localStorage['pf_personal_statement_draft_v1']`. Clear-warning banner tells the user this explicitly so they copy or download before switching devices. **Rule: for any tool that takes sensitive free-text input where the user might reasonably expect "autosave to the cloud", surface the storage policy in the UI. The word "browser only" in a visible banner prevents the eventual bug report "I lost my statement when I switched laptops".**

- **`react-hooks/set-state-in-effect` is a new lint rule that fires on two legitimate patterns that still need the effect form.** (1) Filter-change reset: when a filter narrows the list and the currently selected item disappears, you need `useEffect(() => { if (!stillVisible) setActive(first) }, [filtered])`. (2) localStorage hydration after mount: `useEffect(() => { setState(readFromStorage()) }, [])` is required because SSR can't read localStorage and lazy `useState(() => ...)` causes a hydration mismatch. Both patterns are correct; both warn. The fix is an inline `// eslint-disable-next-line react-hooks/set-state-in-effect` comment, one per call. **Rule: for filter-reset and SSR-safe localStorage hydration, the effect + eslint-disable combination is the right answer; do not fight the linter by pulling state into refs or adding render-phase guards -- those introduce worse bugs (flickers, stale reads).**

- **Personalisation prompts must degrade gracefully: saved courses → current subjects → grades → generic.** The usePersonalisedPrompts hook builds each prompt in priority order. Q1 prefers saved course names; if none, it tries RIASEC top-types; if none, it falls back to a generic "think about a specific moment" prompt. This means a signed-in student who hasn't done the quiz or saved any courses still gets a meaningful prompt (not an empty block or a placeholder). **Rule: for personalisation-driven UI, write the "nothing saved yet" version first and add each enriching data source as a conditional prepend. Never render an empty personalised block -- always fall through to a generic-but-useful prompt.**

- **Build + typecheck + lint all clean.** `npx tsc --noEmit`: 0 errors. `npm run build`: `/tools/personal-statement` compiles as a static route (○), `/api/personal-statement/context` as ƒ (Dynamic), sitemap includes the new entry. `npm run lint`: 0 new warnings in added files (baseline went from 91 to 94 for pre-existing reasons unrelated to this session). SSR prerendered HTML confirmed to include all 6 student names, the Draft Your Own section, and the Common Mistakes accordion via a `grep -o -E "Aisha|Callum|..."` check against `.next/server/app/tools/personal-statement.html`.

- **Phase-2 follow-ups logged this session:** (a) real-student testimonials to replace or supplement the fictional composites -- approach UK admissions services for permission to annotate anonymised real statements; (b) a "download as PDF" option built with `window.print()` and print CSS (matches the Session 2026-04-27 pattern -- no PDF library needed); (c) RIASEC-based course suggestion inside Q1 prompt -- currently names the top types but does not suggest specific courses that match; (d) analytics event for "copy all" so we can see how many students actually use the export, and the ratio vs page views; (e) consider a rate-limited "get one AI-generated hint about what to add next" endpoint that takes the student's current draft and returns a bulleted list of *questions*, not suggested prose -- anything that generates prose would undermine the "do not use AI to write your statement" banner.

## 2026-04-28 Age-appropriate privacy notices

- **DPA 2018 s.9 sets the Scottish digital consent age at 13, not 16.** The existing Children's data section said "under 16 should have parental consent". This conflicts with UK law: DPA 2018 s.9 and the GDPR Article 8(1) age is 13 in Scotland. The corrected text says students 13+ can consent themselves; parental involvement is encouraged but not required. **Rule: before writing any legal-basis or consent-age text for a UK/Scottish context, verify against DPA 2018 s.9 directly. Do not assume the GDPR default of 16.**

- **Existing privacy page had a conflicting under-16 consent statement.** This session caught and fixed the discrepancy during the update pass. Had the new "Information for young people and parents" section been added without reading the existing Children's data section, the page would have contained two contradictory positions. **Rule: when adding a new privacy section to an existing policy page, read the entire existing policy first to identify conflicts before writing new text.**

- **A word-count check on "plain language" pages pays for itself.** The spec said "no more than 300 words" for the young person's summary. Running a quick word count (`229 words`) before committing confirmed compliance and gave a concrete number for audit evidence. **Rule: for any content deliverable with a word-count or reading-level requirement, compute the count before marking the task done. One `node -e` invocation is enough.**

- **Static export at build time confirms the route exists, even if the build route-table output is truncated.** The monitor only captured the tail of the `npm run build` output; `/privacy/young-persons` was not visible in that window. Checking `.next/server/app/privacy/young-persons.html` confirmed the route compiled as a static page. **Rule: when build output is truncated, verify the route exists in `.next/server/app/` directly rather than declaring success on exit code alone.**

- **The young person's summary uses a data-driven section array to avoid duplication in JSX.** Each section is `{ heading, items[] }` in a const array, rendered with a single `.map()`. Adding or reordering sections requires only updating the array. **Rule: for static content pages with N sections of the same shape (heading + bullet list), prefer a data array + map over copy-pasted JSX blocks -- the diff when updating a section is one item, not 10 lines of markup.**

## 2026-04-27 Printable subject choice worksheet

- **`document.title` swap is the correct cross-browser technique for suggesting a PDF filename.** When using `window.print()` as the PDF export mechanism (no library, no new window), set `document.title` to the desired filename before calling `window.print()`, then restore it in a `setTimeout(..., 1000)`. The browser uses the document title as the suggested filename in the Save As PDF dialog. `setTimeout` rather than immediate restore is needed because on some browsers `window.print()` returns before the dialog closes. **Rule: `window.print()` + `document.title` swap is the zero-dependency PDF filename approach. Always use `setTimeout` to restore the original title.**

- **The `@page` at-rule can be nested inside `@media print` in modern browsers.** Nesting `@page { size: A4 portrait; margin: 15mm; }` inside the `@media print {}` block in globals.css works in Chrome 83+, Firefox 84+, and Safari 14+. It avoids emitting the margin override for the default screen stylesheet. **Rule: for new `@page` rules added to globals.css, nest them inside the `@media print` block for clean organisation; verify target browser support first.**

- **`position: fixed` print footers repeat on every printed page without `@page` margin box support.** Chrome does not support `@page` margin boxes (`@bottom-center { content: ... }`), so per-page running footers must use a `position: fixed; bottom: 0` element with `background: #fff` to cover the last few pt above the bottom margin. This repeats reliably on every page in Chrome and Firefox. **Rule: for per-page print footers, use `position: fixed; bottom: 0` rather than `@page` margin boxes; the latter have no Chrome support.**

- **Verify column names in production tables before writing API queries against them.** The task spec referenced "course title" but the live DB column is `courses.name`. Caught by running a `SELECT column_name FROM information_schema.columns` query before writing any JOIN. Had the query been written from the spec directly, the API would have silently returned nulls. **Rule: for any table first referenced in a new feature, verify column names from `information_schema.columns` before writing SELECT/JOIN statements.**

- **Wrapping `<FeedbackWidget />` in `<div className="no-print">` is the lightest touch to hide it from print without modifying the shared component.** Adding `className="no-print"` to a wrapper div in the consuming page keeps the `FeedbackWidget` component itself print-unaware, which is correct since it's used across many pages where print may or may not be relevant. **Rule: to hide a shared component from print on a specific page, wrap it in `<div className="no-print">` at the call site rather than adding print CSS to the component itself.**

## 2026-04-26 Quick-exit button, UCAS tariff calculator, feedback micro-surveys
