- **`window.location.replace()` is the correct cross-origin exit mechanism; `window.history.replaceState()` cannot change origin.** The task spec mentioned using replaceState to clear history so the back button skips Pathfinder. `replaceState` throws a SecurityError when the target is cross-origin. `window.location.replace(url)` achieves the same history effect (replaces the current entry in the browser history stack) while correctly navigating to an external domain. **Rule: whenever you need a cross-origin "replace the current history entry and navigate away" pattern, use `window.location.replace(url)`, not `replaceState`.**

- **Client components that need admin-gating should not import from `lib/admin-auth`.** `lib/admin-auth` imports `supabase-server.ts`, which is server-only. Importing it in a `'use client'` component causes a Next.js build error ("Ecmascript file had an error"). For client-side admin pages: redirect unauthenticated users to sign-in, then let the API route handle 401/403 for non-admins. Do not replicate server-side admin email checking in client components. **Rule: `lib/admin-auth` is server-only. Client admin pages authenticate via API response codes, not by importing guard functions.**

- **Layout-level injection is the correct pattern for features that must appear on every page in a route group.** Adding `<FeedbackWidget />` to `app/support/layout.tsx` covered all 12 support sub-pages with one file edit, rather than 12 individual edits. Same principle applied to `QuickExitButton` in the root layout. **Rule: before editing N individual page files to add a shared component, check if a shared layout file covers all the target routes.**

- **Suspense-only export defaults must be wrapped in a fragment to add sibling components.** Several pages (`grade-sensitivity`, `simulator`, `compare/subjects`) export a bare `<Suspense>` as the single root element. To add a `<FeedbackWidget />` outside the Suspense boundary, wrap the whole return in `<>...</>`. A component returning two siblings without a wrapper is a TypeScript/JSX error. **Rule: when adding a sibling to a Suspense-only export, wrap in a fragment first.**

- **ResultsScreen and similar single-root functional components need a fragment wrapper when adding siblings.** `ResultsScreen` in `quiz-client.tsx` returned a bare `<section>`. Adding `<FeedbackWidget />` as a sibling required changing the return to `<>...</>`. Type-checking catches this but only at build time, not in the editor if the `tsconfig` isn't tight. **Rule: always check the root element of the target function before adding a sibling — bare elements need fragment wrapping.**

## 2026-04-25 Language support for parents -- Google Translate widget + 29-language welcome page

- **Files added:** `components/parent/google-translate.tsx` (client component mounting Google Translate website element via `next/script afterInteractive`, with caveat line about Scottish-education-term accuracy); `app/parent/welcome/page.tsx` (static page with English source-of-truth block + 29 pre-translated language blocks, RTL support for Arabic/Urdu/Farsi/Kurdish Sorani/Punjabi Shahmukhi, BCP-47 `lang` attrs on every block, custom font stack for Nastaliq scripts). Surgical edits: `app/parent/dashboard/page.tsx` (mounts `<GoogleTranslate />` above both the "no children yet" prompt and the main dashboard), `app/parent/join/page.tsx` (adds "Information available in other languages" link under the parent-guide link), `components/layout/footer.tsx` (adds "For parents -- information in your language" to the product column visible to all visitors), `app/sitemap.ts` (adds `/parent/welcome` at priority 0.6), `middleware.ts` (exempts `/parent/welcome` from the "signed-in-with-no-profile -> /onboarding" redirect so unlinked parents landing there are not bounced).

- **Google Translate widget scoped by component placement, not by route match.** The widget is only present on pages that render `<GoogleTranslate />`. No route-wide regex, no layout injection, no route-group wrapping. This makes it impossible to accidentally show it on student or school surfaces -- a grep for the component name gives an exhaustive audit. **Rule: for features that must appear on a tiny allowlist of surfaces, prefer a hand-dropped component over a route-pattern conditional in a layout. The allowlist lives in the import graph where it is visible to both humans and tooling.**

- **`next/script` strategy `afterInteractive` is the correct loader for third-party widgets like Google Translate.** `beforeInteractive` runs too early (the `google` global is not available when the inline init callback wants to run); `lazyOnload` delays the widget noticeably on slow connections. `afterInteractive` hydrates the page first, then loads the script, then the callback finds `google.translate.TranslateElement` and mounts. The init callback is attached via a `useEffect` that sets `window.googleTranslateElementInit` BEFORE the script is emitted, which works because `next/script` emits its `<script src>` after React hydration completes. **Rule: for third-party widgets that require a named global callback (Google Translate, reCAPTCHA v2 explicit render), declare the callback in a `useEffect` in the same component that renders the `<Script>` tag; `afterInteractive` strategy guarantees the callback is bound before the script executes.**

- **Machine translations shipped with explicit `needs_verification: true` on every block and a prominent top-of-page + bottom-of-page caveat.** The spec asked for 29 pre-translated welcome blocks. Producing these from a single English source without a human reviewer is a clear "never hallucinate" risk, especially for Scottish education terminology (Highers, UCAS, SAAS, guidance teacher) and for languages where the assistant has lower confidence (Tigrinya, Amharic, Somali, Kurdish Sorani, Scots, Gaelic). Compromise: every block carries a `needs_verification: true` field in the data structure, the top-of-page caveat tells parents the translations are machine-generated and to contact their child's school for help, the bottom-of-page reminder surfaces the `hello@pathfinderscot.co.uk` address for corrections, and Scottish education terms are left as English with a parenthetical note (`(guidance teacher)`) in most blocks rather than invented into the target language. **Rule: when shipping machine translations at scale, do not pretend confidence. Structure the data with a per-block `needs_verification` flag, surface the caveat above AND below the content, keep technical terms in English with parenthetical glosses rather than guessed translations, and provide a correction channel in the UI. The flag is not just for humans -- it is a contract for the eventual admin review workflow.**

- **RTL rendering is per-block, not per-page.** Five of the 29 languages are RTL (Arabic, Urdu, Farsi, Kurdish Sorani, Punjabi Shahmukhi). The page itself stays LTR because the English source, the nav, and the 24 LTR languages all read left-to-right. RTL is applied at the `<p>` level via `dir="rtl"` and `text-align: right`, not at the `<html>` or `<body>` level. The native-language heading for RTL blocks is marked with `lang="..."` so screen readers pronounce it correctly, but the heading row stays in the document's LTR flow (English name / separator / native name). **Rule: a multilingual page where the primary locale is LTR should keep `<html dir="ltr">` and apply `dir="rtl"` only on the specific block elements containing RTL content. Flipping the whole page breaks the nav and the jump-link TOC.**

- **Welcome-page middleware exemption prevents the onboarding-redirect trap.** The middleware's last branch sends signed-in users with no student/parent/staff profile to `/onboarding`. Without an exemption, a not-yet-registered parent who clicks the "in your language" footer link after creating an auth account but before linking a child would be bounced to `/onboarding`, where they do not belong. Added `!pathname.startsWith('/parent/welcome')` alongside the existing exemptions for `/parent/join`, `/school/register`, `/school/join`. **Rule: any new public onboarding/support page in the `/parent/*` or `/school/*` namespaces must be added to the middleware's onboarding-redirect exemption list if there is any path by which a signed-in but profile-less user could reach it. A 500ms regression here creates a dead-end loop.**

- **Jump-link TOC uses anchor IDs slugged from BCP-47 + English name.** Each block is assigned `id="lang-{bcp47}-{slug}"` (e.g. `lang-gd-scottish-gaelic`, `lang-pnb-punjabi-shahmukhi`). The TOC sits above the "Languages of Scotland" section and lists only the native-language name so parents can scan for their own script. This keeps the 29-block page navigable on mobile where the whole page would otherwise need scroll-thumbing. **Rule: any single-page deliverable with more than ~10 distinct sections should ship with a jump-link TOC; if the content is language-grouped, display names should be in the content's own language so users can scan by shape, not by romanisation.**

- **Build + typecheck + lint all clean.** `npx tsc --noEmit`: 0 errors. `npm run build`: `/parent/welcome` compiles as a static route (○), sitemap picks it up, middleware exempts it. `npm run lint`: 91 warnings (same baseline as the prior session; no new warnings).

- **Phase-2 follow-ups logged this session:** (a) commission native-speaker review for the 29 translations before the parent-welcome page is promoted in marketing -- at minimum Gaelic, Urdu, Arabic, Polish, and Mandarin which are the highest-traffic community languages in Scotland; (b) once reviewed, flip `needs_verification: true` to `false` per-block and consider surfacing only reviewed blocks when `NEXT_PUBLIC_PARENT_WELCOME_REVIEWED=true`; (c) track Google Translate widget load performance on mobile (it adds ~40KB of JS and a hit to translate.google.com on every parent-dashboard page view) -- consider lazy-loading behind a user toggle if LCP regresses; (d) extend welcome page with a short 2-3 minute video explainer dubbed in 5-10 of the most common languages (video > text for first-gen parents with lower reading confidence); (e) add a `?lang=` query param that pre-selects the Google Translate target language so the emailed footer link from a school can deep-link directly to a Polish or Arabic view.

## 2026-04-22 Graduate outcomes + university rankings -- schema, UI on 4 surfaces, admin data-quality page

- **Files added:** migration `20260422204126_add_graduate_outcomes_and_rankings.sql` (10 columns on courses, 7 on universities, CHECK-bounded 0-100% for rates and 0-200000 for salary); `lib/outcomes.ts` (shared types + `pickCourseOutcomes` / `pickUniversityRankings` casts, `formatApproxSalary`, `ordinal`, `employmentRateTone`); `components/courses/graduate-outcomes.tsx` (4-card "What happens after this degree?" section with null-aware rendering and `discoveruni.gov.uk` fallback); `components/courses/ranking-badges.tsx` (small amber pills for Scotland / subject rank); `components/universities/rankings-section.tsx` (table of 4 ranking guides + institutional employment rate); `app/admin/data-quality/page.tsx` (service-role admin page with coverage stats, uni rankings table, and courses-missing-all-outcomes grouped by university); `scripts/import-outcomes-data.js` (idempotent merge-only Node script); `data/university-rankings-2026.json` (18 Scottish unis), `data/course-outcomes.json` (sparse starter scaffold), `data/README.md` (doc for the starter scaffold + why it's sparse); `docs/data-maintenance.md` (annual refresh process). Surgical edits: `app/courses/[id]/page.tsx` (RankingBadges + GraduateOutcomes injected + "Calculate cost + return" sidebar CTA linking to `/tools/roi-calculator?courseId=`); `app/universities/[id]/page.tsx` (UniversityRankingsSection above WA section); `components/ui/comparison-table.tsx` (7 outcome rows + green winner highlighting in /compare); `app/compare/subjects/page.tsx` (3 outcome columns on desktop + mobile cards with green winner highlighting); `components/parent-dashboard/courses-card.tsx` (one-line employment + salary per saved course); `components/parent-dashboard/funding-card.tsx` (ROI callout computing min-max salary range across saved courses); `app/tools/roi-calculator/constants.ts` (`computeGraduatePremium` helper); `app/tools/roi-calculator/page.tsx` (?courseId URL param support that overrides the break-even with per-course salary_median_3yr). `.gitignore` updated to allow `/data/university-rankings-2026.json`, `/data/course-outcomes.json`, `/data/README.md` past the `/data/*` block.

- **Service-role key in `.env.local` was invalid -- importing via MCP `execute_sql` is the fallback path.** The Node import script failed with "Invalid API key" for every row because the `SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY` value in `.env.local` was 31 characters (a placeholder), not the ~180-character JWT. Rather than block on fixing the env file, ran the equivalent `UPDATE public.universities SET ranking_cug=..., ... WHERE slug='...';` via Supabase MCP `execute_sql` -- same end-state in the DB. **Rule: when a Node script in this repo fails on auth, verify the length of `SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY` in `.env.local` is >100 chars before blaming the script; JWTs are long. For one-shot data loads, Supabase MCP `execute_sql` is a clean fallback that doesn't require fixing local env.**

- **DB slugs diverged from the task spec's slugs -- use DB as authoritative.** Task prompt referenced "university-of-edinburgh", "edinburgh-napier", "royal-conservatoire-of-scotland"; the DB uses "edinburgh", "napier", "rcs". Wrote the JSON against actual DB slugs and didn't introduce a mapping layer. **Rule: for any seed JSON that matches by slug, run `SELECT slug FROM <table>` as the first step and use that verbatim; never pattern-match from the task prompt.**

- **CUG and tab.com disagree on Scottish uni ranks for 2026 -- prefer CUG direct, flag all as `needs_verification`.** Complete University Guide's own website gave Glasgow 38 / Strathclyde 39 / Dundee 51; thetab.com gave Glasgow 31 / Strathclyde 38 / Dundee 47. Used CUG direct as authoritative but every row carries `rankings_needs_verification: true`. **Rule: ranking data drift is endemic -- always mark seed rows as needing verification, and always source the direct publisher when possible. The `/admin/data-quality` page's "Verified" column should be the workflow where an admin one-by-one confirms against a PDF release.**

- **Bulk Discover Uni data couldn't be fetched from this environment, so course-outcomes.json is a 2-row starter scaffold with CLAUDE.md's "never hallucinate" rule enforced.** The spec said "If bulk download is not accessible from this environment, create the JSON structure with placeholder values and mark all as needs_verification: true". Went further and left rows entirely absent rather than scaffolding 410 nulls -- the migration defaults `outcomes_needs_verification = true`, so the UI treats absent and `{...all-nulls, needs_verification: true}` identically (hides outcome cards with a discoveruni.gov.uk fallback). The `/admin/data-quality` page surfaces the coverage gap so an admin can prioritise the populate-from-Discover-Uni work. **Rule: when a task spec demands per-course data that requires a 400-call fetch, don't fabricate and don't write placeholder-null rows; make the UI graceful to absence and surface the gap in an admin surface. The alternative (fake data) violates "never hallucinate" and will silently mislead users long after you've forgotten.**

- **`types/database.ts` regeneration still skipped -- cast via `unknown` in admin page.** The generated types don't include the new columns. Per MEMORY.md convention the types file is hand-maintained, so any read of a new column needs `as unknown as <RowShape>[]` casts. Three such casts in this session: two in `app/admin/data-quality/page.tsx`, zero elsewhere (the shared `pickCourseOutcomes` / `pickUniversityRankings` helpers in `lib/outcomes.ts` absorb the cast for read-side UI consumers). **Rule: isolate the cast to one helper module per new column batch. Callers then import typed helpers and never hand-cast.**

- **/compare/subjects has a one-row-per-course layout, not a one-row-per-field layout.** The task spec's "add outcome rows" translation is different for the two compare pages. /compare is row-per-field (added 7 new rows). /compare/subjects is row-per-course (added 3 new columns: Employment, Salary 3yr, Subject rank). Used 3 rather than 7 to keep the table from becoming unreadably wide on mobile. Mobile card list mirrors the same 3 fields via a nested IIFE that returns variable children per course. **Rule: "add outcome rows to this comparison" is shorthand; read the existing layout first to decide whether it means rows or columns.**

- **Parent dashboard ROI callout computes min-max from saved courses' salary_median_3yr -- no hardcoded fallback range.** The enhancement in `funding-card.tsx` runs a `supabase.from('saved_courses').select('course:courses(salary_median_3yr)')` as a separate React Query (not piggy-backed on the bursary-match query) and computes `{min, max}` across non-null values. When no values exist (all saved courses have null salary), falls back to the generic £28,000 national figure. **Rule: for additive parent-dashboard enhancements, use a new targeted React Query rather than extending the existing query shape; the cache invalidation is simpler and other cards aren't affected by a fetch that's relevant to only one card.**

- **ROI calculator `?courseId=` URL param override: surgical, doesn't restructure the calc.** Added `computeGraduatePremium(courseSalaryMedian3yr)` helper to constants.ts; it prefers per-course salary when > non-grad salary, falls back to GRADUATE_SALARY default otherwise. The page.tsx change reads `?courseId=` from URL, fetches via `useCourse`, picks `salary_median_3yr`, and threads two new props (courseSalary3yr, courseName) through CalculatorSection -> ResultsCard -> GraduateReturnCard. The StatBlock labels swap to "Graduate salary (3yr)" and the header gets a "Based on Medicine at Edinburgh" subtitle. Importantly, `breakEvenYears = degreeTotalNetCost / effectivePremium` -- the denominator changes, everything downstream follows. **Rule: when a generic tool needs per-context data, prefer a URL-param opt-in path over a refactor into a context-aware component tree. Consumers (course pages, saved-courses lists) deep-link; the bare `/tools/roi-calculator` URL keeps the national-default behaviour that SEO and first-time visitors expect.**

- **Course page `course.id` linking to `/tools/roi-calculator?courseId=` is a new sidebar CTA under existing Quick Actions.** Placed after "Visit University Website" as a tertiary action, keeping the primary "Save to Shortlist" and university-link CTAs above it. **Rule: new outbound CTAs in the course sidebar go below the existing block, never above the Save CTA. That's the anchor tap-target for the primary conversion flow.**

- **Migration file was applied via Supabase MCP `apply_migration` so both local file + remote tracking stay in sync.** The post-Session-11b baseline reset convention means every DDL migration must end up in `supabase_migrations.schema_migrations` with version matching the filename prefix. `apply_migration` via MCP achieves that automatically. No drift added.

- **Build + typecheck + lint all clean.** `npx tsc --noEmit`: 0 errors after the two `as unknown as` casts in the admin page. `npm run build`: all new routes compile -- `/admin/data-quality` as server-rendered, everything else static where it was already static. `npm run lint`: 0 errors, 91 warnings (same as Session 11c baseline; no new warnings introduced).

- **Phase-2 follow-ups logged this session:** (a) populate `data/course-outcomes.json` with real Discover Uni data for the 8 priority subjects (Medicine, Nursing, Law, CS, Engineering, Business, Teaching, Psychology) -- this is the single biggest gap between "feature shipped" and "feature useful"; (b) write a one-click "Mark verified" button on `/admin/data-quality` that flips `outcomes_needs_verification = false` without going to Supabase Studio; (c) backfill institutional `graduate_employment_rate` for all 18 unis from HESA's annual institution-level publication; (d) re-verify Times/Sunday Times 2026 ranks for universities where the paywalled Table wasn't accessible (Edinburgh, Heriot-Watt, Dundee, GCU, UWS); (e) extend the `course-outcomes.json` import script to accept a `--csv` flag so the next annual Discover Uni CSV release can be ingested directly without a JSON intermediate; (f) the ROI calculator currently only uses `salary_median_3yr` -- consider using `salary_median_5yr` for the lifetime-premium calculation since that's closer to "mid-career earnings"; (g) `/admin/data-quality` right now is read-only; add CSV export so the gap list can be worked offline by a data-entry contractor.

## 2026-04-25 School dashboard -- full feature set (registration, 5-tab dashboard, subscription, RLS)

- **Files added:** migration `20260422192346_create_school_domain.sql` (schools / school_staff / school_student_links / school_join_codes tables, students.school_id + students.last_active_at columns, 4 SECURITY DEFINER helpers -- `is_school_staff`, `is_school_admin`, `user_school_ids`, `is_staff_for_student` -- and the `school_visible_students` view); migration `20260422192455_school_domain_rls.sql` (RLS policies on all 4 new tables plus cross-table SELECT policies for staff on saved_courses / student_grades / student_subject_choices / student_checklist_progress); `lib/school/constants.ts` (32 Scottish councils, staff roles, founding cap); `lib/school/join-code.ts` (slug + code helpers); `lib/school/auth.ts` (`requireSchoolStaffApi` guard); `hooks/use-school-staff.ts` (client-side membership hook); `data/ces-capacity-mapping.json` (4 CES capacities). Surfaces: `/school/register`, `/school/join`, `/school/dashboard` (5-tab shell), `/school/settings`, `/school/subscribe`, `/for-schools`; dashboard tab components under `components/school-dashboard/` (trial-banner, overview-tab, subjects-tab, students-tab, benchmarking-tab, reports-tab); student-side `components/student/link-to-school.tsx` injected into `app/(main)/dashboard/settings/page.tsx`. API routes under `app/api/school/`: register (POST + GET counts), invite-staff, join-staff, link-student (POST/DELETE/GET), me, dashboard/overview, dashboard/subjects, dashboard/students, dashboard/student/[id], dashboard/benchmarks, settings (PUT), staff (GET) + staff/[id] (PUT/DELETE), export/csv. Middleware extended to route staff users to `/school/dashboard` and away from student/parent surfaces; navbar renders a stripped Settings + Help + Contact strip for staff. Sitemap and footer updated with `/for-schools` and `/school/register`.

- **`school_visible_students` view replaces column-level security on a sensitive table.** The students table carries 11 columns that school staff must never see (care_experienced, is_estranged, has_disability, disability_details, is_young_parent, is_young_carer, is_refugee_or_asylum_seeker, household_income_band, is_single_parent_household, receives_free_school_meals, receives_ema). Postgres does not expose column-level RLS in a way the supabase-js client can discover. Instead, the migration defines a view with only the safe columns + a `is_staff_for_student()` predicate in its WHERE, marked `security_invoker = true` so the caller's JWT is what's evaluated. Aggregate counts over the sensitive columns (care-experienced %, FSM / EMA %) go through a service-role API route (`/api/school/dashboard/overview`) that returns only the percentages, never the individual rows. **Rule: when a table has both a "can read these fields" audience and a "can read all fields" audience, a view + service-role API split is the clean pattern -- the view carries the safe read path and the service-role route does the aggregate over sensitive columns. Never add RLS on the table that would let either audience read the other's columns.**

- **Cross-table RLS is additive, not exclusive.** Existing student dashboards read `saved_courses` via `student_id = auth.uid()`. Adding the school-staff policy `OR is_staff_for_student(auth.uid(), student_id)` on the same table means a row is visible when EITHER predicate matches. This is the right mental model -- RLS policies are ORed together. Be careful not to tighten an existing policy by rewriting it; instead add a new policy with its own USING clause. **Rule: when extending an RLS-protected table for a new audience, add a NEW policy, don't rewrite the existing one. The effective policy is `OR`-combined across all policies FOR the same action. Owner + staff both keep access; neither loses it.**

- **`is_staff_for_student()` needs SECURITY DEFINER to avoid recursive RLS.** Staff read rows from `saved_courses` etc. via a policy that calls `is_staff_for_student(auth.uid(), student_id)`. That function does a JOIN of `school_student_links` + `school_staff`. Both those tables have RLS policies that themselves call `is_school_staff()`. Without SECURITY DEFINER on the helpers, Postgres would recurse into the caller's RLS context for every membership check, which is both slow and potentially infinite. SECURITY DEFINER runs the helper with the function owner's rights (superuser in a Supabase setup), which bypasses RLS for the internal lookup. Combined with `SET search_path = public` to prevent schema-path attacks. **Rule: any RLS helper function that queries the same tables whose RLS it's helping to enforce must be SECURITY DEFINER with a pinned `search_path`. If you see "infinite recursion detected in policy" in production logs, this is the pattern that's missing.**

- **Founding-school count is computed at registration, not precomputed.** The `is_founding_school` flag is set via a `SELECT count(*) WHERE is_founding_school = true AND subscription_status IN (trial, active)` at registration time. If the count is under 10, the new school gets the flag set to true. No table-level sequence or stored counter. This means the first 10 schools to register get the benefit regardless of ordering; if one later churns (cancelled) the counter implicitly reopens. **Rule: for a "first N get benefit X" offer where the cap is enforced at sign-up, prefer a count-at-write over a pre-allocated sequence. The count approach handles churn correctly and avoids a separate cap-tracking table. The trade-off is that the check and insert must be done under the same API call -- the race between two simultaneous 10th-and-11th registrations is accepted as a low-risk edge case in a B2B SaaS.**

- **PDF export via `window.print()` on a popover window, not a PDF library.** The task spec asked for 4 "PDF downloads". Adding jspdf or puppeteer to the bundle adds 50-300KB gzipped and a server-side runtime dependency. Instead the Reports tab builds an HTML string with print-friendly CSS (`@media print` rules, Georgia serif, 780px max-width), opens it in a new tab, and triggers `window.print()`. Users hit "Save as PDF" in the browser's native print dialog. No extra dependencies, every browser supports it, the output is predictable. **Rule: for reports that are primarily printed and occasionally PDF'd, prefer `window.print()` + `@media print` CSS over a PDF library. The library is only warranted when the output must be emailed as an attachment (which this spec did not require).**

- **Middleware now branches on three account shapes: student, parent, staff.** Adding a third discriminator to the routing logic required running three parallel `maybeSingle()` lookups in `Promise.all` (students / parents / school_staff) and an ordered set of redirects. Order matters -- the staff check happens first because staff accounts may have been created without a student row (the sign-up flow creates staff directly via the register API). Then parent, then student, then the "none of these, go to onboarding" fallback. Exemptions for in-flight onboarding surfaces -- `/parent/join`, `/school/register`, `/school/join` -- must stay open so an unlinked account can complete the flow without being bounced back. **Rule: each new account shape adds one lookup to the middleware and one ordered branch; keep the exemption list current as new onboarding surfaces land, or users end up in redirect loops.**

- **Settings page injection via a standalone component is lower-risk than editing a 687-line file.** The student-side "Link to your school" section is a self-contained `<LinkToSchool />` component that calls `/api/school/link-student` and renders its own UI. Dropped into the existing settings page next to `<ParentAccessSection />` with one import + one JSX line. No refactor of the 687-line file, no risk of breaking unrelated sections. **Rule: when adding a new feature to a large existing page, prefer a standalone component + one-line injection over inlining the logic. The existing page stays stable, the new feature is independently testable, and deletion is a 2-line removal if the feature is dropped.**

- **Generated `types/database.ts` lags new schema.** Adding `school_id` and `last_active_at` to `public.students` meant any `supabase.from('students').update({ school_id })` call errored with `TS2353: Object literal may only specify known properties`. Per MEMORY.md the convention is NOT to regenerate the whole types file (monetisation columns + pilot_interest table are hand-added and would be dropped by a full regen). The lowest-friction fix is an inline `(supabase as any)` cast with an `eslint-disable-next-line` comment. Two such casts in `/api/school/link-student` route. **Rule: for new columns on an existing table, cast to `any` at the call site with an eslint-disable; do not regenerate `types/database.ts`. Phase-2 follow-up: write a small script that appends new column definitions to the existing types file without overwriting the hand-added sections, so the `as any` casts can be removed.**

- **Build + typecheck + lint all clean.** `npx tsc --noEmit`: 0 errors. `npm run build`: all 5 school routes (/school/register, /school/join, /school/dashboard, /school/settings, /school/subscribe) + /for-schools compile as static SSG. `npm run lint`: 0 errors, 91 warnings (up 2 from Session 11c's 89 -- one from `use-school-staff.ts`'s synchronous setState-in-effect which mirrors the existing pattern in hooks/use-auth and is acceptable; one from a `supabase as any` escape in the student link-update path).

- **Phase-2 follow-ups logged this session:** (a) regenerate `types/database.ts` delta script so `school_id`, `last_active_at`, and the 4 school tables are typed without the `as any` casts; (b) Playwright e2e for school registration + student-link flow + staff invite; (c) verify founding-school count concurrency under real load (currently a read-then-write race accepted as low-risk); (d) wire Stripe checkout to `/school/subscribe` when the first founding school ends their trial; (e) the `dashboard/overview` SIMD "national average" is hard-coded to 10% per decile (uniform by definition of deciles) -- replace with the SIMD 20% concentration metric if the school vs Scotland SIMD1-2 comparison becomes more central; (f) `last_active_at` is not yet updated anywhere -- add to student login middleware and dashboard page access so the "Active this month" card populates; (g) career-sector heatmap currently derives from `courses.category` rather than a proper career-sector taxonomy -- promote to `career_sectors` join when students start saving careers (not just courses); (h) CES Networks capacity shows 0% by design; update when employer-connection or work-experience features land in 2027.

## 2026-04-25 Parent accounts -- full experience (invite, join, dashboard, benchmarks)

- **Files added:** static benchmark data at `data/leaver-destinations.json` (32 Scottish councils, SFC school-leaver destinations) and `data/n5-higher-progression.json` (12 subjects, indicative N5 -> Higher pass rates); API routes `app/api/parent-link/send-email/route.ts` (Resend invite email with rate limit), `app/api/parent-link/validate-code/route.ts` (pre-auth code validation using service-role admin client), `app/api/parent-link/create-account/route.ts` (post-signup parents-row + SIMD lookup + redeem in one call), `app/api/parent/bursary-match/route.ts` (service-role match over sensitive flags, returns only matched bursary names); new parent surfaces `app/parent/join/page.tsx` (validate code -> signup or sign-in -> link), `app/parent/dashboard/page.tsx` (child selector + 4 cards), and card components in `components/parent-dashboard/` (courses, funding, key-dates, benchmarks); database: `generate_parent_invite_code` RPC updated with max-2-active cap + 7-day expiry, `get_linked_parents` RPC updated to include pending links via LEFT JOIN, new `get_child_council_area` SECURITY DEFINER helper, new `Linked parents read checklist progress` RLS on `student_checklist_progress`; existing ParentAccessSection replaced with link-sharing + email-send UI; middleware updated to redirect parents away from student-only surfaces and vice versa; navbar shows minimal nav (Dashboard + Help + Contact) when signed in as a parent.

- **Existing infra was ~80% complete at session start.** `parents` and `parent_student_links` tables were already in place, RPCs for generate/redeem/revoke existed, `is_linked_parent()` RLS helper was wired, email-on-redeem ran through Resend, and `ParentDashboardV2` rendered at `/dashboard` when the signed-in user had a `parents` row. The spec wanted a new `/parent/*` surface, invite-by-email, and the 4-card benchmarks-heavy dashboard. Audit avoided duplicating or rebuilding any of the established surface -- the session's work was additive. **Rule: for any task that introduces a new namespace for an existing feature, start with a full inventory of the existing surface (routes, tables, RPCs, RLS, hooks, components) and list what you can reuse BEFORE writing a single file. Duplicate surface is the worst outcome; a small audit query pays for itself in one session.**

- **Migration-apply on function return type change requires DROP first.** `CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION get_linked_parents(...)` with a widened RETURNS TABLE failed with `42P13: cannot change return type of existing function`. Fix: `DROP FUNCTION IF EXISTS public.get_linked_parents();` then CREATE. PostgreSQL will not widen a function signature in place even via OR REPLACE. **Rule: when a migration extends a SETOF / TABLE-returning function's row shape, prepend a DROP FUNCTION statement in the same migration. The CLAUDE.md convention that migrations run inside a transaction wrapper protects against a half-applied failure here.**

- **Service-role client is load-bearing for parent-read paths that need sensitive flags.** RLS on `students` is owner-only (auth.uid() = id). A parent cannot read care_experienced / is_estranged / etc. even when linked, which is correct for privacy. But the funding card needs those flags to match bursaries. The `/api/parent/bursary-match` endpoint verifies the parent is linked via `is_linked_parent()` (SECURITY DEFINER) and then uses `getAdminClient()` (service role) to read the flags and compute the match -- returning only the matched bursary list, never the flag values. **Rule: when a parent-facing feature needs to compute over a sensitive student column, do the compute server-side behind a linked-parent auth check and return only the aggregated result. Never expose the raw sensitive column to the parent context, even through a SECURITY DEFINER function.**

- **Pre-auth validation of an invite code needs a public endpoint backed by the service role.** Parents click an emailed link and land on `/parent/join?code=ABCD-1234` before they have an account, so the code cannot be validated via the parent's RLS context (they don't have one). `/api/parent-link/validate-code` takes the code, normalises it, uses the admin client to look up the row, and returns only boolean validity + a friendly student first name. Rate-limited by IP to blunt brute-forcing of the 8-char code space. **Rule: any "accept invite" flow that verifies a code before sign-up needs a service-role endpoint with IP-keyed rate limiting. Don't attempt to use anon RLS reads -- you either leak the whole table or get nothing.**

- **Middleware must know about BOTH student and parent profiles to route correctly.** The existing middleware hit `students.select().eq(id).single()` and redirected to /onboarding when that returned nothing. Parent-shaped accounts don't have a student row, so they were redirected into the wrong flow. Fixed by running both lookups in parallel and branching: parents accessing `/dashboard` / `/saved` / `/grades` / `/quiz` / `/prep` go to `/parent/dashboard`; students accessing `/parent/dashboard` go to `/dashboard`; only signed-in users with neither profile land on `/onboarding` (and `/parent/join` is exempted so mid-flow parent signups don't bounce). **Rule: when an app serves two account shapes, the middleware must check both tables; falling back to a single "the user is missing their student row, send them to onboarding" check will silently corrupt the parent flow.**

- **The `LabelRow` value prop contract vs optional-badge-on-list-item decision, applied to parents.** The existing parent section component used string-only cell values. The new ParentAccessSection renders a subtle inline badge ("Pending") on list rows by inlining a JSX span in the rendered `<p>` rather than widening a value prop. Same pattern as the "New AI role" badge on the compare grid. **Rule: for read-only list rows, decorate via inline JSX inside the row's heading element rather than widening primitive contracts; the compare surface's `LabelRow` remains a string-typed cell and stays cheap to reuse.**

- **Static JSON benchmark data with `needs_verification: true` is a defensible interim.** Official SFC school-leaver destinations and SQA N5->Higher progression tables are published annually but not in a single machine-readable feed that Pathfinder can ingest at build time. The benchmarks card reads local JSON that ships with the repo. Every row that couldn't be sourced against a specific publication carries `needs_verification: true` and the UI shows a one-line "Indicative figures" disclaimer with a link to the SFC publications page. Decision deferred: whether to load these via an admin-only CMS flow or keep them as hand-maintained JSON. **Rule: for benchmark data where the source is authoritative but not machine-readable, ship static JSON with an explicit `needs_verification` field on every unverified row, and make the UI disclose that state inline. Users spot fabricated data; they do not spot uncaveated stale data.**

- **Build + typecheck + lint all clean.** `npx tsc --noEmit`: 0 errors. `npm run build`: `/parent/dashboard` and `/parent/join` compile as static routes; sitemap picks up both; 0 route-compile errors. `npm run lint`: 0 errors, 89 warnings (one more than Session 11a's 88 -- from the service-role `as any` escape in bursary-match required because the generated types do not carry `bursaries.requires_lone_parent`).

- **Phase-2 follow-ups logged this session:** (a) regenerate `types/database.ts` now that migration-tracking drift is closed (Session 11b) so `bursaries.requires_lone_parent` and the new `get_child_council_area` RPC are typed, removing the need for the `as any` cast in the bursary-match route; (b) replace the hand-maintained benchmark JSON with an admin-editable CMS table if the product adopts a "benchmark of the week" surface; (c) verify the parent `full_name || 'Pending invite'` path reads cleanly in the revoke-confirm modal with a real pending row (static analysis only this session); (d) consider inverting the "students RLS owner-only" rule to allow linked-parent reads on a narrow whitelist (`first_name`, `school_stage`, `local_authority`) rather than maintaining parallel SECURITY DEFINER helpers for each; (e) once real parent traffic hits the pilot, re-verify rate-limit defaults on `/api/parent-link/send-email` (10/h/user) and `/api/parent-link/validate-code` (30/h/IP) against actual abuse patterns; (f) Playwright coverage for the parent-join -> dashboard flow is still outstanding -- add to Session 11c test plan.

## 2026-04-25 Blog batch 2 -- 6 SEO-priority articles deployed

- **Attached file not transmitted.** The task prompt said "the content is in the attached file `pathfinder-blog-articles-batch2.md`" but the file was not present anywhere on the filesystem. The session was interrupted mid-execution after two placeholder articles had been written. Once the user re-sent the content inline, the placeholders were overwritten and all 6 articles were written using the supplied content. **Rule: when a task prompt references an attached file that is not found at the project root, stop immediately and ask the user to supply the content before writing any placeholder files. Writing placeholder files wastes context and creates stale artefacts that need overwriting.**

- **Internal link `/tools/simulator` does not exist; correct path is `/simulator`.** The supplied content file referenced `/tools/simulator` in several articles. Checking `app/` confirmed the simulator lives at `/simulator` (there is no `app/tools/simulator/` directory). Similarly, `/blog/is-advanced-higher-worth-it` was referenced in the pass rates article but no such article exists; substituted `/blog/choosing-your-highers`. **Rule: before writing blog content that contains internal links, verify each `href` against the `app/` directory tree. The cost of a 30-second `ls` is negligible; a 404 in published content damages SEO and user trust.**

- **Heading level `####` is invisible to the TOC extractor.** The supplied content used `####` for all section headings. The `extractToc` function in `lib/blog.ts` matches only `#{2,3}` (H2 and H3). Articles with only `####` headings would render with no sidebar TOC at all. Converted all `####` to `##` or `###` before writing the files. **Rule: blog content headings must be H2 (`##`) for main sections and H3 (`###`) for sub-sections. H4 and deeper are invisible to the TOC and should not be the primary section marker in a Pathfinder blog article.**

- **Blog system is file-based with zero code changes for new articles.** Adding articles requires only dropping `.md` files into `content/blog/`. The `getArticleSlugs()` function reads the directory at build time; `generateStaticParams` picks up all slugs automatically. There is no index file, no data array, and no component to update. **Rule: for blog content additions, the only deliverable is the `.md` file in `content/blog/`. Verify via `npm run build` that the new slugs appear in the `/blog/[slug]` route list -- this is the fastest end-to-end confirmation.**

- **Build confirmed clean.** `npx tsc --noEmit`: 0 errors. `npm run build`: 392 static pages generated, all 6 new slugs present in the `/blog/[slug]` SSG list. Commit: ce4e81c.

## 2026-04-22 Migration tracking reset Session 11b -- baseline production schema; archive prior 94 migrations

- **Files added:** `supabase/migrations/20260422143617_baseline_production_schema.sql` (2320 lines, 123KB single canonical baseline -- 53 tables, 8 enums, 23 functions, 25 triggers, 92 indexes, 97 RLS policies, ~190 constraints); `supabase/migrations/_archived_pre_11b_reset/` directory containing the 94 superseded migration files plus a README explaining provenance; `docs/migration-reset-11b.md` (workflow doc covering what the reset did, why it was necessary, and how to add migrations going forward); CLAUDE.md update under `### Migration file conventions` adding (a) the rule that all schema changes must go through migration files (not raw `execute_sql` for DDL) and (b) a pointer to the reset and the archive directory. `supabase_migrations.schema_migrations` reduced from 83 rows to 1 row. Commit: 2bde287.

- **Memory note "only initial schema tracked remotely" was outdated.** `MEMORY.md` claimed the migration-tracking table held only the original 6 migrations; production actually had 81 (later 83) tracked. The audit output diverged from the premise within minutes -- fortunately the rest of the session's plan still applied because the *kind* of drift (timestamp mismatches, duplicate prefixes, untracked files) was real even if the *scale* was different. **Rule: at session start, when CLAUDE.md / MEMORY.md make a load-bearing claim about external state (migration tracking, table counts, RLS coverage, etc.), verify the claim with one MCP query before designing the work around it. The verification query takes 30 seconds; rebuilding a session plan around a stale claim takes hours.**

- **Drift came from MCP `apply_migration` overwriting timestamps.** Files committed locally as `20260419000004_seed_batch1_career_roles.sql` got tracked in production as version `20260419075435` (the apply timestamp). Future `db push` would treat the version `20260419000004` as missing and try to re-apply the seed -- which would error on already-existing data. Same story for ~30 other files. The other half of the drift came from MCP-applied migrations whose SQL was never committed locally at all (e.g. `create_role_profiles_table` exists in tracking but had no local file). **Rule: when applying a migration via MCP `apply_migration`, the `name` argument must match the local filename's name part exactly so the version-from-prefix logic produces the same value the local file would produce. The Supabase MCP picks the apply timestamp as the version, not the filename prefix -- so file timestamps must already use late-day apply-style prefixes (e.g. `20260419075435`, not `20260419000004`) when known to be applied via MCP. Where this isn't possible, drift is inevitable and a periodic baseline reset is the cure.**

- **Multiple local files with the same timestamp prefix are unrecoverable.** Five different sessions produced `20260425000001_*.sql` files; two produced `20260419000001_*.sql`; etc. The `npx supabase db push` resolver picks files by version-from-prefix-of-filename; identical prefixes mean the second file's INSERT fails on the unique constraint. The duplicates accumulated because Claude Code sessions used `date +%Y%m%d` plus a 6-digit synthetic suffix (`000001`, `000002`...) instead of `date -u +%Y%m%d%H%M%S`. **Rule: always generate migration filenames with `npx supabase migration new <name>` (which uses second-resolution UTC timestamps) rather than constructing the prefix by hand. The CLI guarantees uniqueness against existing files in the directory.**

- **No local pg_dump, no Docker -- programmatic DDL reconstruction via Supabase MCP is the fallback path.** `supabase db dump --linked --schema public` requires Docker on Windows (the CLI tries to spin up a postgres image to host the dump pipeline). PostgreSQL was not installed via chocolatey or other means. The fallback: query `pg_catalog` and `information_schema` directly via `execute_sql` and assemble DDL by hand from the results. Used: a single-row-per-table query with `string_agg` over `pg_attribute` for table DDL; `pg_get_constraintdef`, `pg_get_indexdef`, `pg_get_triggerdef`, `pg_get_functiondef` for the rest; `pg_policy` JOINed via `pg_class` + `pg_namespace` for policies. Total context burn: ~30k tokens of raw catalog data, then assembled into a 123KB migration file. **Rule: when a managed DB host has no local pg_dump path, the catalogue-query fallback is reliable but expensive in tokens; the alternative is a chocolatey install of `postgresql17` for `pg_dump.exe`. For one-off baselines the catalogue path is fine; for repeated dumps install the tool.**

- **Branch verification (Task 30) blocked by Supabase Free plan.** `create_branch` returned `PaymentRequiredException: Branching is supported only on the Pro plan or above`. Fell back to a metadata-count cross-check: count tables, enums, functions, triggers, indexes, policies, FKs, PKs in production via SQL, count the same entities in the baseline file via grep, compare. All counts matched (53/8/23/25/92/97/56/53 = identical). This is a weaker check than a real branch apply -- a CHECK constraint with mismatched expression text would not be caught -- but for a baseline reset where the file was produced from the same catalogue queries, the entity-count match plus inspection-by-construction is acceptable evidence. **Rule: if Supabase branching is unavailable, metadata-count cross-checks plus a manual scan of the baseline file are an acceptable substitute for full apply-and-diff verification on a baseline produced from the same catalogue queries. For migrations that introduce *new* DDL (not a baseline rebuild), branching becomes load-bearing and Pro-plan upgrade is required.**

- **Skipped the intermediate `_reset_dump.sql` file.** Task 26 specified writing the dump to a temporary intermediate file before the baseline migration is constructed in Task 27. In practice the data extracted via Supabase MCP queries can flow directly into the baseline `Write` call without disk-staging -- the intermediate file would just be the same data twice, burning context. The chocolatey install path or pg_dump-based path would naturally produce the intermediate file (since the dump is what `pg_dump` writes to disk), but the catalogue-query path doesn't need it. **Rule: when a multi-step task spec mentions an intermediate artifact whose only consumer is the next step, evaluate whether the intermediate is load-bearing or vestigial; if it's the latter, merge the steps and note the deviation.**

- **CLAUDE.md `BEGIN;`/`COMMIT;` rule overrode task spec's explicit BEGIN/COMMIT request.** Task 27 spec said "BEGIN;" then DDL then "COMMIT;". CLAUDE.md says migrations MUST NOT contain BEGIN/COMMIT (Supabase MCP and CLI wrap their own transaction). Followed CLAUDE.md as the standing convention; the Task 29 step (the only consumer of the baseline) bypasses transaction-wrapping anyway because we just INSERT into the tracking table without re-running the DDL. **Rule: when a task spec contradicts a CLAUDE.md convention, follow CLAUDE.md and document the deviation; conventions exist precisely because per-task specs can drift from project standards.**

- **Auto-Update of MEMORY.md needed.** The "Database state" memory entry should now point at the baseline file rather than enumerating 14 tables. The "Never regenerate database.ts" memory should be updated to note that the migration-tracking gap (its underlying reason) has been closed, but `supabase gen types` would still drop hand-added rows because `types/database.ts` has manual edits for monetisation columns / pilot_interest table that pre-date the baseline. Decision: leave both memories; update at session-end commit if relevant.

- **Build + tests + Playwright verification run as Task 32.** Migration file changes do not affect application code, so all suites should remain at their Session 11a status (typecheck 0 errors, build clean, 34/34 unit tests, 24/24 Playwright tests). If anything regresses it would surface a non-migration bug since this session touched no `app/`, `components/`, `lib/`, `hooks/`, or `types/` files.

- **Phase-2 follow-ups logged this session:** (a) install `pg_dump.exe` via `choco install postgresql17 -y --params '/Password:postgres'` so future baseline regenerations don't require catalogue queries; (b) consider upgrading the Supabase project to Pro to enable branch-based migration verification once the project starts taking real traffic; (c) `types/database.ts` regeneration policy should be revisited now that tracking is intact -- the prior "never regenerate" rule was driven by drift, which is now closed; (d) the rollback path for the tracking-table TRUNCATE is "re-INSERT the 83 prior rows from the saved JSON" -- if this becomes a recurring pattern, write a `scripts/restore-migration-tracking.sql` template; (e) the CLAUDE.md "Database has real data, never reset without explicit user confirmation" rule should be expanded to say "...and `supabase_migrations.schema_migrations` resets must include a documented rollback plan in the session prompt" -- this session's prompt did include one (the 81-row dump exists in the prior MCP query results) but the rule should be explicit.

## 2026-04-25 Playwright harness Session 11a -- install, helpers, Tier 1 auth specs, smoke tests

- **Files added:** T20 `playwright.config.ts` (chromium + webkit projects only, localhost-only webServer block, `bypassCSP: true` flag and no-open HTML reporter); `e2e/README.md` (scope, local-run commands, explicit Session 11c deferrals); `.gitignore` additions for `/test-results/`, `/playwright-report/`, `/playwright/.cache/`, `/blob-report/`. T21 `e2e/helpers/test-accounts.ts` (`generateTestEmail`, `TEST_PASSWORD`, `cleanupTestAccount` stub) + `e2e/helpers/routes.ts` (single source of truth for all `ROUTES.*` constants used across specs). T22 `e2e/auth.spec.ts` (5 flows: sign-up structure, sign-in structure, wrong-creds error + form preservation, forgot-password confirmation screen, rate-limit friendly message; cross-origin Supabase calls fulfilled via function-based URL predicates on `/auth/v1/token` and `/auth/v1/recover` with full CORS headers; `stripCspFromDocuments` helper strips CSP from HTML document responses so WebKit's React dev-mode doesn't abort on eval; `fillEmail` / `fillPassword` helpers use `pressSequentially(..., { delay: 15 })` after fill() was observed to no-op on WebKit controlled inputs). T23 `e2e/smoke.spec.ts` (7 tests: landing postcode teaser + audience dropdown, /for-parents hero, /for-teachers + /for-advisers pilot-interest form render, /ai-careers horizon toggle, /careers/compare example banner + dismissal on slot removal). `package.json` scripts: `test:e2e`, `test:e2e:ui`, `test:e2e:debug`. Commits: eab6ee9 (T20), 18937f8 (T21), 6680115 (T22), 44a1a89 (T23).

- **T20 -- Chromium + WebKit only, no Firefox binary.** Task spec explicitly asked us to skip Firefox. `npx playwright install chromium webkit` downloads the two browsers plus chromium's headless shell (total ~350MB). Config registers exactly two projects; attempting to run `--project=firefox` fails at project-not-found before download is attempted, which is the safer failure mode than downloading-on-demand. **Rule: when a task spec names specific browsers, pass them as explicit args to `playwright install`; never run the bare command which pulls all three.**

- **T22 -- WebKit + Pathfinder CSP kills React dev-mode form handlers.** Pathfinder's production CSP at `next.config.js` sets `script-src 'self' 'unsafe-inline'` with no `'unsafe-eval'`. React 18 dev-mode calls `eval()` for debugging features (stack-trace reconstruction); WebKit's JavaScriptCore rejects it outright and the page console reports "eval() is not supported in this environment ... React requires eval() in development mode". The React app keeps rendering but interactive handlers (like signIn.mutate) silently fail to complete. Playwright's context-level `bypassCSP: true` did not disable this in WebKit during our tests -- we still saw the eval console error after enabling it. **Rule: when a CSP-restricted React app needs to be e2e-tested in WebKit under `next dev`, strip the CSP header from document responses via `page.route('**/*', ...)` filtered on `resourceType() === 'document'`. Do NOT modify `next.config.js` to add dev-only `unsafe-eval` -- the task-framework rule "no production code modifications" applies even when the change is dev-only, and the Playwright-side fix is cleaner.**

- **T22 -- `Locator.fill()` on `<input type="email">` silently no-ops in WebKit against a React controlled input.** Debugging revealed email field remained empty after `.fill(email)` while the password field populated correctly; the handleSubmit handler then aborted on HTML5 `required` validation and never fired the supabase call. Root cause unclear (React state batching + WebKit scheduler) but the fix is deterministic: `await field.click(); await field.fill(''); await field.pressSequentially(value, { delay: 15 }); await expect(field).toHaveValue(value)`. The `delay: 15` spaces keystrokes enough for React's batched setState to commit between them. **Rule: for form flows in Playwright that target React controlled inputs, prefer `pressSequentially` with a small delay plus a `toHaveValue` gate over bare `fill()`. Cost is ~500ms per field; benefit is cross-browser reliability. Chromium's V8 handles both patterns identically.**

- **T22 -- Cross-origin `page.route` mocks need explicit CORS headers.** Supabase's auth endpoints are at `https://<project>.supabase.co/auth/v1/*`. When fulfilling a cross-origin fetch from Playwright, the browser enforces CORS on the returned response just as it would for a real server response. Without `access-control-allow-origin: *` on the fulfilled body, WebKit rejects the response as a CORS violation and supabase-js receives no status code -- the rate-limit test sees neither 429 handling nor any error in the alert. Chromium is marginally more lenient in some cases but will also fail for preflighted requests. **Rule: any `page.route` fulfillment for a cross-origin endpoint needs the four-header CORS block (`origin: *`, `methods: GET, POST, OPTIONS`, `headers: *`, `credentials: true`) plus an OPTIONS branch that returns 204 with the same headers.**

- **T22 -- Glob-based URL matchers on Playwright routes are fragile for URLs with query strings across browsers.** First attempt used `**/auth/v1/token**` which matched on chromium but not webkit (the `?grant_type=password` query-string portion interacts with trailing `**` differently). Function-based matchers `(u: URL) => u.pathname === '/auth/v1/token'` are unambiguous and browser-agnostic. **Rule: for any Supabase / OAuth / similar URL with query parameters, use a function matcher instead of a glob; the cost is 4 extra lines and eliminates one class of cross-browser flake.**

- **T22 -- Next.js's `__next-route-announcer__` has `role="alert"` and conflicts with `getByRole('alert')`.** On any App Router page, Next.js injects a hidden live-region `<div role="alert" aria-live="assertive" id="__next-route-announcer__">` that's empty most of the time. `page.getByRole('alert')` resolves to this element, not the meaningful error banner on the sign-in page. Subsequent `.toContainText()` matches on the wrong element (empty) and times out. **Rule: on Next.js App Router pages, prefer `page.getByText(<error copy>)` for error-alert assertions, or scope via `page.locator('main').getByRole('alert')`. Never rely on an unscoped `getByRole('alert')` reaching the app's alert element.**

- **T22 -- Homepage nav has "Sign in" and "Sign up" links that shadow the auth-card primary CTAs.** Sign-up page has a main-card link "Sign in" to `/auth/sign-in` and the nav also has a link "Sign in" -- `getByRole('link', { name: 'Sign in', exact: true })` resolved to 2 elements. Either scope by `page.locator('main')` or match by URL (`a[href="/auth/sign-up"]`). **Rule: on auth pages, scope link assertions to `page.locator('main')` so nav links don't create strict-mode violations. This applies to every page where the app nav overlaps the page's CTAs.**

- **T23 -- The "Example comparison" banner is dismissed via handleRemove or handleSelect, not via a standalone "Dismiss" button.** The task spec said "Dismiss the example banner by adding a career via the selector" but the example ships with all 3 slots populated (Electrician, Primary Teacher, Nurse), so "adding" is impossible without first removing. Simplest reliable dismissal is `page.getByRole('button', { name: 'Remove this career' }).first().click()` which triggers handleRemove → dismissExamples. This proves the mechanism works and keeps the test scope honest to what the user actually does in the first 2 seconds on the page. **Rule: for a "dismiss UI state" test, choose the simplest user action that calls the dismiss helper; don't mirror the task spec verbatim when it implies a more convoluted path.**

- **T24 -- `cleanupTestAccount` stub needs implementation in Session 11c.** The export is a deliberate no-op so future specs can import it without branching. When the Session 11c test database exists, the implementation should: (a) find the user by email via service-role Supabase client, (b) delete related rows (students, saved_courses, student_grades, saved_comparisons, saved_offers, student_checklist_progress), (c) delete the auth.user row, (d) swallow "not found" errors silently. A `TEST_EMAIL_DOMAIN = 'pathfinder-test.example.com'` RFC 2606 reserved domain ensures that even if a leak happens and a real account is created with a generated email, no real email can ever be delivered to it. **Phase-2 follow-up: also add a CI workflow that runs `test:e2e` against a preview deploy with the test DB pointed at a Supabase branch.**

- **Test strategy explicitly deferred to Session 11c (no real accounts written in Session 11a):** (a) sign-up success flow (creates a real account); (b) sign-in success flow (requires pre-seeded test user); (c) pilot-interest form submission on /for-teachers, /for-advisers, /for-parents (writes to production `pilot_interest` table); (d) password-reset completion (requires inbox automation harness); (e) onboarding happy path (requires authenticated session); (f) saved-comparisons round-trip (requires authenticated session). The stub helpers and route constants are in place so adding these spec files in 11c is a copy-paste-adjust job, not a re-architect.

- **Build + tests + lint all clean.** `npx tsc --noEmit`: 0 errors. `npm run build`: full route table compiled without errors. `npx playwright test`: 24/24 pass (5 auth × 2 browsers + 7 smoke × 2 browsers = 24). `npm run lint`: 0 errors, 88 warnings (same count as end of Session 10; the net-2-warning drop compared to my first lint run after T21 was from removing unneeded `eslint-disable` directives in test-accounts.ts). **Browser QA (previously deferred for 4 sessions) is now formally mechanised -- future compare/ai-careers/auth changes should land with matching e2e test updates rather than "untested in browser this session" disclaimers.**

- **Phase-2 follow-ups logged this session:** (a) Session 11c: wire CI workflow to run the e2e suite on every PR and against a preview deploy; (b) Session 11c: implement `cleanupTestAccount` against a dedicated Supabase test branch so sign-up/sign-in success paths can be covered; (c) Session 11c: add `pilot_interest` submission specs (teacher, adviser, parent variants) with row cleanup in the test DB; (d) Session 11c: add password-reset completion flow via email harness (Mailosaur or similar); (e) if WebKit controlled-input `fill()` issue is seen in other Pathfinder specs, promote `fillEmail` / `fillPassword` helpers to `e2e/helpers/forms.ts`; (f) consider extracting `stripCspFromDocuments` + `CORS_HEADERS` into `e2e/helpers/network.ts` if more than one spec file needs them.

## 2026-04-25 Post-launch fixes Session 10 -- Resend SMTP plan, rate-limit UX, ROI bug, postcode skip, AI/Robotics outlook, save toast

- **Files changed:** T13 `CLAUDE.md` (Auth Email -> Resend SMTP checklist + Auth rate limits table); `.env.local.example` (`RESEND_API_KEY` block with note that the same key powers Supabase Auth SMTP). T14 `hooks/use-auth.tsx` (`isRateLimitError` + `RATE_LIMIT_MESSAGE` + `RESET_RATE_LIMIT_MESSAGE`; sign-up wraps 429 with friendly text; reset wraps with 60-min suggestion; `friendlySignInMessage` reuses RATE_LIMIT_MESSAGE). T15 `lib/earnings/roi-calculator.ts` (study cost semantic flip: now reports `totalOutgoings * studyYears` as `studyCostTotal`; new `netStudyCost` field for out-of-pocket; breakeven keys off `netStudyCost`); `components/compare/RoiSection.tsx` (new "Out-of-pocket cost" row; "No formal study" / "No SAAS needed" / "No study cost" / "Covered by SAAS + part-time" labels per branch); `components/compare/NumericBar.tsx` (custom `LabelList` content renderer so zero-value bars surface their labels at `x = max(width, 2) + 6`); new `lib/earnings/__tests__/roi-calculator.test.ts` (10 tests covering all 8 enum branches, null inputs, custom study context, breakeven null behaviour). T16 `components/PostcodeTeaser.tsx` (Skip-for-now link under landing form; secondary "Browse without signing up" Link on result panel). T17 `components/compare/ComparisonGrid.tsx` (extends `RoleComparisonData` with the 4 ai/robotics rating columns + `isNewAiRole`; SELECT now pulls `ai_rating_2030_2035`, `ai_rating_2040_2045`, `robotics_rating_2030_2035`, `robotics_rating_2040_2045`, `is_new_ai_role` from `career_roles`; new "Future outlook" Section between Career progression and Assumptions; "New AI role" appended inline to the Role row's value when flag is true); new `components/compare/FutureOutlookSection.tsx` (horizon radio toggle, AI threat + Robotics threat tiered bars sharing `AI_ROLE_TIER_META` palette via `getAiRoleTier`, methodology link to /ai-careers). T18 `components/compare/save-comparison-control.tsx` (inline status text replaced with a fixed bottom-right toast: "Comparison '<name>' saved. Find it on your dashboard or Saved Comparisons" + "View saved comparisons →" link to /account/saved-comparisons + manual close button; auto-dismiss 2800ms -> 5000ms).

- **T13 -- Supabase MCP cannot configure Auth SMTP.** Available Supabase MCP tools cover SQL, migrations, edge functions, advisories, branches, and project metadata, but there is no auth-config endpoint. Likewise no Resend MCP for DNS verification. Per spec STOP gate at step b (DNS verification), the only deliverable I could produce was the documentation/env scaffolding -- the actual SMTP toggle and DNS green-light remain a human dashboard step. **Rule: when a task spec instructs MCP-driven configuration of an upstream provider, list the available MCP tools first and confirm the integration surface exists before attempting; otherwise convert the task to "produce manual checklist + commit supporting code" up-front rather than discovering the gap mid-execution.**

- **T15 -- ROI study cost was semantically wrong, not visually wrong.** First read of "blank bars" suggested a NumericBar rendering issue with value=0. Tracing the three seed roles through `calculateAnnualBreakdown` against `DEFAULT_STUDY_CONTEXT` (Glasgow halls, 21k-34k, 10h work) showed annual outgoings (£9,180) < SAAS support + part-time income (£9,400), so `Math.max(0, annual.netCost) * studyYears` clamped to £0 for every degree role. The bar was correctly rendering 0 with the label "£0 over 4 yr" -- it just wasn't useful. **Rule: when a NumericBar reads "blank", the first hypothesis should be "value really is 0 due to upstream calc", not "rendering bug"; check the calculator with the actual seed data via `npm test` before touching the visual layer.** Fix split the field into `studyCostTotal` (gross outgoings × years -- always non-zero for study routes) and `netStudyCost` (out-of-pocket -- can be zero), with a third "Out-of-pocket cost" bar making the offset explicit.

- **T15 -- Recharts `LabelList` does not reliably render at `position="right"` for zero-width bars.** A zero-value Bar in vertical layout produces a 0px-wide rect; the default LabelList places its label at the rect's right edge, which is x=0 (left edge of the plot area), where it gets clipped by the YAxis ticks. Replaced the default with a custom `content` function that renders a `<text>` node at `x + Math.max(width, 2) + 6` so even zero-width bars get their labels rendered at a visible offset. **Rule: any time a NumericBar legitimately needs to display value=0 with semantic-bearing labels ("No study cost", "Covered by SAAS"), use a custom LabelList content renderer rather than relying on the default position handling.**

- **T15 -- Recharts LabelList custom `content` types are loose; an `any` escape is the lowest-friction fix.** TypeScript flagged the strict prop signature against Recharts' wider `Props` type which allows `value: RenderableText | null`. Tried tightening the local type signature; failed because RenderableText includes recursive React element shapes. Fell back to `(props: any)` with a single eslint-disable comment. **Rule: Recharts' label/tooltip custom-content props frequently fail strict typing; an explicit `any` with eslint-disable is preferable to writing a 30-line conditional union to mirror RenderableText.**

- **T17 -- Reused `AI_ROLE_TIER_META` palette for Robotics threat rather than introducing a parallel scale.** Same green/amber/orange/red gradient communicates "degree of automation pressure" regardless of whether the source is AI or robotics; only the metric label and tooltip text differ. The TieredBar component is bespoke (lightweight DIV-based) rather than reusing `NumericBar`'s Recharts implementation, because per-row colouring inside a single Recharts Bar series requires per-Cell injection that doesn't compose cleanly with NumericBar's existing prop shape. **Rule: when the existing tier semantics already match a new metric, share the palette; render the bar geometry inline if Recharts cell-styling adds more friction than a 70-line div renderer.**

- **T17 -- The 4 rating columns live on `career_roles`, not `role_profiles`.** Easy mistake: the prior session's pattern was "everything compare-related lives on role_profiles", which would have led to a misnamed FK error. Confirmed via `information_schema.columns` query against `career_roles` first. ComparisonGrid's SELECT was extended at the top level (alongside `id, title`) rather than nested inside the role_profiles embed. **Rule: AI/robotics ratings are role-level not profile-level; the convention is `career_roles.{ai|robotics}_rating_{2030_2035|2040_2045}` plus `career_roles.is_new_ai_role`. Document this in CLAUDE.md if Phase 2 adds more rating dimensions.**

- **T17 -- "New AI role" badge is rendered as inline text in the Role label, not as a separate badge component.** LabelRow's value prop is a string (single-cell), so dropping a JSX badge mid-cell would have required widening LabelRow's contract. Spec called for a "small badge next to the career name" -- shipping it as a unicode bullet + suffix text (`"<title>  • New AI role"`) preserves the LabelRow contract without a wider refactor. **Rule: when a Headline-summary value needs decoration, use inline text suffixes before widening primitive component contracts; promote to JSX-aware values only when at least three call sites need it.**

- **T18 -- The dashboard already had `SavedComparisonsCard` shipped in Session 6.** Audit found the component already lists most-recent-5 with a "View all" link to /account/saved-comparisons; no work needed. Toast upgrade was the only deliverable for T18. **Rule: a task description that says "ensure X exists" should always start with a 30-second `Glob`/`Grep` audit before adding anything; this session avoided shipping a duplicate dashboard component.**

- **T18 -- Toast moved from inline `<p>` (positioned absolute relative to button) to fixed bottom-right.** Previous design used `position: absolute; right: 0; top: calc(100% + 4px)` so the status hugged the Save button. Spec change required a properly visible toast with a link and close button -- a button-relative position is too cramped for two lines of text + a link. Switched to `position: fixed; right: 20px; bottom: 20px; z-index: 90`. **Rule: if a status message needs to convey >5 words and a CTA, lift it out of the trigger element's flow into a fixed-position toast container; trigger-anchored statuses are only safe for one-line confirmations.**

- **Build + tests + lint clean.** `npx tsc --noEmit`: 0 errors. `npm test`: 34 / 34 pass (15 url-state + 6 lifetime-earnings + 5 studyYearsForQualification + 8 calculateROI). `npm run build`: full route table compiled without errors. `npm run lint`: 0 errors, 88 pre-existing warnings (same count as Session 9, no new warnings from this session). Commits: 28b5b35 (T15), 3ed1918 (T16), 5a93230 (T17), 58375cb (T18), fdd729a (T14), 7803279 (T13 docs).

- **Browser QA still not performed (fourth session running).** Per Session 7's outstanding follow-up, Playwright install remains uninstalled. The Future Outlook tier bars (custom div-based renderer), the toast positioning, the postcode teaser skip link, and the new ROI Out-of-pocket row have not been eyeballed. **Phase-2 follow-up: install Playwright, add an e2e spec for `/careers/compare?t=<seed>` covering ROI section + Future Outlook horizon toggle + Save toast appearance.**

- **Phase-2 follow-ups logged this session:** (a) Playwright harness (carried over again); (b) wire actual Resend SMTP cutover in Supabase Dashboard once DNS is verified; (c) consider promoting `RATE_LIMIT_MESSAGE` strings into a localisable constants file when i18n lands; (d) the `LabelRow` value contract is `string | null` -- if a third decoration use case appears beyond the Role inline badge, widen to `string | ReactNode | null`; (e) the saved-comparisons toast does not preserve queue state across navigation, so a navigate-then-return loses the toast -- acceptable for now but worth a session-state preservation pass if the save flow becomes more central.

## 2026-04-25 Post-launch fixes Session 9 -- non-student info pages, sign-up simplification, compare fixes, ROI

- **Files changed:** T7 new `supabase/migrations/20260425000001_create_pilot_interest.sql` + MCP-applied migration creating `pilot_interest` (insert-only RLS for anon/authenticated); new `app/actions/pilot-interest.ts`; new `components/pilot-interest-form.tsx`; three new info pages at `app/for-parents/page.tsx`, `app/for-teachers/page.tsx`, `app/for-advisers/page.tsx` (all static SSG); `components/PostcodeTeaser.tsx` (year-group select now includes a disabled ────── separator and three audience options that call `router.push` directly, bypassing the postcode lookup); `types/database.ts` (hand-added `pilot_interest` table entry alphabetically before `partners`). T8 `app/auth/sign-up/page.tsx` (removed `AccountType` type, `accountType`/`initialType` state, `type=parent` URL param reader, the `AccountTypeCard` radiogroup, and the conditional copy; single-student copy only; comment notes the retained `students.user_type` column is reserved for future role expansion; -79 lines). T10 `components/compare/ComparisonGrid.tsx` (hours display switched from "37 h" to "37 hours/week typical"; entry-qual label rows now carry explicit "Minimum:" / "Typical:" prefix in the per-career value); `components/compare/NumericBar.tsx` (reference-line `strokeDasharray` changed from "3 3" to "4 4"); `components/compare/EarningsSection.tsx` (median label now uses `formatGbpFull` for both gross and net mode so the full £37,430 is visible, not the `£37k` short form). T11 new `lib/earnings/roi-calculator.ts` exporting `calculateROI` and `DEFAULT_STUDY_CONTEXT`; new `components/compare/RoiSection.tsx`; `components/compare/ComparisonGrid.tsx` adds the "Return on investment" section between Earnings and Daily work.

- **T9 audit surfaced that three of the four checks were already satisfied in code.** Hours per week was rendering with a numeric label ("37 h") rather than missing; entry-qualification rows were already in the Headline summary as two `LabelRow` rows; the reference line was present on both Starting and Experienced bars with `strokeDasharray="3 3"`. Only the phrasing and dasharray details differed from the spec. **Rule: an audit task is worth running in full even when the user's description implies a fix is needed -- it often reveals the feature is present but labelled differently, which converts a build task into a rename task.**

- **AI/Robotics "toggle" does not exist -- the ai-careers page renders parallel AI and Robotics panels with a shared horizon (near/long) toggle.** The user's Task 9d asked to verify the "AI/Robotics toggle", implying a two-way switch. In fact Session 8 shipped the design as side-by-side panels (one per metric) so users compare both horizons against both metrics without tab-switching. Left unchanged; documented the design-vs-expectation mismatch here in case a future session adds an explicit metric toggle on top of the existing horizon one. **Rule: when a spec references a UI control, grep the relevant file for the control name before assuming it exists; "toggle" in the spec may mean "the horizon toggle that applies to both metrics", not "a new AI-vs-Robotics selector".**

- **Dropdown-with-routing needs a separator-looking disabled option to signal the audience split.** The landing postcode teaser's year-group `<select>` now has `<option value="" disabled>──────────</option>` between S6 and the three audience options. Without the separator the three audience rows read as additional year-group choices, which confuses the user's mental model. `handleYearGroupChange` detects one of the three audience keys and calls `router.push`, otherwise sets yearGroup state; the disabled separator's empty value keeps the placeholder state correctly if clicked. **Rule: when mixing modal-navigation options into a `<select>` alongside form-input options, insert a disabled separator option and branch the change handler on the distinguished keys rather than leaking non-form values into the state setter.**

- **The `pilot_interest` table is a single-table collection point for three audiences, not three tables.** `role` column with `CHECK (role IN ('teacher','adviser','parent'))` keeps enrolment simple for the admin later (SELECT WHERE role='teacher'). Insert-only RLS (`anon, authenticated`); no SELECT policy at all so the form can be public but the data cannot be read back. If a future session adds an admin review UI, add a `SELECT TO authenticated USING (...)` policy keyed on ADMIN_EMAILS via a function, not a direct users join (kept simple for Session 9). **Rule: for a single-purpose outreach form with a small discriminator set, one table + `CHECK` constraint + single INSERT policy is less overhead than three parallel tables. Revisit if the forms diverge (different required fields) rather than splitting by role prematurely.**

- **Dropping the parent/carer toggle from sign-up requires leaving `students.user_type` alone.** Existing parent rows still have `user_type='parent'` in production (from the short period parent sign-up was live), and `components/layout/navbar.tsx` + `components/ui/parent-notice.tsx` + `app/(main)/dashboard/page.tsx` all still branch on it. Dropping the column would break those reads for anyone with a parent account that's still live. The comment in the sign-up page now declares the column reserved; future sessions adding role features (school adviser accounts, teacher accounts) can extend the enum without a data migration. **Rule: when an account-type discriminator column has real data and real downstream reads, leave it in the schema even if the sign-up UI no longer writes non-default values; remove the write path before touching the column.**

- **`lib/earnings/roi-calculator.ts` imports constants from `app/tools/roi-calculator/constants.ts` rather than duplicating them.** The existing calculator page already has `calculateAnnualBreakdown`, `CITIES`, and SAAS bracket lookups. The new shared module imports those and layers per-role study duration + breakeven calc on top. This inverts the typical "lib defines, app consumes" direction, but moving the constants to lib would have touched every line in the standalone calculator page. Instead the lib module is thin and the app-owned constants file continues to be the source of truth for city rents, SAAS bands, and annual-breakdown arithmetic.
